- **Finance Ops Phase 4-1/4-4/4-5/4-15 + Phase 4-0 — Codex P2 #1 + P2 #2 fixes** (Codex consolidated review of `d0b2d53f` / `4af8647d` / `b5bdda85` / `3066e8d8` / `d03a1e66` / `3a036d10`, Slack TS `1779891522.980869`): Applied the 2 P2 findings without weakening any guardrail. **P2 #1 (packet identity / numbering drift)** — Codex flagged that the Phase 4-0 design freeze's authoritative §10 inventory still defined `4-4 = tenant candidate`, `4-5 = owner matrix`, `4-15 = observability runbook`, `4-16 = rollback runbook`, but Slack TS `1779847626.625429` directed the new design freezes to use `4-4 = observability design`, `4-5 = rollback design`, `4-15 = support+escalation design`. The conflict left the original tenant-candidate and owner-matrix slots unfilled and made downstream references (Phase 4-5 lines 61 + 90 referring to "Phase 4-0 §10.2's 4-5 documentation slot" as the owner-matrix packet; Phase 4-4 line 139 referring to "Phase 4-15 implementation packet for the support / escalation runbook" colliding with old 4-15 observability) ambiguous or wrong. **Fix:** renumbered Phase 4-0 §10.1 inventory + §10.2 per-packet dependency map + §10.3 cross-packet rules + §10.4 cadence + §11.2 activation-gate table + §11.3 + §13 acceptance + §14 next-active-item to a new 22-packet inventory that absorbs the three new design freezes. The activation gate moved from Phase 4-19 → Phase 4-20; activation execution moved from Phase 4-20 → Phase 4-21. Old 4-15 (observability operational runbook) and old 4-16 (rollback operational runbook) are dropped from the numbered planning-slot sequence — they remain as downstream implementation packets of the Phase 4-4 design freeze and Phase 4-5 design freeze respectively, with no dedicated planning slot. Old 4-4 (tenant candidate) → new 4-6; old 4-5 (owner matrix) → new 4-7; old 4-6 through 4-12 shifted by +2 to new 4-8 through 4-14; old 4-13 / 4-14 (adapter worker / ERPNext proof) shifted by +3 to new 4-16 / 4-17; old 4-17 / 4-18 (regression / evidence pack) shifted by +1 to new 4-18 / 4-19. Phase 4-0's §7 slice table updated where each "Phase 4 packet that delivers it" column changed (slice #5 = Phase 4-4, slice #6 = Phase 4-5). §9 owner matrix updated to reference Phase 4-4 observability and Phase 4-5 rollback rather than the old 4-15 / 4-16 slots. §6 supported-provider-path table updated (Phase 4-14 → Phase 4-17). New packet files updated: Phase 4-1 references to "Phase 4-19" → "Phase 4-20"; Phase 4-2 references to "Phase 4-14" → "Phase 4-17" + "Phase 4-19" → "Phase 4-20"; Phase 4-3 references to "Phase 4-19" → "Phase 4-20", "Phase 4-6" → "Phase 4-8", and the old "Phase 4-16 (rollback/operations)" wording replaced with "operational rollback runbook downstream of Phase 4-5 design"; Phase 4-4 references to "Phase 4-19" → "Phase 4-20" and "Phase 4-14 controlled-flip window" → "Phase 4-17 controlled-flip window"; Phase 4-5 references to "Phase 4-20" → "Phase 4-21" (old execution), "Phase 4-19" → "Phase 4-20" (gate), "Phase 4-14" → "Phase 4-17" (ERPNext proof mirror), "Phase 4-6" → "Phase 4-8" (migration runbook), and the specific lines 61 + 90 owner-matrix-slot references updated from "Phase 4-0 §10.2's 4-5 documentation slot" to "Phase 4-7 (the production owner matrix packet — Phase 4-0 §10.2's 4-7 documentation slot under the post-`3a036d10` P2 #1 renumbering)"; the Phase 4-5 lines 213 / 222 / 261 references to "Phase 4-16 (the production rollback runbook — Phase 4-0 §10.2's 4-16 slot)" replaced with "the operational rollback runbook (downstream of this Phase 4-5 design freeze; no dedicated planning slot per the post-`3a036d10` P2 #1 renumbering)"; Phase 4-15 references to "Phase 4-19" → "Phase 4-20" and "Phase 4-14" → "Phase 4-17" and the specific line referencing "Phase 4-5 (owner matrix population)" replaced with "Phase 4-7 (owner matrix population, per Phase 4-0 §10.2's 4-7 documentation slot under the post-`3a036d10` P2 #1 renumbering)". **Verdicts addressed:** P2 #1 closed across Phase 4-0 + the 6 new packets — the design-freeze baseline and the new packets now use one consistent numbering scheme; downstream implementation sequencing references are unambiguous. **P2 #2 (`/journal-entries` contract drops existing route-visible states)** — Codex flagged that Phase 4-1 §4 mapped persistent-mode `GET /journal-entries` to a direct `audit_events` query filtered to `journal.posted` and `journal.reversed` events, but the current route's `service.listJournalEntries()` at `backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js:134-137` returns the full `bucket.journalEntries` array — which includes `draft` and `pending_approval` entries (line 199, 367, 457, 507). The proposed design would silently drop those statuses from the GET response under persistent mode — a user-visible behavioral regression. **Fix:** Phase 4-1 §4 row for `/journal-entries` replaced — the persistent-mode read source is now a **new `journal_entries` projection** that consumes the full journal-entry lifecycle event vocabulary (`finance.journal.draft_created`, `finance.journal.validation_failed`, `finance.approval.requested`, `finance.approval.approved`, `finance.journal.reversal_requested`, plus any future `finance.journal.posted` / `finance.journal.reversed` emit-sites) and maintains a per-(tenant, journal_entry_id) snapshot keyed by status (`draft` / `pending_approval` / `posted` / `reversed`). The route response shape matches the current in-memory `service.listJournalEntries(tenantId)` shape bit-for-bit, preserving the full status set. Phase 4-1 design also notes that `backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js:681-684` records that journal posting is NOT a Slice 2 deliverable (journal stays at `pending_approval` until a separate posting slice lands), so the implementation packet either adds the missing `finance.journal.posted` emit-site OR documents that the projection captures `pending_approval` as the terminal pre-posting state until that slice lands. §9 test row 8 replaced (was "no journal-entries projection introduced" → now "`journal_entries` projection introduced with full state coverage" + bit-parity sub-assertion verifying persistent-mode response shape matches in-memory branch's response for the same event sequence; new test file `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/journalEntriesProjection.test.js`). §9 test row 4 ("projection-backed reads end-to-end") expanded to seed the full journal lifecycle and verify draft + pending-approval entries appear in the response. §10 staging proof item F updated to verify the round-trip lands via the `journal_entries` projection snapshot. §12 acceptance entry updated. **What did NOT change:** §3 planning-vs-activation distinction unchanged; §5 candidate tenant criteria unchanged; §6 supported provider path unchanged (ERPNext sandbox/local first; non-ERPNext out of scope); §8 10-row operator-side evidence contract unchanged; §12 hard constraints unchanged. Both fail-closed postures preserved end-to-end. No runtime code, no env-var changes, no migration application, no provider writes, no Coolify mutation, no production action by this fix. Doc-only.

- **Finance Ops Phase 4-15 — Production Support and Escalation Design Freeze (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-15-production-support-escalation-design.md` (NEW))**: Parallel-track design freeze for the Phase 4-0 §9 support owner role + security incident escalation paths, enabling Phase 4-0 §11.2 row 15 activation-gate verification (customer-side primary contact reachable + support owner availability confirmed). **No code, no env-var changes, no migration application, no customer communication occurred (pilot not activated), no security incident escalation drilled.** §3 support owner role contract — customer-facing first point of escalation; 1-hour response window during business hours; triage authority (route to monitoring / rollback / security reviewer / AiSHA customer-success); cannot unilaterally trigger rollback (rollback owner authority per Phase 4-5 §3) or flip levers; records every interaction in single evidence file; engagement window from Phase 4-19 GO through stand-down + 7 days. §4 operator-visible symptom triage map — Phase 4-4 §3 17 internal signals each mapped to triage action; customer-side report categories ("Finance Ops shows error" → confirm against signal 1/2/3; "I'm seeing data that isn't mine" → security tier immediate; "I want to opt out of the pilot" → Phase 4-5 §5 row 8); operator-side periodic spot checks. §5 customer communication posture — support owner is single customer-facing voice during pilot; severity-scaled notification windows (15 min CRITICAL / 30 min WARNING for customer-impact, security may be delayed pending containment); framing rules (state what happened + what we did + what we're doing now; no internal naming of engineers/workers; no speculation/blame); 30-min update cadence during incident; multi-channel for CRITICAL; 14 template categories with triggers/audiences (downstream operational packet drafts the actual wording). §6 security incident escalation playbooks for the four mandated categories: §6.1 tenant leakage (page security reviewer + contain via §4 row 1/row 2 + identify scope via audit_events queries + delayed customer disclosure pending containment + 7-day RCA + may result in pilot termination); §6.2 credential leak (rotate credential + identify leak source + may rotate encryption key per Phase 4-3 §7 + Phase 4-3 §10 row 11 test failure is post-incident fix); §6.3 provider-write anomaly (flip kill switch + inventory writes from audit_events + provider-side reversal via provider's own non-destructive contracts); §6.4 audit-log integrity (full rollback Phase 4-5 §4 rows 1/4/7/8 + out-of-band PITR snapshot for forensics before any restore + may result in pilot termination + may require third-party security review). §7 evidence ownership matrix — pilot incident log (support owner) + customer communication log (support owner) + security incident record (security reviewer) + rollback evidence record (rollback owner per Phase 4-5 §6) + Phase 4-4 signal snapshots (monitoring owner) + post-incident RCAs (deploy + security reviewer) + pilot stand-down summary (support + deploy owner). Phase 4-19 packet template includes "evidence consumed" section listing files + owners + timestamps. §8 hard constraints + Codex Gate F (concrete + role-bound + Phase-4-19-traced; not generic support text; no credential values or internal engineer naming in customer comms; re-activation requires fresh Phase 4-19 GO). §9 acceptance. Anchored on HEAD `d03a1e66`.

- **Finance Ops Phase 4-5 — Production Rollback Design Freeze (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-5-production-rollback-design.md` (NEW))**: Parallel-track design freeze for Phase 4-0 §7 slice #6, enabling Phase 4-0 §11.2 row 6 activation-gate verification. **No code, no rollback executed, no rehearsal executed, no env-var changes, no production action.** §3 rollback owner separation contract — distinct individuals from deploy owner with independent reachability (separate Doppler/Coolify/SSH access paths); pre-authorised by Phase 4-19 GO; trigger autonomy (rollback decision does not require concurrence; concurrence captured during evidence capture but not blocking); 5-min communication obligation; security reviewer override; stand-down handoff to monitoring owner / security reviewer. §4 rollback lever inventory + per-lever rollback step — 10 levers covering every production-side flip: ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS process-level gate, per-tenant modulesettings.financeOps flag, controlled-tenant allow-list, ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS route flag, FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED kill switch, ERPNext credentials (is_active toggle, NOT row delete), finance projection worker, finance adapter worker, production migrations (PITR + column-drop, never table-drop), UI Slice 1 (no frontend rollback action needed). Each lever's forward action + rollback step + reversibility documented. Priority order during rollback: stop bleeding (route flag / provider writes / workers) → contain → pause data flow (tenant gate / allow-list) → revoke credentials → process-level shutdown → migration revert (reserved for migration-level corruption). §5 11 abort criteria — sustained 5xx, projection degraded, replay failure, sustained adapter sync failure, unauthorised provider write (security reviewer authority), RLS / tenant mismatch (security reviewer authority), credential lookup failure, customer-side complaint, deploy owner unavailable, safety guardrail violation (security reviewer authority), migration apply failure. §6 evidence capture — 14-field per-rollback record: decision timestamp + actor + criterion + signal evidence + levers flipped with per-lever timestamp + start/end + concurrences + customer comms + provider-side effects + post-rollback signals + stand-down + RCA. Pre-authorised by Phase 4-19 GO; re-activation requires fresh Phase 4-19 GO consuming the rollback evidence. §7 6-phase communication protocol — concurrent with rollback execution; t0 decision posted; lever flips confirmed one-line; customer-side at t+15 min; stand-down at t+30 min earliest; post-rollback summary at t+1h; 7-day RCA. §8 non-destructive guarantee — explicit list of forbidden operations: DELETE FROM audit_events / projection_state / tenant_integrations, TRUNCATE on any finance table, DROP TABLE on migration-introduced tables; rollback does NOT call provider DELETE endpoints (uses provider's own non-destructive reversal contracts). §9 rehearsal contract — staging environment, both deploy + rollback owners participate, each lever flip produces expected Phase 4-4 §3 signal change (DEFERRED signals recorded as expected-but-not-yet-observable), evidence record committed to operational runbook before Phase 4-19 may verify row 6. §10 hard constraints + Codex Gate E (config-gated + non-destructive). - **Finance Ops Phase 4-3 — Credential Encryption Migration Design Freeze (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-3-credential-encryption-design.md` (NEW))**: Parallel-track design freeze for Phase 4-0 §7 slice #4, enabling Phase 4-0 §11.2 row 4 activation-gate verification. **No code, no migration applied anywhere, no env-var changes, no production action.** Replaces decision E4's plain-JSONB POC posture for `tenant_integrations.api_credentials` with at-rest encryption before any production credential lands. §3 forward-only migration shape — adds `api_credentials_encrypted BYTEA` + `api_credentials_key_version SMALLINT` + `api_credentials_encrypted_at TIMESTAMPTZ`; does NOT drop plaintext column (separate forward-only migration after every active row encrypted); does NOT encrypt existing staging plaintext rows automatically; no destructive operation. §4 encryption contract — AES-256-GCM (or equivalent AEAD; non-AEAD modes forbidden); envelope format `version || nonce || ciphertext+tag`; JSON-serialised credentials are the plaintext; only `api_credentials` is encrypted (tenant_id, integration_type, is_active, base_url stay plaintext so sandbox-only guard can apply without decryption); random nonce per encryption; deterministic encryption forbidden; no client-side encryption. §5 key management — Doppler-supplied OR external KMS (Phase 4-3 design accommodates both; implementation packet picks one); key in process memory only after boot; never on disk after boot, never logged, never in HTTP response; only credential router has access via encrypt()/decrypt() exports (key itself not exported); per-version numbering; boot-time test vector decryption required (backend refuses to start on key misconfig — same fail-loud posture as Phase 4-1 §5); one key per environment, not per tenant. §6 decrypt-at-read code path inside Phase 4-2 router boundary; legacy plaintext fallback only for transitional staging rows with mandatory warning log (production rows MUST be encrypted, enforced by Phase 4-6 production migration runbook). §7 rotation — operator-driven per-row re-encryption (not automatic on every write); old version retired only after all active rows on new version; mixed-version reads supported during window; decrypt failure under all versions logged + observable per Phase 4-4 signal 14 + treated as malformed per Phase 4-2 §8. §8 rollback — forward-only migration with column-drop rollback under PITR-snapshot protection; per-row rollback to plaintext is fully recoverable; **no rollback procedure depends on destructive data deletion** (mirrors Codex Gate E across Phase 4-3 and Phase 4-5). §9 audit logging — `finance.credential.lookup.ok` / `.fail` / `.rotate` event types with `tenant_id` + `integration_type` + `key_version` + `failure_reason`; never credential or key values; sampling for success, always-log for failures; deferred decision on whether to emit success events to `audit_events` vs separate audit log table. §10 14-row required test surface including row 11 "no credential / key value in any log / error / exception". §11 hard constraints + Codex Gate C (no plaintext store-side fallback as long-term posture; no log leak). Anchored on HEAD `4af8647d`. Pairs with Phase 4-2.

- **Finance Ops Phase 4-2 — Per-Tenant ERPNext Credential Router Design Freeze (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-2-erpnext-credential-router-design.md` (NEW))**: Parallel-track design freeze for Phase 4-0 §7 slice #3, enabling Phase 4-0 §11.2 row 3 activation-gate verification. **No code, no migration applied, no tenant_integrations row inserted, no env-var changes, no provider writes, no Coolify mutation, no production action.** Replaces the current process-env credential read path at `backend/workers/financeAdapterWorker.js:471-516` (one set of credentials per worker process, shared across all tenants — acceptable for Phase 3 single-tenant staging, unacceptable for production scaling) with per-tenant lookup via the existing `tenant_integrations` table from migration 004. §3 design notes on existing table — `tenant_id TEXT` stays (router accepts UUID input and maps to existing column); `integration_type` reserved namespace `'finance.erpnext.sandbox'`; `is_active` honored; `api_credentials JSONB` is the plaintext POC posture Phase 4-3 replaces; `config.base_url` separated from credentials so sandbox-only URL guard applies without decryption; RLS preserved as defence-in-depth; no new column required by Phase 4-2. §4 router interface contract — single-tenant async lookup returning credentials-or-null; no batch API; no fallback; implementation packet may add per-tenant TTL cache. §5 tenant isolation contract — 5 hard rules: SQL `WHERE tenant_id = ... AND integration_type = ... AND is_active = true` is the primary boundary; at most one active row per (tenant, type); no process-env fallback (the whole point of the router is to retire that path); controlled-tenant allow-list checked before router invocation; credentials never logged or surfaced. §6 sandbox-only routing — router does NOT maintain its own URL allow-list; existing `erpnextSandboxAdapter.js:89-128` guard remains authoritative; production-ERPNext URLs out of scope until Phase 4-14 sub-decision. §7 adapter worker integration — new per-tenant flow replacing `financeAdapterWorker.js:471-516`: no global adapter at boot; per-job credential lookup; cache by (tenant_id, credential-row-id) for worker lifetime; existing `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false` kill switch at `adapterJobProcessor.js:332-345` untouched. §8 fallback/stop behaviour — 7-row state machine (missing → null → skip; inactive → null → skip; malformed → throw → skip with no secret in error; sandbox-guard fail → AdapterConfigError → skip; duplicate rows → throw → skip; pg blip → propagate scrubbed; valid + writes-disabled → existing kill-switch path). No silent fallback ever. §9 audit/logging posture — `tenant_id` and `integration_type` logged; failure type categorised; credential values never appear; Phase 4-3 decides audit_events emission. §10 14-row required test surface including row 8 "credentials never appear in logs/errors" + row 6 "no process-env fallback" + row 13 "no global adapter registered at boot". §11 hard constraints + Codex Gate B (no global/shared masquerade). Anchored on HEAD `d0b2d53f`. Pairs with Phase 4-3 per Phase 4-0 §7 implementation cadence rule.

- **Finance Ops Phase 4-1 — Persistent-Events Route Lift + Projection-Backed Reads Design Freeze (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-1-persistent-events-projection-reads-design.md` (NEW))**: Primary Phase 4 architecture packet. Design freeze operationalising Phase 4-0 §7 slices #1 (route lift) + #2 (projection-backed reads), enabling Phase 4-0 §11.2 rows 1 + 2 activation-gate verifications. **No code, no env-var changes, no migration application, no provider writes, no Coolify mutation, no production action by this task.** Current fail-closed guard at `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:48` remains untouched in committed code; this packet does not remove, weaken, or propose flipping `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` anywhere. §1 frames scope (lift the dangerous flag safely by replacing split-brain in-memory reads with projection-backed reads from the same Postgres event store the route would write to; §7 slices #1 + #2 paired in this design but verified separately at the §11.2 gate). §2 live-execution posture all "None". §3 current architecture summary — what split-brain looks like today: route writes to in-memory bucket, projection workers read Postgres, the two never meet; flipping the flag in this state is structural corruption the `finance.v2.js:48` guard prevents. §4 read-source mapping per route — all 5 existing GETs mapped: `/runtime/status` becomes composite (audit_events count + projection_state cursor + `runtime.persistence='persistent'` + `runtime.mode='persistent'` replacing the `mock_read_only` placeholder honesty gap from UI Slice 1 §8.2.9); `/journal-entries` becomes direct `audit_events` query filtered by event type (no new journal_entries projection introduced — event store is the canonical journal); `/ledger` consumes `ledgerProjection`; `/profit-loss` + `/balance-sheet` derived from `ledgerProjection` snapshot reusing existing domain service derivation logic. §5 route construction and env-gating sequence: single env read at construction time; no runtime adapter swap; loud-on-misconfig (route throws at construction if persistent-events true + no pgPool); persistence mode is deploy-time, not runtime. §6 no-silent-fallback contract — four-row required-vs-forbidden behaviour table covering pgPool query failure, projection lag, adapter construction failure, mid-flight env clearance. §7 migration / replay / cursor dependency on `audit_events` + `projection_state` healthy + projection worker advancing + replay determinism PASS, each chained to a specific Phase 3 §13 evidence pack row. §8 boot-time wiring via a `FinanceReadAdapter` abstraction (`InMemoryFinanceReadAdapter` for default posture, `ProjectionBackedFinanceReadAdapter` for persistent-events), selected once at construction. §9 11-row required test surface before guard can be lifted (adapter selection, loud boot failure, in-memory branch unchanged regression-protection, projection-backed end-to-end, no silent fallback on transient failure, lag observability, persistence-mode-is-deploy-time, no journal-entries projection introduced, replay determinism, no new mutating endpoint, `financePersistencePolicy.test.js` adapted). §10 9-item required staging proof contract (route lift lands → migrations applied → projection worker healthy → flag flipped in staging → real audit_events row from real route call → GET returns same data via direct query → ledger GET reflects new event → replay drill PASS → negative-proof flag clear). §11 hard constraints status-confirmed. §12 12-item acceptance. §13 next active item = Phase 4-1 implementation packet (separately dispatched after Codex clears this design). Anchored on HEAD `cfcbb135` (Phase 4-0 Codex-cleared). **Codex review gate A enforced**: design prevents split-brain reads + preserves fail-closed guard until tests + staging proof land.

- **Finance Ops Phase 4-0 — Codex P2 + P3 fixes** (Codex review of `673df707`, Slack TS `1779845604.078829`): Applied the 2 findings without weakening any guardrail. **P2 (§11.2 row 1 conflated §7 slice #1 + slice #2 in the activation gate)** — §7 enumerates slice #1 (persistent-events route lift) and slice #2 (projection-backed reads) as separate required pre-activation deliverables (`phase-4-production-pilot-design-freeze.md:162-163`), but §11.2 row 1 listed them as `§7 slice #1 (route lift + projection-backed reads)` (`:340`). That weakened the contract: a Phase 4-19 gate verifier could mark row 1 satisfied if slice #1 cleared, even though slice #2 was unverified, because the two are paired in Phase 4-1 but not interchangeable. Fix: split row 1 into two rows — new row 1 verifies slice #1 (route lift) against §8 row 6 (Phase 3-7 route activation) + row 9 (Phase 3-10 ERPNext sandbox proof, where the route-to-projection path is exercised end-to-end); new row 2 verifies slice #2 (projection-backed reads) independently against §8 row 4 (Phase 3-5 projection worker activation) + row 5 (Phase 3-6 replay drill — byte-identical determinism) + row 7 (Phase 3-8 smoke matrix), with explicit text that slice #2 cannot be implicitly cleared by slice #1's pass. Renumbered rows 3-16; §11.2 verification table is now 16 rows; §13 acceptance entry updated from "15-item" to "16-item Phase 4-19 verification table with §7 slices #1 and #2 verified separately". **P3 (§10.2/§10.3 over-serialised the planning sequence relative to the stated parallel-safe goal)** — Band B in the prior §10.2 was blocked on all of 4-1 + 4-2 + 4-3 landing, and §10.3 said "no Band B packet may be authored before its Band A code dependency lands" (`:273-301`). That was broader than the per-packet dependencies the doc itself described: 4-7 (production RLS / service-role / PostgREST verification) does not need any of the 4-1/4-2/4-3 code slices to be authored because RLS + PostgREST exclusion live at the database / API-gateway layer, not in the finance runtime code being lifted; 4-8 (production Coolify deployment) is independent because Coolify-app provisioning mirrors Phase 3-4 against the production server irrespective of in-process code changes; 4-15 (production observability) is largely independent because the signal catalog adapts Phase 3-11 without needing the code slices implemented. As written, the banding turned a dependency map into a blanket serialization rule that contradicted the parallel-safe goal. Fix: replaced §10.2 "Parallel-safe execution bands" diagram with §10.2 "Per-packet dependency map" — an authoritative per-packet table listing each Phase 4 packet's `depends on` set (e.g., 4-7 depends only on 4-0; 4-9 depends on 4-0 + 4-1 design freeze, not implementation; 4-11 depends on 4-1 design freeze + implementation Codex-cleared; 4-13 depends on 4-2 + 4-3 design freezes; etc.); bands kept as an approximate scheduling summary explicitly marked informational with the per-packet map declared the source of truth on drift; §10.3 "Cross-band rules" replaced with §10.3 "Cross-packet rules" (per-packet `depends on` is authoritative; "design freeze" vs "implementation" dependency distinction explicit; runtime-state references require Codex-cleared implementation; Phase 4-19 consumes the full §11.2 16-row gate; Phase 4-20 is operator execution under 4-19 GO). §11.1 trigger #10 wording updated from "downstream Bands B + C re-baseline" to "downstream packets whose §10.2 `depends on` entry references the affected design freeze re-baseline". §14 next-active-item updated to enumerate the packets parallel-safe with 4-1 (Phase 4-2, 4-3, 4-4, 4-5, 4-7, 4-8, 4-15) rather than referencing "§10 Band A". §13 acceptance entry updated from "21 packets in 6 bands; cross-band rules" to "21 packets with an authoritative per-packet dependency map; bands kept only as an approximate scheduling summary; cross-packet rules". **Verdicts addressed:** P2 closed (slice #1 + slice #2 verified separately at the activation gate); P3 closed (per-packet dependency map is authoritative; bands are informational). **What did NOT change:** §3 planning-vs-activation distinction unchanged; §5 candidate tenant criteria unchanged; §6 supported provider path unchanged (ERPNext sandbox/local first; non-ERPNext out of scope); §7 6-slice contract unchanged (slice #1 + slice #2 already enumerated separately; the fix is to the gate that verifies them); §8 10-row operator-side evidence contract unchanged; §9 owner matrix unchanged; §12 hard constraints unchanged; both fail-closed postures preserved. No runtime code, no env-var changes, no migration application, no provider writes, no Coolify mutation, no production action by this fix. Doc-only.

- **Finance Ops UI Slice 1 — Codex P2 follow-up fix (canonical-wins resolution)** (Codex re-review of `a6996c69`, Slack TS `1779826966.071559`): The alias-module fix in `a6996c69` removed the canonical-only restriction but used a single `moduleSettings.find((m) => acceptableNames.includes(m.module_name))` over the raw Supabase rows. Supabase does not guarantee row order, so on a conflict (e.g. rows `[enterpriseFinance=false, financeOps=true]`) the find() could pick the alias row first and deny access, while the backend `isFinanceOpsEnabled()` at `backend/lib/finance/financeModuleGate.js:40-48` explicitly prefers the canonical `financeOps` row over the legacy `enterpriseFinance` alias when both exist (R-6 rule). Net: residual frontend/backend access drift in the conflicting-rows case. **Fix:** `src/utils/permissions.js` now resolves in two passes — find the canonical row first; only when no canonical row is present, fall back to any alias row. The earlier flat lookup is replaced by an explicit canonical-then-alias sequence, mirroring the backend's R-6 resolution. Comment block at the call site cites the backend file and the R-6 rule so future maintainers can verify alignment. Tests: 4 new regressions in `src/utils/__tests__/permissions.financeOps.test.js` covering the conflicting-rows case in _both_ array orders (canonical-first + alias-first × canonical=true + canonical=false). All 9 permissions tests PASS. No backend code change, no guardrail loosened. UI-1A, UI-1C remain finding-free; UI-1B P2 #1 (403 misclassification from `a6996c69`) still closed; this fix closes UI-1B P2 #2 follow-up.
- **Finance Ops UI Slice 1 — Codex P2 + P2 + P3 fixes for UI-1A/UI-1B/UI-1C** (Codex review of `e239ba89` / `0e5331e4` / `28ebc484`, Slack TS `1779825355.550989`): Applied the 3 findings without weakening any guardrail. **P2 (UI-1B / cross-packet): 403 misclassification** — `src/pages/FinanceOps.jsx` previously collapsed any HTTP 403 from `/runtime/status` into the "Tenant not enrolled" state, but `validateTenantAccess` (`backend/middleware/validateTenant.js:138-163`) also returns 403 for "User not assigned to any tenant" and "Access denied: ... permission to access this tenant's data" — neither of which is a module-enrolment problem. `isTenantNotEnrolledError()` now matches on the exact financeOps module-gate message (`'Finance Ops is not enabled for this tenant'` from `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:78-82`); other 403s flow to the generic-error path so the operator sees the right remediation. Added two regression tests in `FinanceOps.smoke.test.jsx` covering the two validateTenantAccess 403 messages, plus a comment block in `FinanceOps.jsx` enumerating all three known 403 messages so future code reviewers can verify the discrimination at the source. **P2 (UI-1B / cross-packet): frontend/backend alias-module access drift** — the backend gate at `financeModuleGate.js:7-16,29-48` accepts both `'financeOps'` (canonical) and `'enterpriseFinance'` (legacy alias), but the frontend `moduleMapping` originally only recognised the canonical key. A tenant enrolled via the alias would clear the backend route successfully but be hidden in the frontend nav — frontend/backend access drift in either direction (the page would show when backend denies an alias=false, or hide when backend allows an alias=true with no canonical row). Fixed in `src/utils/permissions.js` by adding a `moduleAliases` table inside `hasPageAccess` (`financeOps → [enterpriseFinance]`) and extending the lookup to accept any listed alias. Mirrored the alias declaration as a top-level `MODULE_ALIASES` export in `src/utils/navigationConfig.js` so future consumers do not re-introduce the drift. Added 5 regression tests in `src/utils/__tests__/permissions.financeOps.test.js` covering: enabled canonical row grants access, enabled alias row grants access, disabled alias row denies access (the regression the fix actually catches), disabled canonical row denies access, alias scope confined to financeOps. **P3 (UI-1A / cross-packet): runtime-mode honesty gap** — the design freeze §8.2.9 documents a 9th honesty gap (`runtime.mode` is a hard-coded `'mock_read_only'` placeholder at `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:110`, not an authoritative mode signal) but the shipped client's `FINANCE_API_GAPS` only contained 8 entries and `RuntimeOverview` rendered `runtime.mode` as if it were authoritative. Added the 9th entry `FINANCE_API_GAPS.runtimeMode` with the same shape (endpoint + designRef + naturalBackingSource + affectedScreen) and an annotation block in `RuntimeOverview.jsx` that surfaces a small note beneath the mode row whenever the value is the `mock_read_only` placeholder, citing the §8.2.9 design ref. Test updated to expect 9 gaps + a new test asserting the runtimeMode descriptor's contents and a RuntimeOverview test pair (annotation appears when mode is placeholder; hides when mode advances to e.g. `'persistent'`). **Verdicts addressed:** UI-1A P3 closed; UI-1B P2 #1 + P2 #2 closed; UI-1C remains finding-free; cross-packet drift resolved at the access layer. **What did NOT change:** no backend code, no env, no migration, no Coolify mutation, no provider write, no production action. `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` fail-closed at `finance.v2.js:48`, `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` default-closed at `adapterJobProcessor.js:332-345`, sandbox-only ERPNext URL guard at `erpnextSandboxAdapter.js:89-128` — all preserved. The 6 mutating Finance v2 endpoints remain absent from `src/api/finance.js`. No role gate introduced (P2 fix in `bc0bce52` preserved). All 94 finance-UI + permissions tests PASS.
- **Finance Ops UI Slice 1 — Codex P2 + P3 fixes**: Applied the 2 findings from Codex's `5db9d45b` review (Slack TS `1779801307.859339`). **P2** (substantive — backend-contract drift): §4.1 + §11.3 + §6.1 had restricted the Slice 1 access model to `admin` / `superadmin` only, but the actual Finance v2 backend route enforces no role check at all (just `validateTenantAccess` + the per-tenant `financeOps` module gate at `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:67-85`). The stricter frontend-only rule could have hidden a legitimate read-only console from enrolled tenant users who are not admins. Reconciled to match the real backend contract: Slice 1 access model is now "authenticated tenant + `financeOps` enabled" (same as the backend); §11.3 rewritten to separate the factual backend contract from a deferred role-as-product-policy decision, with the explicit rule that any future frontend role gate must land alongside a corresponding backend role check so the rule is enforced at both layers; §4.1 "Who" clause rewritten to drop the absolute role gate and explicitly note the backend authorization contract; §6.1 `systemPages` clause rewritten so the new posture is the active design rather than a footnote. **P3** (counting): §1 scope boundary said "The five mutating endpoints" but listed six — corrected to "The six mutating endpoints" matching the enumerated set (`POST /draft-invoices`, `PATCH /draft-invoices/:id`, `POST /journal-drafts`, `POST /simulate/deal-won`, `POST /journal-entries/:id/reverse`, `POST /approvals/:id/approve`). All other §8.3 / §13 enumerations of the mutating surface are already six and correct. No backend code change, no runtime change, no UI code shipped, no guardrail loosened — `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` fail-closed, `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` default-closed, sandbox-only ERPNext URL guard all unchanged.

Design freeze document only — **no UI code, no React component, no API client, no nav-config entry, no module-mapping change, no route binding, no test, no `.env` change, no migration, no Coolify mutation, no provider write, no production action by this task**. The document freezes the read-only Finance Operations Console design before any UI implementation begins so the parallel implementation packets (UI-1A…UI-1F) can proceed without re-deciding architecture mid-flight. §1 frames the scope (closes the operator/admin observability gap exposed by Phase 3 + Slice 2 closure: finance admins / operators currently have zero UI surface for inspecting runtime health, approval backlog, ledger / journal state, the adapter queue, or the audit timeline) and enumerates the scope boundary (no mutating controls of any kind, no frontend execution of any `POST /api/v2/finance/*`, no new backend endpoint, no `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` activation, no provider writes, no production action). §2 live-execution posture lists "None" for every modality including any frontend file created. §3 prerequisites: Phase 3 closed (`ce7d8cd8`), Slice 2 closed (`d1371632` and earlier), backend Finance v2 read surface stable. §4 three personas — finance admin (primary, customer-side CFO/controller/finance-ops-manager, daily/weekly observability), operator/support engineer (incident-driven plus periodic spot checks, bound to one tenant at a time via existing impersonation banner), implementation engineer (uses UI as live oracle during backend slice dev cycles). §5 13 jobs-to-be-done with explicit cite to the §8 backing read source for each: 4 satisfied by existing routes (runtime health, ledger, P&L, balance sheet, posted journal entries), 9 blocked on backend gaps (draft invoices list, journal drafts list, approval queue list, adapter queue list, audit timeline list, projection cursor view, registered-adapter list, evidence pack HTTP surface, runtime-mode authoritative value). §6 information architecture: single primary-nav entry ("Finance Operations", `href: FinanceOps`, gated by `financeOps` module enablement); page hosts 10 tabs + 1 placeholder; query-param tab state (matching the existing `Settings.jsx` pattern); no row-level deep linking in Slice 1; open question for UI-1A on reconciling `moduleMapping` display labels with the `financeOps` canonical key. §7 screen inventory for all 10 read-only screens + evidence placeholder: Runtime overview (default tab, reads `/runtime/status` end-to-end), Ledger summary, Draft invoices (gap), Journal drafts (gap), Journal entries (posted) reads `/journal-entries`, Approval queue (gap), Adapter queue (gap), Audit timeline (gap), Projection/degraded (reads `/runtime/status.runtime.persistence` + gap card), Sandbox adapter (reads `/runtime/status.runtime.provider_sync` + gap card), Evidence placeholder (stub for the existing `auditEvidenceBuilder.js` runtime that has no HTTP surface). §8 API contract mapping: §8.1 enumerates the 5 existing Finance v2 GET routes (`/runtime/status`, `/journal-entries`, `/ledger`, `/profit-loss`, `/balance-sheet`) Slice 1 consumes; §8.2 publishes a 9-entry honest gap inventory (no `GET /draft-invoices`, no `GET /journal-drafts`, no `GET /approvals`, no `GET /adapter-jobs`, no audit-events list, no per-projection cursor endpoint, no registered-adapter list, no evidence-pack HTTP surface, `runtime.mode` hard-coded string concern) with the natural backing source for each; §8.3 enumerates the 6 mutating endpoints Slice 1 explicitly does NOT consume (`POST /draft-invoices`, `PATCH /draft-invoices/:id`, `POST /journal-drafts`, `POST /simulate/deal-won`, `POST /journal-entries/:id/reverse`, `POST /approvals/:id/approve`). §9 data freshness model: manual refresh only (no polling, no SSE, no optimistic updates); per-screen empty states (gap-states distinguished from error-states; gap-state explicitly framed as "backend not yet exposed", not a degraded environment). §10 guardrail banners — four persistent banners stacked above tabs: persistent-events fail-closed banner (always rendered while `runtime.persistence === 'in_memory'`), provider-writes default-closed banner, sandbox-only adapter banner, production-activation-not-authorized banner (rendered unconditionally for all tenants in Slice 1 — deliberately conservative until backend exposes a `production_authorization` field). §11 authorization: process-level `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` (frontend renders 404 path), per-tenant `modulesettings.financeOps` (frontend renders 403 path + hides nav), `admin`/`superadmin` role required, existing `ImpersonationBanner` honored, wrong-tenant safety net via tenant-switch cache-bust. §12 error states: route disabled, tenant not enrolled, wrong tenant / impersonation mismatch, degraded projection runtime (gap), worker disabled (gap — frontend has no signal today), adapter unavailable (gap), provider writes disabled (banner not error), network/5xx with manual retry, 401 hands off to existing app-wide handler. §13 explicitly deferred mutating actions — 19-item exhaustive table listing every approve / reject / claim / reverse / post / create-invoice / edit-invoice / replay / retry / cancel / provider-sync-trigger / activate-persistent-events / enable-provider-writes / add-credentials / generate-evidence / run-replay-drill / enable-tenant-module / promote-to-production affordance with the backend path that would back it (or "no endpoint today") and the slice that would deliver it. §14 parallel implementation packet split: UI-1A (shell + nav wiring + base API client), UI-1B (Runtime overview + Ledger / P&L / Balance sheet + Journal entries), UI-1C (guardrail banners), UI-1D (gap-state screens), UI-1E (Projection/degraded + Sandbox adapter + Evidence placeholder), UI-1F (error states + gap inventory publication for backend consumption) — each packet's allowed-files set is disjoint so all five (1B–1F) are parallel-safe after UI-1A lands; cross-packet contracts frozen (single `<RuntimeStatusContext>`, shared `<GapStateCard>` and `<ErrorStates>` components, no direct `fetch` from screens, no mutating endpoint imports anywhere); per-packet Codex review checklist mirrors the backend Slice 2 cadence. §15 8 hard constraints re-stated for implementation packets. §16 9-item acceptance for the design freeze packet. §17 sign-off recording: persistent-events route guard preserved at `finance.v2.js:48`, default-closed `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` preserved, sandbox-only ERPNext URL guard preserved at `erpnextSandboxAdapter.js:89-128`, no production action; UI Slice 1 and backend Phase 4-0 are explicitly parallel and do not block each other. `backend/middleware/authenticate.js`), tenant isolation (`X-Tenant-Id` + JWT claim match at `backend/middleware/validateTenant.js` with the explicit "RLS does not protect finance from service-role backend" caveat from `service-role-tenant-claim-verification.md` §5.5), `financeOps` per-tenant module gate (canonical key + alias resolution at `financeModuleGate.js:12`, 403 with exact message at `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:78-82`), RLS posture (migration 175's 9 tables + 35 policies + 5 no-hard-delete triggers + 3 audit-events immutability triggers + 1 projection_state updated_at trigger), PostgREST exclusion (`finance` schema not in `db.schemas` per `postgrest-isolation-verification.md` §3.1 repo-side PASS), service_role-only backend access (`backend/lib/supabaseFactory.js:38-42` service-role-only client construction), two-layer provider-write gates (`FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` kill switch at `adapterJobProcessor.js:332-345` + `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE=draft_only` with `assertWritePermitted` named-export `AdapterCapabilityError` for finalising ops), sandbox-only ERPNext URL guard (`erpnextSandboxAdapter.js:89-128` structural constructor rejection with built-in patterns + operator-extended `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_SANDBOX_BASE_URLS` allowlist), persistent-events fail-closed route guard (`backend/routes/finance.v2.js:48` module-load-time throw with `financePersistencePolicy.test.js` 4/4 coverage), provider payload metadata stripping (`providerPayloadBuilder.js` 11-item denylist + leading-underscore + per-adapter allowlist + `assertNoInternalMetadata` test helper per E6), producer split (code separation between `adapterJobPromoter.js` `sync_queued` and `adapterJobProcessor.js` `sync_succeeded`/`sync_failed` + Slice 2D PRODUCER SPLIT test + envelope-only no-drift contract clarified per Codex P2), actor identity spoofing prevention (route-layer session-derived `actor.type` per `04a76bae` + `financeGovernanceDecision.test.js` 25/25), no-hard-delete enforcement (DB triggers + service guard + no DELETE routes per `security-rls-hardening.md` §3), append-only `audit_events` guard (migration 173 immutability triggers + `financeEventStore.pg.test.js` 20/20), controlled-tenant scope (`parseControlledTenantIds()` returns `[]` for empty/unset — no implicit "process all" fall-through, re-exported by both workers), sandbox-only credential storage (Doppler `stg_stg` only per decision E4, never `prd_prd`, no production credentials in repo), no QuickBooks/Xero/NetSuite (none of those adapters implemented; no OAuth flow configured anywhere), heartbeat-based liveness (no exposed `/health` HTTP port per Phase 3-4 §5.1 carried over with the deliberate-design trade-off documented). §6 pass/fail criteria at three levels (regression PASS at this task, security PASS at this task, combined PASS at the review-packet level — execution-level PASS deferred to Phase 3-13). §7 8 stop conditions (test failure persisting across reruns, Slice 2D lifecycle invariant fails, cite-rot, working tree no longer clean at `d1371632`, `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS=true` anywhere, `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=true` outside the Phase 3-10 §6.6 controlled window, any production endpoint/credential in any artifact, QB/Xero/NetSuite OAuth configuration). §8 8 hard constraints all status-confirmed. §9 13-item acceptance for the review packet. §10 evidence pack with §10.1 capturing the three executed-this-session checks (full regression 390/390, Slice 2D lifecycle 10/10, ### Fixed

- **Silent-drop prop bugs — stale UI, missing Kanban refresh, duplicate customer records (PR #622, branch `fix/opportunity-account-dropdown-intermittent`, commits `d981e351`/`0df3c23`/`84f84e7`/`80c30bc0`)**: Three independent bugs, all caused by React silently ignoring unknown prop names. (1) `src/hooks/useOpportunitiesData.js` — removed `supportingDataLoaded.current = true` from the catch block; it was permanently locking the accounts list at `[]` for the page lifetime after any API error, preventing retries. (2) `src/components/opportunities/OpportunityForm.jsx` — added a self-healing `useEffect` that calls `Account.filter()` when `propAccounts` arrives empty (fallback for the race between form-open and supporting data fetch); added `cancelled` flag + effect cleanup to prevent stale-tenant responses from writing into a re-keyed form (superadmin tenant-switch race); changed the sync effect to guard on `propAccounts.length > 0` so a parent error-path `[]` cannot wipe good fallback data. (3) `src/components/opportunities/OpportunityKanbanBoard.jsx` — `onSave={handleSave}` → `onSubmit={handleSave}` (OpportunityForm only destructures `onSubmit`; `onSave` was silently discarded so the board never re-fetched after dialog save); added missing `leads` prop. (4) `src/pages/Customers.jsx` — `account={editingAccount}` → `initialData={editingAccount}` (CustomerForm accepts `customer` or `initialData`, not `account`; the silent drop caused every edit to call `Account.create()` creating duplicate records); captured `wasEdit` before clearing state so the success toast correctly reads "updated" vs "created". Tests: 23 new pure-logic tests across `OpportunityForm.test.jsx` (+8), `OpportunityKanbanBoard.test.jsx` (new file, +6), `CustomerForm.test.jsx` (new file, +9); 3 render-based tests skipped (JSDOM+Radix hang, deferred to Playwright). `vitest.config.ts` — added `src/components/customers/**` globs to the `crm` project include list.

- **Finance Ops Phase 3-10 + Slice 2D CHANGELOG — envelope-only `object_*` no-drift assertion corrected (Codex Slack P2 verdict 2026-05-25 18:11 EDT, message TS `1779747082.592989`) (`docs/architecture/finance/erpnext-staging-sandbox-proof-results.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`)**: Codex's review of Slice 2E flagged that the 3-10 runbook (and one matching line in the Slice 2D CHANGELOG entry) overstated the Track A no-drift contract by asserting `object_type` / `object_id` must be absent from adapter-event **payload bodies** as well as envelopes. The actual contract is envelope-only: `adapterJobProcessor.js:155-156` (`sync_succeeded`) and `:185-186` (`sync_failed`) emit `object_type: job.aggregate_type` + `object_id: job.aggregate_id` inside the event payload by current Slice 2 design; `adapterJobPromoter.js:56-57` does the same for `sync_queued`. The Slice 2D `ENVELOPE` test (`adapterQueueProjection.integration.test.js:485-487`) asserts only `!('object_type' in evt)` + `!('object_id' in evt)` on the envelope object — it does NOT inspect the payload body. If the runbook were executed literally as originally written, a correct execution of the Slice 2 runtime would be marked as a Phase 3-10 failure on a pass/fail condition the shipped processor cannot satisfy. Fix: relaxed every overstated site to envelope-only per Codex's preferred resolution path (option 1 from the review — runbook matches the actual current contract; the runtime stays as-shipped). Sites patched in the 3-10 runbook: §1 lifecycle chain (line 178), §6.5 promoter envelope check (line 372), §6.7 envelope verification with the SQL example rewritten to inspect envelope columns instead of `payload ? 'object_type'` (line 530), §7 exit criterion (line 588), §10 stop condition (line 685), §11 hard constraint (line 712), §12 acceptance bullet (line 738). Each rewrite adds an explicit "payload-body `object_*` are expected per current Slice 2 design" carve-out with the code-line references (`adapterJobProcessor.js:155-156`/`:185-186`, `adapterJobPromoter.js:56-57`) so a future operator reading any single section sees the contract unambiguously. The matching Slice 2D CHANGELOG entry's description of integration test (6) is also corrected to match what the test actually asserts. Phase 3-9 runbook is unaffected (Codex's separate Phase 3-9 verdict was no findings). No code change, no migration, no env-var change, no Coolify mutation. `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged, `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged, production untouched.

- **Finance Ops Phase 3-10 — ERPNext Sandbox Adapter Proof Execution Runbook (Dry Run) (`docs/architecture/finance/erpnext-staging-sandbox-proof-results.md` (NEW))**: Second of two Slice 2E deliverables per [`slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md`](docs/architecture/finance/slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md) §5.5. Runbook only — **no ERPNext proof was executed by this task**, no `checkHealth()` / `listObjects()` / `pushDraft()` call against any ERPNext instance, no `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` flip in staging, no Coolify / Doppler mutation, no `tenant_integrations` row insertion, no migration applied, no backend route HTTP call, no provider HTTP write, production untouched. `adapterQueueProjection.integration.test.js` integration proof, with the in-memory event store + mocked HTTP client replaced with real staging Postgres `finance.audit_events` + real `httpClient.post()` against the sandbox endpoint. §1 frames the full lifecycle chain (backend route `simulateDealWon` → in-memory `adapter_job.status='draft'` → backend route `approveFinanceAction` → promoter `draft→queued` + `finance.adapter.sync_queued` emission → projection worker dispatches → `adapter_queue` 'queued' bucket → adapter worker `runAdapterPollCycle` claims → with `docstatus: 0` → `finance.adapter.sync_succeeded` emission → projection moves to 'completed' bucket) and identifies why 3-10 cannot collapse into 3-9: requires Phase 3-7 backend route activation, a separate later Slice's lift of the `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:48` fail-closed `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` guard (called out as the largest gap between Slice 2's deliverables and 3-10's executable proof, with explicit halt instructions if the lift is unmet), the `tenant_integrations` row from §6.2, and a reachable sandbox ERPNext with sandbox API credentials. §2 live-execution posture lists "None" for every modality including the sensitive ones (HTTP request to any ERPNext, `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=true` anywhere, `tenant_integrations` insertion, production action of any kind, payment movement). §3 13 prerequisites including the Slice 2A/B/C/D commit list (`27ae09fc`/`e66538f0`/`d671d816`/`1d2b41e6`/`95f65144`/`af8f71bc`), Phase 3-5 projection worker healthy (required as the consumer of the `sync_*` events), Phase 3-7 backend route activated, Phase 3-8 smoke tests PASS (specifically §5.6 + §5.7), Phase 3-9 adapter worker healthy with `adapter_count: 1`, and the persistent-events route lift prerequisite. §4 execution envelope splits what changes during 3-10 (the one `tenant_integrations` row, three route HTTP calls across iterations, the bounded `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=true` window in §6.6, one sandbox ERPNext HTTP call) from what stays unchanged (`FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE=draft_only`, the three-tier worker gate, the route mount, the persistent-events lift state, ERPNext sandbox URL/credentials, QuickBooks/Xero/NetSuite). §5 enumerates 8 proof-gate sub-assertions mapped to 2C-9 §5: sandbox connection only (§5.1), `AccountingAdapter` interface satisfaction (§5.2), draft-only at three levels — ERPNext `docstatus: 0` + `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE=draft_only` + `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` kill switch (§5.3), payload mapping correct and metadata-stripped (§5.4), adapter events emitted and replayable (§5.5), producer split holds end-to-end (`sync_queued` promoter-only, `sync_succeeded`/`sync_failed` processor-only) (§5.6), journal stays `pending_approval` (Phase 3-8 §5.7 contract) (§5.7), no live customer accounting write (§5.8). §6 9-step proof procedure: 6.1 preflight (read-only, includes a single `curl /api/method/ping` against the sandbox to verify API key validity); 6.2 insert `tenant_integrations` row for the controlled tenant with sandbox credentials (SQL UPSERT, plain JSONB per decision E4); 6.3 snapshot pre-proof state (`finance.adapter_jobs`, `finance.audit_events` count by event_type, `finance.projection_state`, `adapter_queue` projection `state_json`); 6.4 `POST /api/v2/finance/simulate/deal-won` with critical assertion that the response's `adapter_job.status` is `"draft"` not `"queued"` (draft-before-approval semantics), plus Postgres verification that zero `finance.adapter.*` rows exist; 6.5 `POST /api/v2/finance/approvals/:id/approve` with Postgres verification of exactly one new `finance.adapter.sync_queued` row with the correct envelope and `state_json` `queued` bucket entry; 6.6 the `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=true` controlled-flip window — explicitly the most sensitive step in the entire Phase 3 + Slice 2 arc — broken into 6 sub-steps (6.6.a pre-flip baseline + decision to bracket the kill-switch window around the entire route-call sequence so there's exactly one fresh queued job at the moment of the flip; 6.6.b authorization confirmation with explicit re-checks that `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_BASE_URL` is still the sandbox + revert command pre-typed in a terminal ready to fire; 6.6.c flip via Coolify; 6.6.d run §6.4 + §6.5 + wait one poll cycle + capture worker log `succeeded_count: 1` + ERPNext document JSON showing `docstatus: 0` and the mapped fields + the `sync_succeeded` row with `payload.provider_id: <ERPNext name>` and `payload.dry_run: false`; 6.6.e mandatory + time-bounded revert to `false` and redeploy + verification via `docker exec env`; 6.6.f negative-proof verification — re-run §6.4 + §6.5 with kill switch closed and confirm worker processes as dry-run with `provider_id: null` and no ERPNext doc created); 6.7 producer-split + envelope verification across all three iterations with per-event-type producer attribution table (route → promoter → processor); 6.8 final-state verification (all journals stay `pending_approval`, all three jobs in `completed` bucket, iteration 2's `last_provider_id` is the ERPNext document name); 6.9 record evidence. §7 exit criteria (12 items). §8 verification commands (4 groups including replay determinism check that mirrors Slice 2D test 9). - **Finance Ops Phase 3-9 — Controlled-Tenant Adapter Worker Activation Runbook (Dry Run) (`docs/architecture/finance/staging-adapter-worker-activation-log.md` (NEW))**: First of two Slice 2E deliverables per [`slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md`](docs/architecture/finance/slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md) §5.5. The document specifies the exact dry-run activation sequence the deploy owner uses to flip six to nine env vars on `staging-finance-adapter-worker` (the Coolify app whose YAML service block Slice 2C added to [`deploy/coolify/finance-workers.staging.example.yml`](deploy/coolify/finance-workers.staging.example.yml)) to enable the adapter worker for one controlled staging tenant (`a11dfb63-4b18-4eb8-872e-747af2e37c46`) while registering the ERPNext sandbox adapter at boot. **Worker-only activation, not ERPNext proof execution** — the actual `simulateDealWon → approveFinanceAction → runAdapterPollCycle → adapter_queue` end-to-end demonstration against sandbox ERPNext is **Phase 3-10**. **`FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false` stays as the safest default throughout 3-9** — the one-time flip is Phase 3-10 §6 step 6 only. §1 frames the value of the worker-only intermediate gate (proves tenant config + DB connection + ERPNext adapter registration at boot + heartbeat-file healthcheck transition without exposing any tenant-visible side effect). §2 lists "None" for every modality including `tenant_integrations` row insertion (deferred to Phase 3-10 §6 step 2), `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=true` anywhere, `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE` ≠ `draft_only`. §3 12 prerequisites including the Slice 2A/B/C/D commit list. §4 activation envelope is six to nine env-var changes on one Coolify app: the three enable flags (`ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` / `ENABLE_FINANCE_WORKERS` / `ENABLE_FINANCE_ADAPTER_WORKER` strict `=== 'true'`) plus `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS` (single UUID, no implicit "all" fall-through per `parseControlledTenantIds()` in `backend/lib/finance/financeWorkerCommon.js`) plus three ERPNext credential env vars (`FINANCE_ERPNEXT_BASE_URL` / `_API_KEY` / `_API_SECRET`, sandbox-only, rejected by the adapter constructor URL guard at `erpnextSandboxAdapter.js:89-128` if non-sandbox) plus optional `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_SANDBOX_BASE_URLS` allowlist; safety gates `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE=draft_only` and `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false` explicitly preserved as unchanged at the safest defaults. §5 dry-run activation sequence: 5.1 preflight (no mutation, includes confirming the sandbox ERPNext endpoint matches a built-in pattern OR is enumerated in the explicit allowlist); 5.2 exact env block with strict-equality reminder (matches `isFinanceAdapterWorkerEnabled()` at `backend/workers/financeAdapterWorker.js:116-122`), tenant-id reminder (matches `parseControlledTenantIds()`), and ERPNext credentials reminder (entry block at `:484-516` registers the adapter only if all three credential env vars are set; missing any causes `[finance-adapter-worker] erpnext credentials not configured — provider not registered (worker will skip erpnext jobs)` which is a 3-9 stop condition); 5.3 Coolify redeploy; 5.4 explicit "do NOT touch other apps in 3-9"; 5.5 explicit "do NOT flip `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` in 3-9". §6 expected worker behavior after activation: boot sequence with adapter registration (`[finance-adapter-worker] registered erpnext sandbox adapter` with structured `provider` + `base_url` on success, or `[finance-adapter-worker] failed to register erpnext sandbox adapter — continuing with empty registry` on constructor failure), first/subsequent poll cycles invoking `runAdapterPollCycle({ pool, adapters, tenantIds, eventStore, now })` with the expected empty result because no queued `adapter_jobs` rows exist yet (the prerequisites for any to exist — Phase 3-7 route activation + Slice's later persistent-events lift — are 3-9 out of scope), explicit "what does NOT happen" list (no provider HTTP write thanks to kill switch, no adapter execution against ERPNext sandbox, no `finance.adapter_jobs` mutations, no `finance.audit_events` writes, no journal mutations, no `finance.projection_state` writes, no backend route activity, no tenant-facing change). §7 health/log/heartbeat expectations carry over the Phase 3-4 disabled-state heartbeat limitation; §7.3 lists the exact expected log lines emitted by `backend/workers/financeAdapterWorker.js` (registration line, startup line with `adapter_count: 1`, per-cycle `poll cycle complete` with all four counters at `0`) and the error log lines that indicate trouble (registration failure, credentials not configured, missing pool/eventStore wiring, cycle crashed, enabled-but-no-tenant). §8 verification commands as operator instructions only (7 command groups: container/healthcheck status, log lines confirming enabled + tenant-configured + adapter-registered, heartbeat file read with adapter-worker schema, no new `finance.adapter_jobs` queued/running/succeeded/failed rows, no new `finance.adapter.*` `audit_events` rows, sandbox ERPNext endpoint NOT contacted, no production action confirmation). §9 rollback is config-only with four sub-options (per-worker flag, worker-tier, whole-Finance-Ops on the worker app, tenant-list clear, credentials-only clear) — none touches code or schema; explicit "no data is lost or corrupted" because the adapter worker only reads/writes `finance.adapter_jobs` via optimistic-lock claim and there are zero queued rows during 3-9. §10 16 stop conditions including the most critical: sandbox ERPNext endpoint shows any inbound API call or any newly-created doc (means `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` is somehow `true` — immediate halt, most critical 3-9 safety violation), `finance.adapter_jobs` rows transitioning to `running` / `succeeded` / `failed` (means upstream data leaked in or worker is processing something it shouldn't), any tenant other than `a11dfb63-...` appearing in worker logs, `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE` set to anything other than `draft_only`, production env touched in any way. §11 18 hard constraints all status-confirmed. §12 acceptance for the runbook (17 items checked) + execution acceptance criteria. §13 empty evidence pack table.
