Maps cleanly to 2C-13 controlled-tenant-enablement §"Step 4 — Enable the worker toggles (optional, per worker)" for the adapter worker only. Cross-references [`staging-worker-activation-log.md`](docs/architecture/finance/staging-worker-activation-log.md) (3-5, the structural twin for projection-worker activation), [`adapter-worker-sandbox-plan.md`](docs/architecture/finance/adapter-worker-sandbox-plan.md) (2C-8, the original adapter-worker sandbox posture), and forward to [`erpnext-staging-sandbox-proof-results.md`](docs/architecture/finance/erpnext-staging-sandbox-proof-results.md) (3-10, the proof execution runbook that runs against the activated worker).
- **Finance Ops Slice 2D — `adapter_queue` projection integration proof (`backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/adapterQueueProjection.integration.test.js` (NEW))**: Fourth implementation packet of Slice 2 per the frozen design (`slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md` §5.4). Single end-to-end integration test file (10 tests, 144 ms, zero network IO) that drives the full producer → promoter → processor → projection lifecycle against real component wiring: real `createFinanceDomainService` (Slice 1 + 2B `approveFinanceAction` promoter wire from `e66538f0` / `d671d816` / `1d2b41e6`), real `createErpnextSandboxAdapter` (Slice 2A) with `httpClient.post` mocked only, real `runAdapterPollCycle` (Slice 2B processor), real `createAdapterQueueProjectionWorker` (Phase 2B-10 consumer — Slice 2 makes no projection-side changes), real `createProjectionRunner` driving the worker, single shared in-memory `createFinanceEventStore`. The proof chain: `simulateDealWon` writes `adapter_job.status='draft'` and emits ZERO `finance.adapter.*` events → `approveFinanceAction` promoter transitions `draft→queued` and emits exactly one `finance.adapter.sync_queued` → `adapter_queue` projection surfaces the item in the `queued` bucket → `runAdapterPollCycle` claims the queued row, calls the real ERPNext adapter (which calls the mocked `httpClient.post` with the correct `doctype: 'Journal Entry'` / `docstatus: 0` body at `/api/resource/Journal%20Entry`), and emits exactly one `finance.adapter.sync_succeeded` (or `sync_failed`) → projection moves the item from `queued` to `completed` (or `failed`). Test harness wires every piece via `wireSlice2Chain({ httpClientOverride })` returning `{ eventStore, service, erpnextAdapter, httpClient, httpCalls, runner, worker, storeProvider, dispatchPending, bucketsOf, realBucket }`. `dispatchPending()` drains events appended since the last call and walks them through the runner. `bucketsOf()` is the convenience query for the §7 `{queued, running, failed, completed}` read model. `realBucket()` is the **post-Codex-P2 refactor seam** — async snapshot of the live domain-service tenant bucket AFTER promotion (via `service.getState(TENANT_ID)`), returning the actual post-promotion `adapter_job` row that the promoter mutated in place. Tests cover: (1) `simulateDealWon` pre-approval state (draft, no `sync_queued`); (2) promoter emits `sync_queued` and projection shows queued item with correct envelope (`aggregate_type='adapter_job'`, `aggregate_id=job.id`, `provider='erpnext'`, `mode='draft_only'`); (3) success lifecycle: real adapter call → `httpClient.post` hits correct ERPNext endpoint → `sync_succeeded` → projection moves to completed; (4) terminal-failure lifecycle: throwing `httpClient` + `attempts=4` patched on the real post-promotion row tips into permanent on first failure → `sync_failed` with `permanent: true` → projection moves to failed; (5) producer-split assertion: across the full lifecycle, `sync_queued` is observed ONLY in the promoter window, `sync_succeeded` / `sync_failed` ONLY in the processor window (the test the prior end-to-end was missing per Codex `1d2b41e6` review); (6) envelope invariant: every `finance.adapter.*` event uses `aggregate_type='adapter_job'`, no `object_type` / `object_id` columns at the envelope level (the Slice 2D `ENVELOPE` test at `adapterQueueProjection.integration.test.js:485-487` asserts `!('object_type' in evt)` + `!('object_id' in evt)` on the envelope object exclusively — payload-body `object_*` duplicates inside `evt.payload` exist by current Slice 2 design per `adapterJobProcessor.js:155-156`/`:185-186` and `adapterJobPromoter.js:56-57` and are NOT a drift violation), embedded `adapter_job` snapshot per 2B-10 §3; (7) journal stays at `pending_approval` end-to-end (Phase 3-8 §5.7 contract — no auto-posting); (8) replay determinism: `runner.replay(ADAPTER_QUEUE_PROJECTION_NAME, TENANT_ID)` rebuilds projection state byte-identically (`JSON.stringify` equal) per §4.9 replay parity; (9) idempotent dispatch: re-dispatching the same `sync_queued` event leaves exactly one queue item (projection's "one active item per `adapter_job_id` per tenant" invariant); (10) safety boundary: with `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` unset (default), processor records `dry_run: true` succeeded with ZERO `httpClient.post` calls. **Hard constraints satisfied:** no live ERPNext call (httpClient.post is captured into an array via the test harness), no production endpoint or credential support (sandbox allowlist `['sandbox.example.com']`), no migration applied, no staging / Coolify / Doppler mutation, no route persistent-events activation, `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` remains structurally fail-closed at `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:48`, `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged, no provider writes outside mocked sandbox adapter tests. **Codex P2 follow-up applied within the same packet** — the original drafted test reconstructed the queued job at the processor handoff as `{ ...sim.adapter_job, status: 'queued' }` (`adapterQueueProjection.integration.test.js:262/339/409/465/527/619` in the pre-refactor draft), which would have hidden any promoter-side drift in processor-critical fields (`payload`, `attempts`, `aggregate_id`, `provider`, `mode`). Codex (Slack `#development` 2026-05-25 15:18 EDT, message TS `1779736722.965409`) flagged this as P2: the proof must consume the actual promoter output, not a synthetic reconstruction from the pre-promotion `simulateDealWon` clone. Refactor: introduced `realBucket()` async helper that wraps `service.getState(TENANT_ID)` (the domain service's deep-cloned tenant-bucket snapshot, which contains the real post-promotion `adapter_job` row the promoter mutated in place); replaced all six synthetic reconstructions with `await ctx.realBucket()` passed straight to `runAdapterPollCycle({ bucket: ... })`. The failed-path test patches only `attempts=4` on the real row (everything else — payload, status, provider, mode, aggregate*id — sourced from the genuine promoter mutation) so terminal-failure semantics remain proveable while the cross-stage handoff stays honest. Note that `approveResult.promoted_adapter_jobs[0]` (Codex's literal suggestion) is NOT usable as the processor input because `adapterJobPromoter.js:233-238` returns only a 4-field summary `{id, provider, operation, mode}` — missing `payload`, `attempts`, `status`, `aggregate_id` that `runAdapterPollCycle` needs; reading from the live bucket via `getState` (Codex's "another direct read of the mutated queued row" alternative) is the correct shape. All 10 tests pass after the refactor. **Cross-cutting regression fixed in the same patch (Codex Slack verdict 2026-05-25 16:56 EDT, message TS `1779742613.500779`):** the previously-staged modification to `backend/lib/finance/projections/projectionRunner.js:28-50` had added a `seq` field to `positionOf()` for same-millisecond event tie-breaking, sourced from the in-memory event store's `_seq` insertion index. While the tie-break logic itself is sound, propagating `_seq` into the \_persisted* cursor shape broke the replay-validation harness's cross-rebuild cursor-parity invariant: `_seq` is a store-local counter that is not invariant across runtimes, so two independent rebuilds of the same business stream produced cursors with different `seq` values and `cursor_identical = false` (`replayValidationHarness.js:544`). Verified by running the suspect suites on clean `HEAD` (45/45 pass) vs. the staged branch (37/45 pass — 5 direct cursor-shape failures in `projectionRunner.test.js` + 3 harness invariant failures in `replayValidationHarness.test.js`). Codex chose option 2 (the cleaner architectural fix): keep `_seq` as an internal ordering tie-break in `comparePosition()` / replay sorting, but do NOT persist `seq` into the cursor shape. Implementation: (a) `positionOf()` reverted to returning the portable `{ created_at, id }` shape with a comment explaining why `_seq` is excluded; (b) `comparePosition()` reverted to the original `created_at` ASC + `id` ASC contract; (c) new internal `compareEvents(a, b)` helper added that compares two raw events (not positions), preserves the `_seq` tie-break for events sharing the same `created_at`, and is used only at `projectionRunner.js:329` for replay sort (the in-process sort path that has direct access to event objects, vs. the persisted cursor comparison path which only sees the portable position shape); (d) call site at line 329 changed from `comparePosition(positionOf(a), positionOf(b))` to `compareEvents(a, b)`. Net result: same-millisecond replay ordering still uses `_seq` when present; persisted cursor identity is the portable `{ created_at, id }` it always was; harness invariant restored intact (no harness/test changes needed). All 55 tests across the 3 affected suites pass (26 `projectionRunner.test.js` + 19 `replayValidationHarness.test.js` + 10 `adapterQueueProjection.integration.test.js`); full finance regression 378/378 across 24 individual files (the `node --test __tests__/lib/finance/` directory-level run reports a single spurious `fail 1` that is a Node test-runner discovery-walker artifact for the directory entity itself, not a real test failure — confirmed by per-file enumeration).
- **Finance Ops Slice 2C — `finance-adapter-worker` process shell + shared worker common module (`backend/workers/financeAdapterWorker.js` (NEW), `backend/lib/finance/financeWorkerCommon.js` (NEW), `backend/workers/financeProjectionWorker.js`, `backend/__tests__/workers/financeAdapterWorker.test.js` (NEW), `backend/package.json`, `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.staging.example.yml`)**: Third implementation packet of Slice 2 per the frozen design (`slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md` §5.3). Delivers the disabled-by-default Coolify-deployable worker process that hosts the Slice 2B job processor, plus the factored-out `financeWorkerCommon.js` shared utilities. **`financeWorkerCommon.js`** exports `parseControlledTenantIds(envValue, opts)`, `writeWorkerHeartbeat({ path, workerName, extra, log })`, and `installSignalHandlers(stop, log)` — extracted from `financeProjectionWorker.js` to avoid duplication. **`financeProjectionWorker.js` refactored** to import these helpers mechanically; semantics byte-equivalent (the projection worker is enabled today in Phase 3-5, so this refactor preserves all existing behavior; all 13 existing tests still pass). **`financeAdapterWorker.js`** mirrors the projection worker structurally: three-tier `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS && ENABLE_FINANCE_WORKERS && ENABLE_FINANCE_ADAPTER_WORKER` strict-literal-`'true'` gate via `isFinanceAdapterWorkerEnabled()`; `parseControlledTenantIds()` against `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS` (empty = no tenants = no-op; NO implicit "process all" fall-through); heartbeat-file pattern at `FINANCE_ADAPTER_WORKER_HEARTBEAT_PATH` (default `/tmp/finance-adapter-worker-heartbeat.json`); 5000 ms default poll interval via `FINANCE_ADAPTER_WORKER_POLL_MS`; no HTTP `/health` endpoint (same gap as projection worker per Phase 3-4 §5.1 — heartbeat-file healthcheck is the deploy-time signal). Factory `startFinanceAdapterWorker({ pool, adapters, eventStore, tenantIds, runAdapterPollCycleHandler, now, autoStart })` returns `{ stop, runOnce }`. The `autoStart` option defaults to true for the production entry block and false for tests — needed because calling the factory directly in tests would race the production `setImmediate(runCycle)` against the explicit `runOnce()` and double-invoke the injected poll handler. The disabled-path returns an idle stub with `runOnce: async () => null` and no DB connection opened (the `pg.Pool` object is constructed lazily by the entry block before the gate runs; the disabled gate returns before any `pool.query()` is called). `runOnce` is the test seam — injects `runAdapterPollCycleHandler` to bypass the production import of `runAdapterPollCycle` from `adapterJobProcessor.js`. The entry block at the bottom requires `FINANCE_DB_URL || DATABASE_URL` at process startup (same exit-before-gate pattern as `financeProjectionWorker.js:378-383`). **`backend/package.json`** adds `"worker:finance-adapter": "node workers/financeAdapterWorker.js"` next to the existing `worker:finance-projection`. **`deploy/coolify/finance-workers.staging.example.yml`** adds a `finance-adapter-worker` service block mirroring the projection worker's structure: three enable flags hard-set to `false`; `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false` + `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE=draft_only` (two-layer safety per §4.6); empty `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS`; empty `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_SANDBOX_BASE_URLS`; heartbeat-file healthcheck against the adapter worker's heartbeat path; documents that activation is Phase 3-9 scope (deferred). The deferred-services comment block updated to remove the adapter worker (which is now in the file) and retain the audit worker as the remaining deferred. Tests: **17 in `financeAdapterWorker.test.js`** covering the three-tier gate (each level strict `=== 'true'`, plus 'TRUE'/'1'/'yes' all keep it disabled), `parseControlledTenantIds` parses + trims + dedups, disabled-state returns idle stub (no `runAdapterPollCycle` call), empty-tenants no-op (heartbeat written with zero counters), enabled-with-tenants invokes pollHandler with the contract args `{ pool, adapters, tenantIds, eventStore, now }` (`now` is a callable), processor throw is caught and worker doesn't crash, heartbeat counters reflect cycle results. All 13 existing **`financeProjectionWorker.test.js` tests pass after the `financeWorkerCommon.js` refactor** — no behavioral regression. Total **30/30 in worker tests; full finance regression 380/380**. **Hard constraints satisfied:** worker disabled by default in all configs; no provider writes (`FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` defaults to false); no production endpoint/credential support (sandbox allowlist required); no route persistent-events activation; no staging/Coolify/Doppler mutation (code + YAML change only); config comments explicitly note "operator would deploy this" / "Phase 3-9 scope" language. `__resetAdapterWorkerStateForTests` exported for test isolation. Test helper `withEnv` corrected to be `async` + `await fn()` so env var overrides are visible to the async test body (was a real bug surfaced during validation — synchronous `finally` would have restored env before the async body ran).
- **Finance Ops Slice 2B — Adapter job promoter + processor + `approveFinanceAction()` modification (`backend/lib/finance/adapterJobPromoter.js` (NEW), `backend/lib/finance/adapterJobProcessor.js` (NEW), `backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/adapterJobPromoter.test.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/adapterJobProcessor.test.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/financeDomainService.test.js`)**: Second implementation packet of Slice 2 per the frozen design (`slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md` §5.2). Delivers the producer side of the canonical `finance.adapter.*` event taxonomy. **`adapterJobPromoter.js`** exports `promoteLinkedAdapterJobs({ pool, bucket, tenantId, aggregateId, eventStore, actor, requestId, braidTraceId, now })`. Dual-mode operation: persistent mode (`pool` parameter) uses `BEGIN; SELECT ... FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED; UPDATE ... RETURNING; INSERT event; COMMIT` per the §4.1 lock posture; in-memory mode (`bucket` parameter) walks `bucket.adapterJobs` and mutates row status in place. Emits exactly one `finance.adapter.sync_queued` event per promoted job per §4.7 payload contract (Track A envelope with `aggregate_type='adapter_job'`, `aggregate_id=job.id`, no `object_type`/`object_id` drift; embedded `adapter_job` snapshot showing `status: 'queued'`). Natural idempotency via `status='draft'` filter — already-queued jobs are skipped, no double-promotion, no duplicate `sync_queued` emission. **`adapterJobProcessor.js`** exports `runAdapterPollCycle({ pool, bucket, adapters, tenantIds, eventStore, now, buildProviderPayload, backoffOpts })` returning `{ claimed_count, succeeded_count, failed_count, skipped_count, summary }` per §4.2 contract. Per-tenant single-row claim via `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED LIMIT 1 → UPDATE status='running'` (persistent) or filter+mutate (in-memory). 7-step per-job sequence: adapter lookup → `assertWritePermitted(operation, mode)` per §4.6 behavior matrix (code-side gate; named exports `AdapterPermissionError` + `AdapterCapabilityError`) → `buildProviderPayload` boundary call → `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED` dominant kill switch (skip HTTP + record dry-run when false) → adapter method dispatch via `adapterMethodForOperation` mapping (`push_draft → pushDraft`, etc.) → state update (`succeeded`/`failed`/requeued) → event emission. Emits ONLY `sync_succeeded` and `sync_failed` (never `sync_queued` — that's exclusively the promoter, per §4.7). `AdapterCapabilityError` and payload-build failures are PERMANENT (no retry); other adapter errors are transient and requeue via `applyRequeueInMemory` / `applyTerminalPersistent` with `status='queued'`, incremented `attempts`, and a `next_attempt_at` computed by exported `computeBackoffMs(attempts, opts)` per §4.8 (`max_attempts=5` default via `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MAX_ATTEMPTS`, exponential `2^attempts * base_ms`, cap `1.8e6` ms, ±5s jitter, injectable `random` for deterministic tests). Terminal failure (`attempts >= max_attempts`) emits `sync_failed` with `permanent: true` and freezes the row at `status='failed'`. Adapter `ctx` passed as `{ objectType, runtimePolicy: { provider, mode }, tenantId, jobId, now }` matching Slice 2A's rich-object form. **`financeDomainService.js` `approveFinanceAction` modified**: after marking the approval `approved` and emitting `finance.approval.approved`, the service now calls `promoteLinkedAdapterJobs({ bucket, tenantId, aggregateId: approval.target_id, eventStore, actor, requestId, braidTraceId, now })` and returns `promoted_adapter_jobs: [...]` alongside `approval` and `governance_decision`. The Phase 3-8 §5.7 contract is preserved — the journal entry's `status` stays at `pending_approval`; only the adapter_job transitions `draft → queued`. Tests: **12 promoter tests** (input validation, in-memory promotion + event shape, idempotency via status filter, repeat-call no-op, tenant scoping, persistent-mode SQL discipline with `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` + `BEGIN/COMMIT`, rollback on error + client release); **19 processor tests** (`assertWritePermitted` matrix, `computeBackoffMs` exponential growth + cap + jitter, no-queued-jobs no-op, empty-tenantIds no-op, dry-run path with writes disabled, NEVER claims `draft` jobs, NEVER emits `sync_queued`, skip-when-no-adapter requeues without consuming attempt, writes-enabled adapter call with correct ctx shape, `AdapterCapabilityError` is permanent, transient errors requeue with `next_attempt_at`, terminal failure at max attempts, per-tenant scoping, `buildProviderPayload` invocation, payload-build failure is permanent); **4 new domain-service tests** (regression: `simulateDealWon` does NOT emit `sync_queued`; integration: `approveFinanceAction` promotes linked adapter_jobs and emits exactly one `sync_queued`; contract: journal stays `pending_approval`; idempotency: promoter status filter prevents double-emit). All existing 21 domain-service tests still pass. Total **48/48 in 2B files; full finance regression 380/380**.
- **Finance Ops Slice 2A — Provider payload boundary + ERPNext sandbox adapter (`backend/lib/finance/accountingAdapters/providerPayloadBuilder.js` (NEW), `backend/lib/finance/accountingAdapters/erpnextSandboxAdapter.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/accountingAdapters/providerPayloadBuilder.test.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/accountingAdapters/erpnextSandboxAdapter.test.js` (NEW))**: First implementation packet of Slice 2 per the frozen design (`slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md` §5.1). Delivers the E6 metadata-stripping boundary and the sandbox-only ERPNext adapter. **`providerPayloadBuilder.js`** exports `buildProviderPayload(canonical, runtimePolicy)` that deep-clones the canonical object and strips the 11-item internal-metadata denylist (`draft_only`, `governance_decision`, `policy_decision`, `governance_policy_snapshot`, `braid_trace_id`, `correlation_id`, `causation_id`, `request_id`, `tenant_id`, `ai_generated`, actor-id fields `created_by` / `updated_by` / `approved_by`) plus the leading-underscore convention (any key starting with `_` is internal). Supports per-adapter `runtimePolicy.allowlist` override (Set or array of keys exempted from stripping). Also exports `assertNoInternalMetadata(payload)` test helper that walks the payload recursively (handles cycles) and throws if any denylisted key appears at any depth, and a frozen `INTERNAL_METADATA_DENYLIST` constant. **`erpnextSandboxAdapter.js`** exports a factory `createErpnextSandboxAdapter({ baseUrl, apiKey, apiSecret, httpClient, sandboxAllowlist })` returning the full `AccountingAdapter` interface per `adapter-runtime-contract.md` §2: `pushDraft(canonical, ctx)` constructs `docstatus: 0` ERPNext payload via `buildProviderPayload`, `pullStatus(providerId, ctx)`, `reconcile(...)` (read-only sandbox-OK), and `pushFinal` / `voidRecord` that throw the named-export `AdapterCapabilityError`. Constructor validates `baseUrl` against the built-in sandbox allowlist (localhost, `*.local`, `sandbox.*`) plus opt-in explicit FQDN list from `sandboxAllowlist`; rejects production-looking URLs at constructor time. Also exports `AdapterConfigError` for misconfiguration. Default `sandboxAllowlist` is `[]` — operator must explicitly populate. `ERPNEXT_PROVIDER_OBJECT_MAP` exported for Account + JournalEntry mapping. Tests: **17 in `providerPayloadBuilder.test.js`** covering each denylist item, nested-object stripping, leading-underscore stripping, allowlist override (Set + array), `assertNoInternalMetadata` rejection paths, and cycle handling; **25 in `erpnextSandboxAdapter.test.js`** covering constructor URL rejection (production patterns), constructor URL acceptance (localhost, `*.local`, `sandbox.*`, explicit allowlist), `pushDraft` building correct ERPNext payload with `docstatus: 0` and stripped internal metadata (verified via `assertNoInternalMetadata`), `pushFinal` and `voidRecord` throwing `AdapterCapabilityError`, injected `httpClient` mockability. Total **42/42 pass**, ~174 ms, zero network IO. **Hard constraints satisfied:** no live HTTP calls in tests (injected fake httpClient), no production credentials/URLs in defaults, default sandbox allowlist empty (operator must populate), ERPNext push produces `docstatus: 0` (never `1`), preserves `aggregate_type` / `aggregate_id` vocabulary, ESM modules, native Node test runner. No code outside `accountingAdapters/` modified. Adapter ambiguity calls documented in the §5.1 packet report: (1) `pushDraft` ctx shape accepts either bare `objectType` string OR `{ objectType, runtimePolicy }` to bridge §5.1 vs Track E §2 wording — Slice 2B's processor adopts the rich object form. (2) `reconcile` implemented as a read-only `listObjects`-backed zero-drift report rather than throwing (matches §4.6 read-only permission). (3) `assertNoInternalMetadata` co-exported from the builder rather than as a standalone test-helper file (per the operative prompt; design freeze §5.1 mentioned a separate file).
- **Finance Ops Slice 2-0 — adapter worker + ERPNext sandbox design freeze (`docs/architecture/finance/slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md` (NEW))**: Design-freeze document for the next implementation slice. **No code shipped by this task**, no worker process implemented, no ERPNext adapter implemented, no provider HTTP call, no migration applied, no env var changed, no Coolify mutation, no staging activation, no production action. Slice 2 builds the runtime that makes Phase 3-9 / 3-10 honestly executable. §1 + §2 frame the scope ("what gets built" vs "what stays out": no live provider writes, no production credentials, no QuickBooks/Xero, no `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` lift, no `pushFinal` / `void` execution, no new finance domain semantics). §3 prerequisites including the Phase 3-1 baseline + Track E contract freeze + 2B-10 adapter_queue projection already-implemented consumer. §4 freezes 10 design decisions: (4.1) `finance.adapter_jobs` lifecycle + claim/lock via `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` optimistic-lock UPDATE scoped to `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS`, with a 5-min stuck-job watchdog; (4.2) job processor contract `runAdapterPollCycle({ pool, adapters, tenantIds, eventStore, now })` returning `{ claimed_count, succeeded_count, failed_count, skipped_count, summary[] }` with 7-step per-job processing sequence (load context → assertWritePermitted → buildProviderPayload → provider-writes-enabled code gate → adapter call → state update + event emission → terminal-failure approval row); (4.4) ERPNext sandbox adapter implements every required `AccountingAdapter` method per `adapter-runtime-contract.md` §2 with sandbox-only `base_url` guard (localhost / `*.local` / `sandbox.*` / `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_SANDBOX_BASE_URLS` allowlist), API-key auth, `docstatus: 0` constraint with no submit call, `pushFinal` / `voidRecord` / `reconcile` throw `AdapterCapabilityError`; (4.5) `buildProviderPayload(canonicalObject, runtimePolicy)` boundary strips an 11-item denylist (`draft_only`, `governance_decision`, `policy_decision`, `governance_policy_snapshot`, `braid_trace_id`, `correlation_id`, `causation_id`, `request_id`, `tenant_id`, `ai_generated`, `created_by`/`updated_by`/`approved_by`, leading-underscore convention) — denylist with explicit per-adapter allowlist override; shared `assertNoInternalMetadata` test helper; (4.6) two enforcement layers for the no-live-write guarantee — configuration (`FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false` dominant kill switch + `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE=draft_only`) AND code (`assertWritePermitted` per `adapter-runtime-contract.md` §4 + provider-writes-enabled code gate in the processor, not the adapter) with a behavior matrix for all 6 operation × 4 mode combinations; (4.7) sync event emission contract — `finance.adapter.sync_queued` / `sync_succeeded` / `sync_failed` with frozen Track A envelope (`aggregate_type = 'adapter_job'`, NO `object_type` / `object_id` drift), payload shapes including the embedded `adapter_job` snapshot per 2B-10 §3 expectation, idempotent emission via job-status re-read; (4.8) retry / DLQ minimum posture — `max_attempts = 5`, exponential backoff with ±5s jitter (15s/30s/1m/2m then terminal), terminal failure stays `failed` with `permanent: true` `sync_failed` event AND creates `finance.approvals` row with `target_type = 'adapter_job'`; explicit deferrals named (no HTTP cancel/retry endpoint, no `/ready` dead-letter count, no auto-escalation); (4.9) how the already-implemented `adapter_queue` projection (Phase 2B-10) consumes the events — no projection-side changes needed in Slice 2, just the producer; Slice 2D integration test obligations enumerated; (4.10) end-to-end flow after Slice 2 + Phase 3-9 + 3-10 land. §5 splits implementation into 5 parallel-safe packets: **2A** provider payload boundary + ERPNext sandbox adapter (3 files + tests); **2B** adapter job processor + sync event emission + modifications to `simulateDealWon` (3 files + tests); **2C** `finance-adapter-worker` process shell + config + factored-out `financeWorkerCommon.js` (3 files + projection-worker refactor); **2D** `adapter_queue` projection integration proof (end-to-end producer + consumer test); **2E** Phase 3-9 staging-adapter-worker-activation-log.md + Phase 3-10 erpnext-staging-sandbox-proof-results.md + adapter worker added to `finance-workers.staging.example.yml`. §6 cross-packet ordering: 2A + 2B + 2C parallel-safe; 2D waits for 2A+2B; 2E waits for 2A+2B+2C; 3 cross-packet contract risks flagged. §7 restates all 12 hard constraints with status confirmed. §8 acceptance for the design freeze (16 items all checked). §9 lists 5 open questions for Dre with defaults if no answer (dual-write to in-memory vs persistent, separate vs same Coolify worker app, sandbox-URL allowlist sufficiency, `financeWorkerCommon.js` refactor risk, approve-creates-adapter-job lifecycle wiring). §10 empty evidence pack table for Slice 2 commit hashes. Anchored on Phase 3 baseline `3c60d9ff`. The design freeze produces the contract; each 2A–2E packet lands as its own commit + Codex review.

it does NOT auto-post the journal (the journal stays at `pending_approval` indefinitely under HTTP-only operator actions); (8) `POST /approvals/:id/approve` (ai_agent with body-spoofed `actor_type: 'human'`) → **403** per governance decision path at `financeDomainService.js:611-616` — the long-standing actor-spoofing-prevention contract from commit `04a76bae`; (9) `POST /journal-entries/:id/reverse` split into **§5.9.a** (TESTABLE — reverse a non-posted journal → **HTTP 409** with `'Only posted journal entries can be reversed'` per `financeDomainService.js:523-526`, reject-is-pass framing) and **§5.9.b** (DEFERRED — reverse-success path requires a posted journal, but no HTTP route to posted state exists in the current runtime since `approveFinanceAction()` doesn't auto-post; - **Finance Ops Phase 3-6 — Replay / rebuild operational drill plan (dry run) (`docs/architecture/finance/staging-replay-drill-results.md` (NEW))**: Sixth packet of the Phase 3 controlled staging activation arc. Drill plan only — **no replay was run by this task**, no `runner.replay()` / `runner.replayAll()` invocation against any environment, no worker execution against staging, no Coolify mutation, no Doppler / env var change, no migration applied, no provider HTTP write. The plan adapts the Phase 2C-12 architectural drill design ([`replay-rebuild-operational-drill.md`](docs/architecture/finance/replay-rebuild-operational-drill.md)) into an executable staging runbook for the controlled tenant (`a11dfb63-4b18-4eb8-872e-747af2e37c46`), with concrete commands, pass/fail criteria, stop conditions, and explicit handling of the empty-stream case Phase 3-5 corrected. §1 frames why the drill is meaningful before Phase 3-7 / Slice 2: proves the replay path itself works end-to-end before events start flowing. §4 honestly documents the operator replay surface gap — the 2C-12 design assumes a "projection worker's operator `replay` / `replayAll` control surface" that does NOT exist in the deployed worker today (`runner.replay()` and `runner.replayAll()` are in-process methods on the runner instance built in `buildProjectionRunner()` at `backend/workers/financeProjectionWorker.js:185`, but no HTTP / CLI / IPC exposure for an operator). Three execution paths documented: Option A (run `replayValidationHarness.js` locally — proves invariant but bypasses staging worker), Option B (`docker exec` + one-off Node snippet against staging worker container — operational fidelity, recommended for first drill), Option C (add `backend/scripts/finance-replay-drill.js` per the deferred 2C-12 §7 deliverable — recommended next step but NOT delivered by 3-6, doc-only). §5 walks the 10-sub-step drill procedure: select controlled tenant, snapshot `finance.projection_state` rows + `md5(state_json::text)` hashes + `finance.audit_events` count as the "before" baseline and restore point, trigger `replayAll(tenantId)` (with §5.3 interaction note recommending temporary `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS=""` clear during drill to stop the worker poll loop from interleaving — uses the runner's per-`(projection, tenant)` mutex at `projectionRunner.js:294` as the actual safety guarantee), compare before/after, verify each projection (ledger / approval_queue / adapter_queue / audit_timeline) per its replay-validation harness check, verify repeated-replay determinism, verify degraded recovery is operator-only. **§5.4 nuance table — the Phase 3-5 correction explicitly carried forward and refined**: empty `finance.audit_events` + worker disabled + no operator replay = zero rows; empty + worker enabled + no operator replay = zero rows (3-5 correction, `runProjectionPollCycle()` doesn't write); empty + operator-triggered `replayAll` = **four rows with `cursor: null`, `status: 'idle'`, fresh `last_rebuilt_at`** because `runner.replay()` always writes `setState` per `projectionRunner.js:307,331-338` regardless of stream size; non-empty + replayAll = four rows with `cursor` at the last event. §5.8 enforces the infrastructure-event filtering rules: `audit_timeline` is the only consumer of `finance.audit.event_appended` (opt-in via `includeInfrastructureEvents: true` in `buildProjectionRunner` at `backend/workers/financeProjectionWorker.js:194`); business projections (`ledger`, `approval_queue`, `adapter_queue`) never see it; verified via `replayValidationHarness.js` `checkInfrastructureEventFiltering`. §5.10 honestly notes that the drill cannot easily induce a real degraded projection without violating hard constraints (no event-store mutation, no code change), so 3-6 inherits the 2B-12 `checkDegradedRecovery` proof and only verifies the absence of degraded rows post-drill. §6 consolidated verification commands. §7 pass criteria; §8 enumerates 11 stop conditions. §9 rollback / restore: three deterministic paths (restore from snapshot, re-replay, truncate-and-rebuild) since the event stream is immutable and the projection_state is a rebuildable cache. §10 restates all 14 hard constraints with status confirmed. §11 acceptance lists 14 deliverables (all checked). §12 carries an empty execution evidence table. Anchored on Phase 3 baseline `3c60d9ff`. **Only valid `finance.projection_state.status` values used throughout** (`idle | replaying | degraded` per the runtime contract — no `'ok'` slip-ups). **No assumption that empty-stream-no-replay creates projection_state rows** — the 3-5 correction is preserved throughout.

`backend/__tests__/workers/financeProjectionWorker.test.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/routes/finance.v2.routes.test.js`, `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.example.yml`)**: Seven-task TDD slice that unblocks Phase 3-2 … 3-8 by closing the projection/audit prerequisite gap and wiring the Phase 2B Postgres event store behind an opt-in DI gate. **Task 1** adds dev-only draft migration `175_finance_projection_state_rls_draft.sql` (RLS companion to 174 — applied to nothing, draft until staging gating clears). **Task 2** adds the `audit_timeline` projection worker (consumes the full canonical taxonomy with `includeInfrastructureEvents=true` so `finance.audit.event_appended` is retained as audit context, never delivered to business projections). **Task 3** makes the `projectionRunner` store-provider seam async-aware (`await`s `getLiveStore`/`promoteShadow`/`getProjectionState`/`setProjectionState`) so a Postgres-backed provider can be plugged in without changing the runtime semantics. **Task 4** adds `createFinancePgProjectionStoreProvider` — a Postgres-backed `ProjectionStoreProvider` over `finance.projection_state`, hydrating live store rows from runner, idle-by-default behind the three-tier gate (`ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS && ENABLE_FINANCE_WORKERS && ENABLE_FINANCE_PROJECTION_WORKER`), with optional `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS` allow-list. `reverseJournalEntry`, `approveFinanceAction`) plus `listAuditEvents` / `getState` now `await eventStore.append`/`query`, so the synchronous in-memory store (await of a sync return is a no-op) and the async `financeEventStore.pg.js` adapter both work correctly. **Task 7** wires the pg event store into `createFinanceV2Routes(pgPool, opts)` behind `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS=true` AND a provided pool — the default remains the in-memory event store; `opts.eventStore` injection still wins for tests; the flag-set-but-no-pool case falls back to in-memory rather than throwing at boot. All route handlers awaiting the now-async service. `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.example.yml` gained the `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS=false` and `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS=` env keys with a note that the backend app must also set `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS=true` for events to persist. No migration applied; `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` and `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` remain disabled. - **Finance Ops Phase 2C-13/2C-14/2C-15 — controlled tenant enablement, staging activation review, and production-readiness review (`docs/architecture/finance/controlled-tenant-enablement.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/staging-activation-review.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/production-readiness-review.md` (NEW))**: Final batch of the Phase 2C staging-readiness gate — documentation only, nothing enabled. **2C-13** defines the procedure to enable Finance Ops for **exactly one controlled staging tenant**: the enablement layers (environment-scoped `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` route mount + per-tenant `financeOps` module gate + the three-tier worker gate), why this is structurally one-tenant-only (`ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` only makes the route _exist_; the per-tenant `financeOps` module flag is what grants _access_ — there is no global-enablement switch), tenant selection criteria, the ordered enablement steps, an eight-check smoke-test sequence (route auth, module-gate denied/allowed, runtime status, draft invoice, balanced + unbalanced journal draft, AI approval block), and a single-config-change rollback (per-tenant module-flag disable, or the `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS=false` environment kill switch). **2C-14** is the staging activation review: a checklist mapping every readiness item to its 2C deliverable, every Phase 2C stop condition assessed (all clear — the one "open" item, the `authenticated` JWT-claim verification, is an explicitly gated staging check with a fail-closed fallback), a documentation-vs-execution split listing the operator activation steps, and an explicit recorded decision — **GO** for the staging-readiness gate, **conditional GO** for staging activation execution (pending the environment-dependent verifications), **NO-GO** for production. **2C-15** is the production-readiness review: production stays disabled (`ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unset on Hetzner, no migration, no worker, no provider connection), ten explicit production prerequisites enumerated (provider sandbox maturity, tenant billing, backup/restore, observability maturity, audit retention, incident response, encrypted provider credential storage, SLO/SLA, support procedure, and the carried-forward engineering prerequisites — the incremental event-store query and the `audit_pack_requests` table), and a statement that the production gate is a separate future review that staging activation never rolls forward into. No migration applied; no `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` change; production remains disabled.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2C-10/2C-11/2C-12 — dead-letter/retry verification, observability/alerting, and replay/rebuild operational drill (`docs/architecture/finance/dead-letter-retry-verification.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/observability-alerting.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/replay-rebuild-operational-drill.md` (NEW))**: Fourth batch of the Phase 2C staging-readiness gate — documentation only, no code, nothing deployed. **2C-10** consolidates and verifies adapter retry/dead-letter behavior from `adapter-runtime-contract.md` §3: retry count (`max_attempts = 5`, `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MAX_ATTEMPTS`), exponential backoff with bounded ±5 s jitter (base 15 s, ×2 per attempt, 30-min cap — schedule ~15 s/30 s/1 m/2 m then terminal), terminal failure (`status = 'failed'` with attempts exhausted, `sync_failed` `permanent: true`, a `target_type = 'adapter_job'` pending approval), dead-letter visibility across three surfaces (the job row, the `pending` approval worklist row, and the append-only/immutable `sync_failed` event — the last makes the dead-letter fact permanent and replayable, so it cannot silently disappear), operator recovery steps (inspect cause → re-queue/cancel/escalate, re-queue resets `attempts`), and the replay interaction (event replay rebuilds the `adapter_queue` read model and never re-executes a job — re-running is operator-only). Provider writes stay sandbox-only throughout. **2C-11** maps the nine required observability signals (worker up/down, worker lag, replay failure, degraded projection, adapter sync failure, dead-letter count, audit evidence build failure, RLS/tenant mismatch, finance route 401/403 spikes) each to a source, a surface, and an alert, fitted to the **existing** stack — Pino structured logs, Coolify `json-file` capture, Uptime Kuma on VPS-2, and the worker `GET /health`/`GET /ready` surfaces (Prometheus/Grafana are absent and explicitly not depended on; a `/metrics` endpoint is noted as a future additive enhancement). Logs carry `tenant_id` (a UUID, safe) on every finance line where known; a finance-specific never-log rule plus the existing Pino redaction keep JWT contents and `tenant_integrations.api_credentials` out of logs; every signal is mapped to a concrete operator action. **2C-12** defines the replay/rebuild operational drill (doc-only — the optional `finance-replay-drill.js` script is not delivered): a ten-step procedure for the controlled tenant — select tenant, snapshot `finance.projection_state`, `replayAll`, compare before/after, verify the ledger / approval-queue / adapter-queue projections, verify evidence-pack determinism (byte-identical packs with injected `packId`/`generatedAt`), and verify degraded recovery is operator-triggered — using the already-implemented `replayValidationHarness.js` (2B-12) as its verification engine, with divergence treated as a blocking stop condition and a rollback/restore procedure (restore from snapshot or by deterministic rebuild; the event stream is never mutated). No migration applied; no `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` change; the staging gate remains closed.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2C-7/2C-8/2C-9 — audit/evidence worker, adapter worker sandbox, and ERPNext sandbox proof gate (`docs/architecture/finance/audit-worker-staging-plan.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/adapter-worker-sandbox-plan.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/erpnext-sandbox-proof.md` (NEW))**: Third batch of the Phase 2C staging-readiness gate — documentation only, no code, nothing deployed, no provider connection opened. **2C-7** plans audit/evidence-worker staging activation: the worker is a thin host for the already-implemented, pure read-only `auditEvidenceBuilder.js` (Phase 2B-11), so hosting it cannot introduce a write path; evidence generation is read-only (DB-layer immutability triggers + deep-cloned inputs), evidence packs are deterministic via injectable `packId`/`generatedAt` (byte-identical rebuilds incl. integrity hashes), infrastructure-event inclusion (`finance.audit.event_appended`) is explicit opt-in (`includeInfrastructureEvents`, default false), evidence is tenant-scoped, and malformed lineage is surfaced (logged at `warn`) without corrupting evidence state; `audit_timeline` is hosted here with the infra-event opt-in to isolate infrastructure-event handling. No provider writes, no new public routes — only the internal health surface. **2C-8** plans adapter-worker sandbox-only activation: the row-driven worker drains `finance.adapter_jobs` and emits the canonical adapter events; "no live provider write" is enforced by **two independent layers** — configuration (`FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false` dominant kill switch + `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE=draft_only`) **and** code (`assertWritePermitted` write guard + an in-code provider-writes-enabled gate that skips the HTTP call entirely while the flag is false); provider payloads strip internal runtime metadata (decision E6 `buildProviderPayload` boundary); only sandbox `base_url`s are permitted, no QuickBooks/Xero live credentials; failed jobs are observable (sync_failed events, permanent-failure dead-letter approval record, stuck-job watchdog). **2C-9** defines the ERPNext sandbox integration **proof gate** (doc-only — the `erpnextAdapter.js` implementation is explicitly a future Track-E/Phase-3 deliverable, not part of 2C): why ERPNext is first (decision E5 — self-hosted, API-key auth, no OAuth), the allowed/not-allowed contract, what must be demonstrated (sandbox-only connection, full `AccountingAdapter` interface, draft-only enforced at three levels incl. ERPNext `docstatus = 0` with no submit call, payload mapping with metadata stripping, replayable adapter events), a concrete proof procedure, and exit criteria — with an explicit statement that passing the proof unlocks neither production nor finalising writes nor QuickBooks/Xero. No migration applied; no `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` change; the staging gate remains closed.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2C-4/2C-5/2C-6 — persistent projection store, worker deployment config, and projection-worker staging plan (`docs/architecture/finance/persistent-projection-store-plan.md` (NEW), `backend/migrations/174_finance_projection_state_draft.sql` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/finance-worker-deployment-config.md` (NEW), `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.example.yml` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/projection-worker-staging-plan.md` (NEW))**: Second batch of the Phase 2C staging-readiness gate — documentation, one draft migration, and one example deploy config; no new finance semantics, nothing deployed. **2C-4** selects **Option A — a Postgres `finance.projection_state` table** for persistent projection state (over Redis or a hybrid), because the event store is already Postgres, degraded status and cursors must survive worker restarts, and `projection-runtime.md` §3 already anticipates a Postgres-backed store provider. Migration `174_finance_projection_state_draft.sql` creates one row per `(projection_name, tenant_id)` carrying the serialized read model (`state_json`) plus the runtime `ProjectionState` metadata (`schema_version`, `cursor_event_id`/`cursor_created_at`, `status`, `degraded_reason`, `last_rebuilt_at`, `updated_at` — the latter maintained by a `BEFORE UPDATE` trigger `finance.set_projection_state_updated_at` so it authoritatively reflects last row mutation, not just INSERT time); it is additive, idempotent, RLS-deferred, and intentionally **mutable** (a derived cache rebuilt by `replay()`, so no append-only/no-hard-delete trigger). The migration carries a `_draft` suffix and is not applied to any environment. A Postgres `ProjectionStoreProvider` makes `promoteShadow` a single atomic row `UPDATE`. **2C-5** prepares the disabled-by-default worker deployment configuration realising the Phase 2B-13 worker topology: a reviewed Coolify-native example compose file (`deploy/coolify/finance-workers.example.yml`) defining all three workers (`finance-projection-worker`, `finance-audit-worker`, `finance-adapter-worker`) with **every enable flag hard-set to `false`**. It introduces a three-tier enable gate — `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS && ENABLE_FINANCE_WORKERS && <per-worker flag>` (the new `ENABLE_FINANCE_WORKERS` middle tier extends 2B-13's two-tier gate — strictly more conservative) — plus the adapter safety flags `FINANCE_ADAPTER_MODE=draft_only` and `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false` (the dominant kill switch: no provider write while false). Health checks (`GET /health`/`/ready`), `restart: unless-stopped`, and `json-file` logging are specified; no provider credentials appear. The example file is a reviewed template, not referenced by any deployment. **2C-6** plans projection-worker staging activation **without changing runtime semantics**: the worker is a thin host for the Projection Runner consuming `finance.audit_events` via `financeEventStore.pg`, persisting to `finance.projection_state`, preserving the frozen Track A replay order (`created_at` ASC, `id` tie-break), catching up via `replay()` (the event-store interface exposes no "events after cursor" query — an incremental query is documented as an additive Phase-3 prerequisite, not a Phase 2C item), processing tenant-scoped streams, never delivering `finance.audit.event_appended` to business projections, pausing degraded projections, and recovering only via operator-triggered replay — enabled by the three-tier gate in staging only, with a one-flag non-destructive rollback. The pre-existing `worker-service-topology.md` §2.1 (Phase 2B-13) was reconciled to this `replay`-based catch-up plan — it had carried the same stale "events appended after cursor" assumption — so the Phase 3 worker implementation spec and the staging plan do not diverge. No migration applied; no `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` change; the staging gate remains closed.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2C-1/2C-2/2C-3 — staging RLS, PostgREST isolation, and service-role/tenant-claim verification (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-2c-rls-application-plan.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/postgrest-isolation-verification.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/service-role-tenant-claim-verification.md` (NEW))**: First batch of the Phase 2C staging-readiness gate — documentation only, no schema change, no new finance semantics. **2C-1** finalizes the `finance`-schema RLS posture: the tenant claim strategy is stated explicitly (the backend resolves tenant application-side via an email→`users` lookup and connects with the Supabase `service_role` key, which bypasses RLS), and the final RLS tenant expression is fixed as a normalized, consolidated predicate `tenant_id = (SELECT (auth.jwt() ->> 'tenant_id')::uuid) OR (SELECT auth.role()) = 'service_role'` — derived from the CRM's existing RLS patterns (migration `120_fix_remaining_security_issues.sql` inlines the claim and writes the bypass as `auth.jwt() ->> 'role' = 'service_role'`; `131_optimize_rls_leads_performance.sql` wraps the claim in a `current_tenant_id()` helper), not a verbatim copy of either. All eight finance tables require RLS; `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` plus the `service_role` write policies can be finalized immediately (fail-closed — a non-service-role connection sees zero rows), while the `authenticated` `tenant_match` SELECT policies stay DRAFT until the staging JWT-claim check passes. RLS is finalized in a separate gated staging-only migration, never in 172/173. **2C-2** verifies finance PostgREST isolation: `supabase/config.toml` exposes only `["public", "graphql_public"]` — `finance` is absent, so the stop condition ("stop if finance appears in public exposed schemas") is **not triggered**; documents the runtime re-verification commands (`select current_setting('pgrst.db_schemas')`, dashboard path, a `curl` 404 check) and the controlled read-only-view pattern required for any future exposure. **2C-3** verifies service-role and tenant-claim assumptions: documents the `service_role` RLS-bypass behavior explicitly, the `select auth.role()` staging check (blocking), the six-control backend middleware chain that is the _primary_ tenant enforcement, and a "false confidence" analysis establishing that RLS is a defense-in-depth layer — not the only control — for the backend access path. No migration applied; no `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` change; the staging gate remains closed.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-11 — audit/evidence builder runtime (`backend/lib/finance/auditEvidenceBuilder.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/auditEvidenceBuilder.test.js` (NEW, 17 cases), `docs/architecture/finance/audit-evidence-layer.md`)**: Added a pure, read-only evidence-pack builder that reconstructs auditor-grade evidence purely from the finance event stream. Exports `buildEvidencePack`, `queryAuditTimeline`, `getReversalChain`, and `isCanonicalFinanceEvent`; the `events` argument accepts either an array of event envelopes or a finance event store (`.replay`/`.query`). `buildEvidencePack` produces the SHA-256 tamper-evident pack defined in `audit-evidence-layer.md` §6 — `events_hash`, `approvals_hash`, `pack_hash` — and accepts injectable `packId`/`generatedAt` so the same event stream yields a byte-identical deterministic pack (the only non-deterministic fields are isolated as injectable inputs). It reconstructs correlation/causation/braid-trace lineage, actor lineage, governance-decision snapshots, approval chains, adapter-job lineage, and reversal chains (via `payload.original_entry_id`), each handled gracefully when absent. Strictly tenant-scoped — a mixed-tenant event array yields a pack containing zero foreign-tenant data. Rejects non-canonical `event_type` values so a command name is never treated as a business event, and excludes the reserved `finance.audit.event_appended` infrastructure event from normal evidence unless explicitly requested. No DB, no routes, no provider calls, no mutation of source records. `audit-evidence-layer.md` gained a §9 implementation section; the builder is `async` and awaits its event source, so it works with both the in-memory and Postgres event stores. Test coverage includes determinism, tenant isolation, full lineage reconstruction (approval / governance / braid / correlation / causation / reversal / adapter-job), infrastructure-event filtering, an async (Promise-returning) event-store input, and graceful handling of both missing and malformed lineage with no mutation of source events. 17 new tests pass, lint clean.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-12 — replay validation harness (`backend/lib/finance/projections/replayValidationHarness.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/replayValidationHarness.test.js` (NEW, 19 cases), `docs/architecture/finance/replay-validation.md` (NEW))**: Added a pure validation library that proves a projection rebuilt by full `replay()` converges to the same state as one built incrementally by sequential `dispatch()`. `runReplayValidation()` returns an aggregate `{ passed, checks }` report; each check (`checkConvergence`, `checkReplayOrdering`, `checkPerProjectionParity`, `checkRepeatedReplayDeterminism`, `checkInfrastructureEventFiltering`, `checkDegradedRecovery`, `checkTenantIsolation`) returns a structured `{ name, passed, detail }`. It validates dispatch-vs-replay convergence for ledger / approval_queue / adapter_queue, the frozen replay ordering (`created_at` ASC then `id` ASC, including the tie-break case), per-projection rebuild parity, repeated-replay determinism (replaying the same stream twice yields byte-identical state — `replay()` is a pure function of the event stream), infrastructure-event filtering (`finance.audit.event_appended` never reaches a business projection or advances its cursor — proven by rebuilding with vs. without the infra events), the degraded-recovery invariant (a degraded projection pauses dispatch and recovers only via operator-triggered replay), and per-(projection, tenant) isolation. Every collaborator (event store, store provider, workers, runner options) is injectable; defaults wire the real `projectionRunner`, memory store provider, and the three real projections. Includes a contract-faithful in-memory `createValidationEventStore()` that preserves caller-supplied `created_at`/`id` (the production store deliberately re-stamps `created_at`) so replay ordering can be asserted deterministically. No routes, no worker process, no provider writes, no network calls. 19 new tests pass (every check plus deliberately-failing paths — divergent stream, leaked cross-tenant row, non-deterministic replay); full projections suite green; lint clean.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-13 — worker service topology design (`docs/architecture/finance/worker-service-topology.md` (NEW))**: Design-only spec for the three Finance Ops background workers — `finance-projection-worker` (hosts the projection runner), `finance-adapter-worker` (the E2 job processor; optimistic-lock claim, back-off, dead-letter), and `finance-audit-worker` (`audit_timeline` upkeep and async evidence-pack generation). Restates scaffold decision E2 (separate Coolify worker services on VPS-2 — not in-process, not Supabase cron), defines each worker's responsibilities and source-event contract, the full environment-variable table with `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` and per-worker enable flags all defaulting to disabled, the disabled-by-default posture (code-merged ≠ service-running), the Coolify/VPS-2 deployment shape consistent with `DEPLOY_TOPOLOGY.md`, liveness/readiness health checks, and concurrency/idempotency references to existing contracts. No code, deployment files, or Coolify config; the adapter worker remains sandbox/draft-only with no provider writes.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-14 — staging-safe RLS validation (`docs/architecture/finance/staging-rls-validation.md` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/financePersistencePolicy.test.js` (NEW, 4 cases))**: Added a pre-staging verification checklist for finance migrations 172/173 covering PostgREST schema exclusion (the `finance` schema must stay out of Supabase's exposed-schemas list — finance is backend-mediated only), `service_role` RLS-bypass behavior verification, JWT tenant-claim confirmation (`auth.jwt() ->> 'tenant_id'` must be confirmed before RLS predicates hard-code it), the three-layer no-hard-delete posture, and the migration-gating checklist. Migrations 172 and 173 remain dev/local-only and `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` stays disabled until the checklist clears. Added `financePersistencePolicy.test.js`, a database-free regression guard asserting the in-memory finance event store's append-only posture — the interface exposes exactly `append`/`query`/`replay`/`getCount` (none of `update`/`delete`/`clear`/`remove`/`truncate`/`upsert`), appended events are `Object.isFrozen` and reject mutation, and `replay()` returns `created_at` ASC order. 4 new tests pass, lint clean.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-10 — minimal adapter-queue projection (`backend/lib/finance/projections/adapterQueueProjection.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/adapterQueueProjection.test.js` (NEW, 15 cases), `docs/architecture/finance/projection-contracts.md`)**: Added the operational bridge between finance events and the adapter-job lifecycle — a replayable read model of the outbound accounting-sync execution queue, built on the Phase 2B-7 Projection Runtime. It is explicitly **not** a scheduler, worker, retry engine, or provider client (`projection = observable state`, `worker = execution`, `event store = facts`). `createAdapterQueueProjectionWorker()` is a `ProjectionWorker` that consumes the three canonical adapter sync events — `finance.adapter.sync_queued`, `finance.adapter.sync_succeeded`, `finance.adapter.sync_failed` — and maintains a tenant-scoped queued/running/failed/completed queue in a memory `ProjectionStore`. The store is keyed by `adapter_job_id`, so there is structurally exactly one record per adapter job within a tenant-scoped projection — the invariant that one active queue item exists per `adapter_job_id` per tenant holds by construction. Every adapter event carries the full `payload.adapter_job` snapshot, so each event is self-describing and the handler is an unconditional upsert ("creates or updates"); `sync_queued` after `sync_failed` is the legitimate retry re-queue path. `handleEvent` / `replay` share one apply path (written immutably — a fresh record is always stored), so live dispatch and rebuild-from-zero produce identical state. `getProjection(tenantId, opts, store)` assembles `{ queued, running, failed, completed }`; each queue item carries `{ adapter_job_id, tenant_id, provider, aggregate_type, aggregate_id, operation, mode, status, attempts, error_message, created_at, updated_at, correlation_id, causation_id }` — `status` is derived from the event type and the bucket from `status`. Each bucket is ordered by `updated_at` (the latest status-transition time), so `failed` / `completed` read in the order jobs actually transitioned rather than original-creation order. `tenant_id` is sourced from the authoritative event-envelope tenant, never `payload.adapter_job.tenant_id`. The future-ready events `finance.adapter.sync_cancelled`, `finance.adapter.retry_scheduled`, and `finance.adapter.dead_lettered` are not yet in the canonical taxonomy, so they are not consumed — the runner ignores them (accepted, never crash or degrade). An adapter event missing `payload.adapter_job.id` throws — the runtime surfaces that as a degraded projection and pauses later dispatch. Verified against the runtime: sync*queued→queued / sync_succeeded→completed / sync_failed→failed, status transitions move the item between buckets and never leave it in two (incl. the failed→queued retry path), replay and event-by-event dispatch converge, a repeated replay never duplicates queue entries, a duplicate sync_queued keeps one active item, the read-model tenant comes from the envelope when a payload tenant disagrees, queue state is tenant-isolated, and infrastructure / non-consumed / not-yet-canonical events are ignored. Memory-store only — no DB persistence, no HTTP routes, no worker loops, no scheduling/retries/provider clients; the `running` bucket (no in-flight event canonical yet), the `finance.approval.approved` draft→queued rule, `totals`, `meta`, `as_of`, and query filters are deferred. Track B `projection-contracts.md` §7 gained a Phase 2B-10 implementation-status note, including the `payload.adapter_job` shape contract — a `sync*\*`emitter must emit the canonical`finance.adapter_jobs` record shape (`aggregate_type`/`aggregate_id`/`operation`/`mode`); reconciling that shape across the `simulateDealWon`draft object (which omitted`operation`/`mode`), the migration-172 table, and §7 is a known Phase-1 gap flagged for a separate pass. 180 finance unit + projection tests pass, lint clean.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-9 — minimal approval-queue projection (`backend/lib/finance/projections/approvalQueueProjection.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/approvalQueueProjection.test.js` (NEW, 14 cases), `docs/architecture/finance/projection-contracts.md`)**: Added the first projection consumer that tracks operational workflow state (human-in-the-loop approvals) rather than accounting math, built on the Phase 2B-7 Projection Runtime. `createApprovalQueueProjectionWorker()` is a `ProjectionWorker` that consumes the four approval lifecycle events — `finance.approval.requested`, `finance.approval.approved`, `finance.approval.rejected`, `finance.approval.cancelled` — and maintains a tenant-scoped pending/resolved queue in a memory `ProjectionStore`. The store is keyed by `approval_id`, so there is structurally exactly one record per approval within a tenant-scoped projection — the invariant that no two active pending records exist for one `approval_id` holds by construction. `handleEvent` / `replay` share one apply path (written immutably — a fetched record is never mutated), so live dispatch and rebuild-from-zero produce identical state; a resolution event moves its approval out of `pending` and into `resolved`. `finance.approval.requested` is **create-only** — a duplicate request (at-least-once delivery / replay) for an `approval_id` that already has a record, pending or resolved, is a no-op, so an already approved/rejected/cancelled approval is never reopened. The read-model `tenant_id` is sourced from the authoritative event-envelope tenant (the runtime store-partitioning boundary), never a stale `payload.approval.tenant_id`. `getProjection(tenantId, opts, store)` assembles `{ pending, resolved }` — pending entries carry `{ approval_id, tenant_id, target_type, target_id, risk_level, requested_by, created_at, approval_policy, escalation_target }`; resolved entries carry `{ approval_id, status, resolved_by, resolved_at, target_type, target_id }`. An approval event missing `payload.approval.id`, or a resolution event referencing an approval with no prior `finance.approval.requested`, throws — the runtime surfaces that as a degraded projection and pauses later dispatch. Verified against the runtime: requested→pending, each of approved/rejected/cancelled removes the pending entry and adds a resolved entry, replay and event-by-event dispatch converge, a repeated replay never duplicates queue entries, a duplicate `finance.approval.requested` never yields two pending records and never reopens a resolved approval, the read-model tenant comes from the envelope when a payload tenant disagrees, queue state is tenant-isolated, and infrastructure / non-consumed events are ignored. Memory-store only — no DB persistence, no HTTP routes, no worker loops; `finance.journal.reversal_requested`, `totals`, `meta`, `ai_initiated`, `age_seconds`, and query filters deferred. Track B `projection-contracts.md` §6 gained a Phase 2B-9 implementation-status note. 165 finance unit + projection tests pass, lint clean.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-8 — minimal ledger projection (`backend/lib/finance/projections/ledgerProjection.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/ledgerProjection.test.js` (NEW, 10 cases), `docs/architecture/finance/projection-contracts.md`)**: Added the first projection consumer built on the Phase 2B-7 Projection Runtime. `createLedgerProjectionWorker()` is a `ProjectionWorker` that consumes `finance.journal.posted` and maintains a tenant-scoped double-entry ledger in a memory `ProjectionStore` — `handleEvent` / `replay` accumulate each journal line into a per-account bucket (keyed by `account_id`, else `classification:account_name`), written immutably; `getProjection(tenantId, opts, store)` assembles `{ tenant_id, accounts, totals }` with accounts sorted by `account_name` and `balance_cents = debit_cents − credit_cents`. A `finance.journal.posted` event missing `payload.journal_entry.lines` throws, which the runtime surfaces as a degraded projection. Verified against the runtime: replay rebuilds an identical ledger, a repeated replay does not double balances, replay and event-by-event dispatch converge, infrastructure and non-consumed events are ignored, a malformed posting degrades the projection and pauses later dispatch, and ledger state is tenant-isolated. Memory-store only — no DB persistence, no HTTP routes; `finance.journal.reversed` and point-in-time queries deferred. Track B `projection-contracts.md` §3 gained a Phase 2B-8 implementation-status note. A parity test asserts the projection's replayed output equals `accountingEngine.buildLedger()` — the existing canonical ledger derivation — for the same posted journals (per-account debit/credit/balance buckets and totals across all five classifications), guarding against contract drift as Phase 2B expands. 151 finance unit + projection tests pass, lint clean.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-7 — Projection Runtime harness implementation (`backend/lib/finance/projections/projectionRunner.js` (NEW), `projectionStore.memory.js` (NEW), `projectionRuntimeErrors.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/projectionRunner.test.js` (NEW, 18 cases), `projectionStore.memory.test.js` (NEW, 10 cases), `backend/package.json`)**: Implemented the projection rebuild harness substrate from the Phase 2B-6 design (`projection-runtime.md`) — runtime only, no projections yet. `createProjectionRunner({ eventStore, storeProvider })` provides `register`, `dispatch(event)`, `replay(projectionName, tenantId)`, `replayAll(tenantId)`, and `status`. `createMemoryProjectionStoreProvider()` is the in-memory store: per-`(projection, tenant)` live stores, shadow-store creation, atomic promotion, and the projection-state persistence contract (`getState`/`setState`). The runner enforces the frozen runtime contract — events applied in `created_at ASC, id ASC` order; a `(created_at, id)` cursor per `(projection, tenant)` gives exactly-once delivery, with the runner owning cursor advancement (workers receive only the data store, never the cursor); a failed handler (after 3 retries) enters `degraded` state without advancing the cursor, and degraded state clears only via an operator-triggered `replay`; replay rebuilds into a shadow store and atomically promotes it, leaving the live store untouched on failure; `finance.audit.event_appended` is filtered from business projections and never advances their cursors. 28 new tests pass (registration, dispatch/cursor, degraded state, replay, deterministic ordering, infrastructure-event filtering, replay/dispatch convergence). `package.json` `test` + `test:coverage` extended to discover `__tests__/lib/finance/projections/*.test.js`. Deferred per scope: `getProjection`, Redis/Postgres stores, worker processes, polling loops, projection logic, HTTP routes.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-6 — Projection Runtime harness design (`docs/architecture/finance/projection-runtime.md` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/projection-contracts.md`)**: Added the authoritative runtime/harness contract for the Finance Ops projection layer — design only, no implementation. `projection-runtime.md` defines: the Projection Runner contract (`register`/`dispatch`/`replay`/`replayAll`/`getProjection`/`status`), the projection worker interface, the pluggable tenant-scoped `ProjectionStore` abstraction with shadow-store + atomic-promote replay isolation, event dispatch rules, two-layer event filtering, `(created_at, id)` cursor semantics for exactly-once delivery, idempotent per-event handler behaviour, frozen Track A replay ordering, the replay lifecycle (`idle`/`replaying`/`degraded`), tenant-scoped replay, degraded-projection state with **operator-triggered-only** recovery (no automatic replay), the eventual-consistency model, and infrastructure-event handling — `finance.audit.event_appended` is never dispatched to business projections and never advances a business-projection cursor, and `audit_timeline` consumes it only when `includeInfrastructureEvents=true`. Track B's `projection-contracts.md` §1 (Projection Worker Contract) and §2 (Consistency Model), which previously duplicated this runtime material, are replaced with authoritative pointers to `projection-runtime.md`; Track B now scopes to per-projection read-model definitions (§3–§10).
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B — persistent event store (`backend/lib/finance/financeEventStore.pg.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/financeEventStore.pg.test.js` (NEW, 20 cases), `backend/migrations/173_finance_event_store_append_only.sql` (NEW), `docs/architecture/finance/event-store-persistence.md` (NEW))**: Added a Postgres persistence adapter for the Finance Ops event store, behind the frozen Track A contract. `createFinancePgEventStore({ pool })` mirrors the in-memory `financeEventStore.js` interface (`append`, `query`, `replay`, `getCount`) and persists to `finance.audit_events` — the canonical Postgres-backed finance event stream, not merely an audit side table. `append` honors caller-supplied bare-UUID ids (generating one when absent), lets the DB assign `created_at` (`default now()` is the ordering source of truth), rejects non-`finance.*` and command-name `event_type` values, and returns the frozen inserted row; `replay`/`query` order by `created_at ASC, id ASC`. The adapter is insert-only — no update/delete/upsert path — and never deduplicates: `append` is a plain INSERT, so a duplicate event id is rejected by the `finance.audit_events` primary key and surfaced as `FINANCE_EVENT_STORE_DUPLICATE_EVENT_ID` for the domain layer to handle, never silently merged. Migration 173 (dev-only draft) hardens `finance.audit_events` with an append-only immutability trigger (blocks UPDATE/DELETE/TRUNCATE for any role, including `service_role`) and a `(tenant_id, created_at, id)` replay index. The in-memory store remains the default for tests/local fallback; the adapter is not wired into `financeDomainService`, adds no routes, and performs no provider writes. Also corrected stale `finance.events` / `finance_events` references (Track E `adapter-runtime-contract.md`, `audit-evidence-layer.md`, and two `backend/lib/finance` code comments) to `finance.audit_events` so the docs and code name one canonical event table. 20 new tests pass.
- **Prod compose files reconciled with live VPS-2 state (`prod/03-backend-heavy/docker-compose.yml`, `prod/04-app-fast/docker-compose.yml`)**: These two Coolify-native compose files existed on VPS-2 at `/opt/aishacrm-deploy/prod/` but were absent from git. Captured from the live server and committed verbatim. `03-backend-heavy` defines the backend service (mem_limit 3584m, port 4001, `aishacrm-backend` DNS alias, Doppler prd_prd, `MCP_NODE_HEALTH_URL=http://braid-mcp-server:8000/health`). `04-app-fast` defines the frontend (port 4000) and `aisha-comms` communications worker (mem_limit 768m). Both join the external `aishanet` network by name.
- **Finance Ops Gate 7B runtime surface (`backend/routes/finance.v2.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/finance.v2.routes.test.js`)**: Added `GET /api/v2/finance/runtime/status` for tenant-scoped mock runtime introspection and `POST /api/v2/finance/approvals/:id/approve` for human approval flow against the in-memory Finance Ops runtime. The runtime status endpoint reports `mock_read_only`, `in_memory`, and `provider_sync=disabled` state plus per-tenant counts. - **Finance Ops Phase 4 — PR #621 Codex re-review P2 + P3 #1 + P3 #2 follow-ups** (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-1-persistent-events-projection-reads-design.md`, `docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-production-pilot-design-freeze.md`, `docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-15-production-support-escalation-design.md`): Three residual contract-drift findings from the earlier P2 #1/#2/#3 fix wave on PR #621 (Codex re-review on `f2b9cbb3`). **P2 (Phase 4-1 §8 read-adapter contract drift)** — the `ProjectionBackedFinanceReadAdapter` bullet still said "a direct `audit_events` query path for journal entries (per §4)", contradicting the repaired §4 + §10 which require the new `journal_entries` projection snapshot for persistent-mode `GET /journal-entries`. An implementer reading §8 in isolation could have wired a direct event-store path and re-opened the exact bug Codex's first review fixed. **Fix:** §8 row rewritten to enumerate per-route adapter behavior — `runtime/status` composes `audit_events` count + `projection_state` cursor (the only legit `audit_events` read in the adapter); `/journal-entries` reads from the `journal_entries` projection (explicitly NOT a direct `audit_events` query filtered to posted/reversed); `/ledger` / `/profit-loss` / `/balance-sheet` from `ledgerProjection`. Explicit cross-reference back to the §4 P2 #2 fix so the implementation packet cannot land a direct-event-store path for journal entries. **P3 #1 (Phase 4-0 baseline-source row numbering drift)** — §4 "Phase 4 planning branch" row said "All Phase 4 planning packets (4-0 through 4-19) land on this branch", but §10's authoritative renumbered inventory has the planning sequence running 4-0 through 4-20 (4-20 = activation-decision gate) plus 4-21 (operator activation execution). **Fix:** row rewritten to say "All Phase 4 planning packets land on this branch — per the post-`3a036d10` P2 #1 renumbering in §10, the inventory runs 4-0 through 4-20 (4-20 is the activation-decision gate) plus 4-21 (operator activation execution under 4-20 GO). The earlier '4-0 through 4-19' wording referred to the pre-renumber 21-packet inventory and is superseded here." **P3 #2 (Phase 4-15 §8 hard-constraints row stale gate trace)** — Codex Gate F row said §3 + §6 + §7 are "Phase-4-19-traced" but the gate is now Phase 4-20. **Fix:** row updated to "Phase-4-20-traced (the activation-decision gate per the post-`3a036d10` Phase 4-0 §10 renumbering)."
