- **Finance Ops Phase 4 — PR #621 Codex P2 #1 + #2 + #3 fixes** (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-5-production-rollback-design.md`, `docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-1-persistent-events-projection-reads-design.md`, `docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-2-erpnext-credential-router-design.md`, `docs/architecture/finance/phase-4-production-pilot-design-freeze.md`): Three doc-only P2 findings on the Phase 4 planning baseline PR #621. **P2 #1 (Phase 4-5 rollback in-memory-write divergence, comment ID 3314712617)** — §4 row 4 (`ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` flag rollback) previously documented only the flag flip + backend restart, but left the route mounted in in-memory mode. The 6 mutating Finance v2 endpoints would still accept POSTs, and those writes would go to the process-local in-memory store instead of `audit_events` — silently lost on the next flip back to persistent mode. **Fix:** row 4 now requires pairing with lever #1 (`ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS=false`, full unmount) or lever #2 (`modulesettings.financeOps=false` for the pilot tenant, route returns 403) BEFORE or WITH the flag flip. Lever #3 (controlled-tenant allow-list) explicitly marked insufficient on its own because it doesn't block route mutations. §4 priority-order section gets a `Special case for lever #4` note pointing back at row 4's pairing rule. **P2 #2 (Phase 4-1 activation proof missing journal_entries projection, comment ID 3314712621)** — §7 dependency table required "all 4 projections" health + replay-determinism but the packet introduces a new `journal_entries` projection for persistent-mode `GET /journal-entries` (the P2 #2 fix from the prior cycle). Phase 4-20 could pass while the new projection was missing/stale/replay-broken. **Fix:** §7 rows updated to "all registered projections" with explicit enumeration of `ledger` / `approval_queue` / `adapter_queue` / `audit_timeline` / `journal_entries` (5 projections total); §1 baseline-source list updated; Phase 4-0 §11.2 row 2 also updated with the explicit registered-projection set + a "gate is NOT clear while the new journal_entries projection is missing or failing" rule. **P2 #3 (Phase 4-2 sandbox-pattern claim wrong, comment ID 3314712623)** — §6 routing rules table claimed `*.frappe.cloud` was a built-in sandbox pattern, but `BUILTIN_SANDBOX_HOST_PATTERNS` at `backend/lib/finance/accountingAdapters/erpnextSandboxAdapter.js:89-98` actually only matches: `localhost`/`127.0.0.1`/`0.0.0.0` exact, `.local`/`.lan`/`.internal` suffix, `sandbox.*` prefix, `*-sandbox.*` infix. A generic `customer.frappe.cloud` would NOT match. **Fix:** §6 row rewritten with the actual `BUILTIN_SANDBOX_HOST_PATTERNS` list verbatim + an explicit note that vendor sandboxes without a `sandbox.` or `-sandbox.` token must go in the env allow-list. No behavior change in any environment (doc-only); no migration applied; no provider writes; all 16 Phase 3-13 §7 safety guardrails preserved.

- **Finance Ops adapter_jobs operation CHECK enum + claim-query index — aligned migration 172 with runtime vocabulary (Claude bot PR #618 review blocker #2, issue comment 4559480112)** (`backend/migrations/172_finance_ops_runtime_scaffold.sql`): The `finance.adapter_jobs.operation` CHECK constraint at the migration's CREATE TABLE allowed only `('pull', 'push_draft', 'sync_status', 'void', 'reconcile')`, but `assertWritePermitted` at `backend/lib/finance/adapterJobProcessor.js:93-110` defines the runtime vocabulary as `pull_status` / `sync_status` / `reconcile` (read-only ops) + `push_draft` (permitted in every mode) + `push_final` and `void_record` (gated to non-draft modes by `assertWritePermitted` + further gated by `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED`). Three runtime operation values — `pull_status`, `push_final`, `void_record` — would have been rejected by the CHECK on INSERT/UPDATE in persistent mode. Same root cause class as the P1 column-drift fix: the migration drifted from the runtime contract. **Fix:** replaced the enum with the inclusive set `('pull', 'pull_status', 'push_draft', 'push_final', 'sync_status', 'void', 'void_record', 'reconcile')` — covers every runtime value plus retains the legacy `pull` and `void` labels so any pre-existing row stays accepted. Added an inline comment in the migration citing `adapterJobProcessor.js:93-110` so a future reader can verify the enum still matches `assertWritePermitted`. **Also added** `idx_finance_adapter_jobs_tenant_status_next_attempt` on `(tenant_id, status, next_attempt_at)` to match the `claimPersistent` query at `adapterJobProcessor.js:213-220` (`WHERE tenant_id = $1 AND status = 'queued' AND (next_attempt_at IS NULL OR next_attempt_at <= $2)`), making the queue-claim scan index-only. **No behavior change in any environment**: persistent path stays fail-closed at `finance.v2.js:48`; provider-writes stay default-closed; sandbox-only URL guard preserved. Finance backend tests still PASS after the change.

- **Finance Ops adapter_jobs schema/code drift — added missing columns to migration 172 (Codex PR #618 P1 finding, comment ID 3313804699)** (`backend/migrations/172_finance_ops_runtime_scaffold.sql`): The `finance.adapter_jobs` table created by migration 172 was missing three columns the persistent adapter worker code reads and writes — `attempts integer not null default 0` (incremented by `claimPersistent` at `backend/lib/finance/adapterJobProcessor.js:211` on each claim, written by `applyTerminalPersistent` at `:242`), `next_attempt_at timestamptz` (filter in `claimPersistent` at `:217` for retry backoff; written by `applyTerminalPersistent` at `:244`), and `payload jsonb not null default '{}'::jsonb` (consumed by the processor at `:309` via `buildProviderPayload(job.payload || {}, ...)` and at `:324` as the no-builder pass-through). Without these columns, the first `claimPersistent` poll against a Postgres-backed adapter queue would fail with `column "attempts" of relation "adapter_jobs" does not exist`, blocking any Postgres-mode lifecycle run. Bug was structurally unreachable in the current runtime — `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` fail-closed guard at `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:48` refuses to mount the route under the persistent path, so the broken SQL never executed in any environment — but it would have surfaced the first time Phase 4-1 (route lift design freeze) attempted the safe lift. Pre-existing on the runtime branch from before the renumber; PR #618's renumber commit `82d50292` only renamed the file 172 → 172 without modifying body. Three column adds, no rename, no drop: the existing `request_payload` / `response_payload` / `error_payload` JSONB columns (lines 156-158) are unused by any code path (verified by repo-wide grep) and left in place to keep the change additive and non-destructive. No code change required — the processor and worker already reference the column names being added. CI re-runs to verify. **No behavior change in any environment**: the persistent-events flag stays fail-closed; the kill switch at `adapterJobProcessor.js:332-345` keeps `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false`; sandbox-only ERPNext URL guard preserved. Finance backend tests 332/332 PASS; finance UI tests 98/98 PASS; lint clean.

- **Opportunity records with stage="Won"/"Lost" don't appear when filtered (4VD-63) (`backend/lib/opportunityStageNormalizer.js` (NEW), `backend/__tests__/lib/opportunityStageNormalizer.test.js` (NEW, 11 cases), `backend/routes/opportunities.v2.js`, `backend/routes/opportunities.js`, `src/components/opportunities/OpportunityForm.jsx`, `src/components/opportunities/__tests__/OpportunityForm.test.jsx` (+4 cases), `backend/migrations/172_canonicalize_opportunity_stages.sql` (NEW))**: Canonical opportunity stages per `backend/config/constants.js STATUS.OPPORTUNITY` are `prospecting | qualification | proposal | negotiation | closed_won | closed_lost`. The `OpportunityForm.jsx` stage Select dropdown was writing the legacy short forms `won` / `lost` directly to `opportunities.stage`, while every other touch point — `OpportunityStatsCards.jsx`, `OpportunityKanbanBoard.jsx`, `OpportunityDetailPanel.jsx`, `BulkActionsMenu.jsx`, the V1+V2 GET handlers and the stats aggregator — used the canonical `closed_won` / `closed_lost`. **Visible symptom**: clicking the "Closed Won" stat card produced a query for `stage='closed_won'` that excluded every row stored as `stage='won'` — the count in the card was non-zero (stats aggregator already normalises legacy values in JS at lines 287-288 / 902-903 of `opportunities.v2.js`) but the list returned empty. Exactly the screenshots on 4VD-63. **Fix is three-layered**: (1) **Read-side helper** `backend/lib/opportunityStageNormalizer.js` exports `expandStageFilter(stage)` returning the array of DB values to match (e.g. `'closed_won' → ['won','closed_won','closedwon']`) and `canonicalizeStage(stage)` returning the canonical write value. Pure, no DB, 11 unit tests cover the legacy↔canonical symmetry contract, casing/whitespace, forward-compat for new stages, and falsy-input safety. (2) **Route wire-in**: `opportunities.v2.js` count handler (line ~358), list handler (line ~519) and `opportunities.js` V1 list handler (line ~329) all switched from `.eq('stage', stage.toLowerCase())` to `.in('stage', expandStageFilter(stage))`. The V1 POST + PUT and V2 POST + PUT call `canonicalizeStage()` on the incoming `stage` field so no new row from any caller (form, AI, scripts) can re-introduce the legacy spelling. (3) **Form-side**: `OpportunityForm.jsx` Select options changed from `{ value: 'won' }` / `{ value: 'lost' }` to `{ value: 'closed_won' }` / `{ value: 'closed_lost' }` with the same display labels ("Won" / "Lost"), and the load-from-opportunity effect now coerces legacy `won`/`lost` to canonical on hydrate so editing a pre-migration row + clicking Save persists the canonical value (passive healing). (4) **Migration** `172_canonicalize_opportunity_stages.sql` is a pure UPDATE that converts every remaining `stage IN ('won','lost','closedwon','closedlost')` row to its canonical equivalent, wrapped in `BEGIN/COMMIT` with a pre-condition `RAISE NOTICE` of legacy counts and a post-condition assertion that zero legacy rows remain. Followed by `NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema'` per the CLAUDE.md migration runbook. Idempotent — re-running is a no-op. **Acceptance**: ✓ "Closed Won" stat card click returns matching legacy + canonical rows ✓ Filter URL `?stage=closed_won` and `?stage=won` return the same row set ✓ New opportunities created via the form persist `closed_won`/`closed_lost` ✓ Editing a legacy `stage='won'` row and saving heals the row to `closed_won` ✓ All 11 normalizer unit tests pass ✓ Migration converts legacy rows in one transaction and asserts cleanup completed. **Not in scope** (noted for follow-up since post-migration these become unreachable code paths): `src/components/agents/AgentChat.jsx` `$nin: ['closed_won','closed_lost']`, `src/components/dashboard/UserPerformanceCard.jsx` `stage: 'closed_won'`, `src/components/reports/ForecastingDashboard.jsx` legacy-only filters — all become non-issues once migration 172 runs because no legacy stage values remain.

### Fixed

- **Finance Ops Slice 2 — objectType vocabulary + canonical payload shape across producer/processor/adapter (code review P1 follow-up) (`backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js`, `backend/lib/finance/adapterJobProcessor.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/financeDomainService.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/adapterJobProcessor.test.js`)**: Codex re-review of `d671d816` (the prior P1+P2 fix) caught that the producer→consumer contract was internally inconsistent on **two more dimensions** the P1+P2 fix's capturing-fake-adapter test didn't catch: (1) **vocabulary mismatch** — processor passed `ctx.objectType = job.aggregate_type = 'journal_entry'` (Track A snake_case), but `createErpnextSandboxAdapter().pushDraft()` looks up `ERPNEXT_PROVIDER_OBJECT_MAP[objectType]` which is keyed by `'JournalEntry'` (PascalCase per the 2A adapter's frozen contract). Real adapter would throw `Unsupported objectType: journal_entry` at line 296 of `erpnextSandboxAdapter.js` before any write. (2) **payload-shape mismatch** — the prior fix stored `payload: { journal_entry: clone(draftEntry) }` (wrapped), but ERPNext's `fromCanonical(canonicalObject, objectType)` reads field names from `ERPNEXT_PROVIDER_OBJECT_MAP['JournalEntry'].fields` (`doc_number, txn_date, private_note, currency, lines`) at the **root** of the canonical object. Wrapping under `journal_entry` means `fromCanonical()` finds zero recognized keys → produces an empty body. Even storing the raw `draftEntry` (with `entry_number, created_at, memo`) at root would fail because those aren't the canonical field names — the canonical shape comes from `mapJournalEntryToQuickBooksCanonical` (provider-neutral despite the name; both QuickBooks and ERPNext consume it). **Fix:** `simulateDealWon` now stores `payload: mapJournalEntryToQuickBooksCanonical(draftEntry)` — the canonical fields at root. **`adapterJobProcessor.js` exports** `AGGREGATE_TYPE_TO_OBJECT_TYPE` (frozen `{ journal_entry: 'JournalEntry', account: 'Account' }`) + `aggregateTypeToObjectType(aggregateType)` helper. The processor calls the helper before invoking the adapter, throwing a permanent-classified config error (`code === 'FINANCE_ADAPTER_CONFIG_INVALID'`) if the mapping is missing. The outer per-job try/catch matches that code and classifies it as **permanent** (no retry) — config errors are deterministic; retrying with the same job and code state will fail the same way. **Tests added/updated:** (1) regression — `simulateDealWon adapter_job carries the CANONICAL journal entry shape` asserts `doc_number`, `txn_date`, `private_note`, `currency`, `lines` all at root, NO `journal_entry` wrapper key, currency upper-cased per the mapper, snapshot independence; (2) `aggregateTypeToObjectType maps Track A snake_case to provider PascalCase`; (3) `aggregateTypeToObjectType throws permanent-classified error for unknown aggregate_type`; (4) `runAdapterPollCycle: unknown aggregate_type → permanent failure (not retried)`; (5) the existing processor test that asserted `ctx.objectType === 'journal_entry'` updated to `=== 'JournalEntry'` with explanatory comment; (6) **`END-TO-END: simulateDealWon → approveFinanceAction → runAdapterPollCycle invokes the REAL ERPNext adapter`** — replaces the prior capturing-fake-adapter end-to-end test with one that registers the REAL `createErpnextSandboxAdapter` (with mocked `httpClient.post` only — no network IO) and asserts the full chain succeeds: processor maps `journal_entry → JournalEntry`, adapter accepts the objectType, `fromCanonical` maps the root-level canonical fields to ERPNext fields, `httpClient.post` receives a valid body with `doctype: 'Journal Entry'`, `docstatus: 0`, `posting_date` (mapped from `txn_date`), `accounts` array (mapped from `lines`). If either the vocabulary or the payload-shape fix is missing, this test fails — that's the test the prior end-to-end was missing. Test counts: **45/45 in 2B test files** (was 38, +7 new); full finance regression **385/385** (was 382, +3 new). `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged. `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged. No migration. No staging/Coolify/Doppler mutation. Production untouched.
- **Finance Ops Slice 2 — producer→consumer payload wiring + worker ERPNext adapter registration (code review P1 + P2) (`backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js`, `backend/workers/financeAdapterWorker.js`, `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.staging.example.yml`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/financeDomainService.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/adapterJobProcessor.test.js`)**: Codex per-packet review of `27ae09fc` (2A), `e66538f0` (2B), `95f65144` (2C) returned 2 real findings. **P1 on Slice 2B — `simulateDealWon()` adapter_job had no canonical payload snapshot**: the in-memory adapter_job created at `financeDomainService.js:471-483` did NOT include a `payload` field, but the Slice 2B processor at `adapterJobProcessor.js:304-324` reads `job.payload || {}` and forwards it via `buildProviderPayload` to the adapter. So the first sandbox-enabled push would have collapsed to an empty body. The Slice 2B tests didn't catch this because they fabricated queued jobs with `payload: { foo: 'bar' }` directly, bypassing the simulateDealWon producer. **Fix:** simulateDealWon now writes `payload: { journal_entry: clone(draftEntry) }` on the draft adapter_job — a deep-cloned snapshot of the canonical journal entry taken at create time. The snapshot is what the processor will hand to `buildProviderPayload` (2A's E6 boundary) and ultimately to the ERPNext adapter's `pushDraft`. New regression test `financeDomainService simulateDealWon adapter_job carries a payload snapshot of the draft journal entry (P1 fix)` verifies the payload exists, contains the journal_entry, references the same id, and that the snapshot is deep-cloned (mutating the snapshot does not affect the bucket). New end-to-end integration test `END-TO-END: simulateDealWon → approveFinanceAction → runAdapterPollCycle feeds canonical journal_entry to the adapter (review P1 fix)` drives the full producer → consumer chain against a real `createFinanceDomainService`, real `buildProviderPayload`, and a capturing fake adapter; asserts the adapter receives `received.canonical.journal_entry` and that internal-metadata stripping happened (no `braid_trace_id`, no `governance_policy_snapshot` in the forwarded canonical). **P2 cross-packet — worker entry block had no ERPNext registration**: `financeAdapterWorker.js:461-468` booted with `const adapters = new Map()` and no provider registration logic, so even with the worker enabled the processor would skip every job as "no adapter registered for provider 'erpnext'". The integration claim "2A + 2B + 2C compose into an executable adapter runtime" wasn't actually executable. **Fix:** the worker entry block now reads `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_BASE_URL` + `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_API_KEY` + `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_API_SECRET` + `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_SANDBOX_BASE_URLS` from env. When all three required credentials are present, it lazy-imports `createErpnextSandboxAdapter` (Slice 2A) and registers the instance under the `'erpnext'` provider slot; when any are unset (which is the default state of the staging YAML), the worker boots with an empty registry and logs "erpnext credentials not configured — provider not registered (worker will skip erpnext jobs)". Constructor errors (production-looking base URLs, missing required params) are caught and logged; the worker continues booting with an empty registry rather than crashing. Staging YAML at `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.staging.example.yml` updated with the three new credential env vars (all defaulting to empty — `${FINANCE_ERPNEXT_BASE_URL:-}` etc.) + the existing `FINANCE_ERPNEXT_SANDBOX_BASE_URLS` env (which was referenced in a comment but not declared as an actual env line). Per-tenant credential loading from `tenant_integrations` is explicitly out of scope for Slice 2 and tracked as a future packet — for Slice 2 the worker registers a single ERPNext adapter instance from env, and Phase 3-10 §6's draft-write proof runs against that one sandbox configuration. **Hard constraints preserved:** no production credentials in defaults; default sandbox allowlist empty; `FINANCE_PROVIDER_WRITES_ENABLED=false` remains the dominant kill switch (registration alone does not enable writes — the processor still skips the HTTP call when this is false); `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` / `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged; no staging/Coolify/Doppler mutation; no migration; no production action. Total **38/38 in 2B test files (was 36 pre-fix, +2 new); full finance regression 382/382 (was 380, +2 new tests).**
- **Finance Ops Slice 2-0 — one more stale producer-attribution sentence at §4.7 line 360 test-obligation note (code review P3 re-review) (`docs/architecture/finance/slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md`)**: Codex re-review of commit `4fcd2f72` (the prior 5-location reconciliation) caught one remaining stale producer-attribution sentence the grep-whole-doc sweep had missed. §4.7's idempotency / test-obligation paragraph at line 360 said "Slice 2B and Slice 2D add producer-side tests that emit each of the three events from the actual job processor and verify the projection consumes them correctly end-to-end." After the §4.1 / §4.7 producer split, this is no longer accurate: the processor (`runAdapterPollCycle`) only emits `sync_succeeded` / `sync_failed`; `sync_queued` is emitted by the `approveFinanceAction()` promoter (`promoteLinkedAdapterJobs`), not the processor. The previous `4fcd2f72` sweep grepped for `simulateDealWon`, `emits sync`, `produces.*sync`, `produces.*queued`, `emit.*queued`, `sync_queued` — but missed this sentence because its stale phrasing was "the actual job processor" without naming the event types adjacent to the producer claim. **Fix:** rewrote the test-obligation sentence to explicitly cite the corrected producer split: "`sync_succeeded` and `sync_failed` are emitted by the job processor (`runAdapterPollCycle`); `sync_queued` is emitted by the `approveFinanceAction()` promoter (`promoteLinkedAdapterJobs`), NOT by the processor. The end-to-end integration assertion is that all three events — regardless of producer — are observed correctly by the `adapter_queue` projection (the consumer doesn't care which producer emitted them; the envelope contract is uniform per §4.7)." Also verified the adjacent §4.7 idempotency note at line 358 ("double-emitting `sync_succeeded` for a job that already reached terminal state") — accurate as-is because `sync_succeeded` IS emitted by the processor. **Process-lesson sharpening:** the grep pattern needs to include phrasings that don't co-locate event names with producer claims — added the lesson that producer-attribution sweeps should also grep for `job processor`, `processor emit`, `actual job processor`, `producer-side test`, and other phrasings that reference the producer without naming the specific event. - **Finance Ops Slice 2-0 — stale producer attribution in 5 places after the §4.1/§5.2 lifecycle correction (code review P3) (`docs/architecture/finance/slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md`)**: Codex re-review of commit `0e246ff1` (the P1+P2 lifecycle fix) caught one §5.4 Slice 2D test obligation that still claimed `simulateDealWon` produces a `finance.adapter.sync_queued` event observable by the `adapter_queue` projection. After the §4.1/§5.2 correction that is no longer true: `simulateDealWon` inserts the adapter_job in `status='draft'` with no event, and `sync_queued` is emitted only when `approveFinanceAction()`'s promoter transitions linked jobs `draft → queued`. Applying the Phase 3-8 grep-whole-doc lesson found four additional stale references the original P1+P2 fix had missed: (1) §2 capability summary line 30 said "the adapter job processor… emits canonical `finance.adapter.sync_queued / sync_succeeded / sync_failed` events" — the processor only emits the latter two, the promoter emits `sync_queued`; (2) §3 prerequisite line 74 said "Slice 2's job processor emits the events that projection has been waiting for" — same conflation; (3) §4.7 producer lead-in line 311 still said "Slice 2B's adapter-job creation path (`finance.adapter.sync_queued` — also emitted by the domain service's existing `simulateDealWon` and future job-create endpoints)" — directly contradicting the §4.7 detail block at lines 319/330 that the same P1+P2 fix had corrected; (4) §4.9 verification item 1 line 391 attributed `sync_queued` emission to "the new job processor" — should be the promoter; (5) §4.10 end-to-end ASCII flow block lines 411-428 ran `simulateDealWon → INSERT → sync_queued event → adapter_queue projection` with no approval step at all, also routing the flow straight to the worker poll without the promoter intermediate. **Fix — all 5 stale references reconciled to the corrected §4.1/§5.2 contract**: (a) §2 line 30 now lists only `sync_succeeded / sync_failed` for the processor and adds an explicit "The companion `sync_queued` event is emitted upstream by the `approveFinanceAction()` promoter (see §4.1, §4.7), not by the processor" clause. (b) §3 line 74 now splits producer attribution between the promoter (`sync_queued`) and the processor (`sync_succeeded / sync_failed`). (c) §4.7 lead-in line 311 now reads "Slice 2B's adapter job processor (`finance.adapter.sync_succeeded / sync_failed`) and Slice 2B's `approveFinanceAction()` promoter modification (`finance.adapter.sync_queued`, emitted at the `draft → queued` transition per §4.1). `simulateDealWon` (and any future adapter-job-creation path that targets approval-required journals) inserts the row in `status='draft'` and does NOT emit `sync_queued`; the event is exclusively the promoter's responsibility." — internally consistent with §4.7 detail lines 319/330. (d) §4.9 line 391 now explicitly cites the promoter as the producer with cross-references to §4.1 + §4.7. (e) §4.10 end-to-end ASCII flow rewritten to insert an "Approver calls POST `/api/v2/finance/approvals/:id/approve` → `approveFinanceAction()` → `adapterJobPromoter` → atomic UPDATE `draft → queued` → emit one `sync_queued` per promoted job → adapter_queue projection consumes → 'queued' bucket" block between the `simulateDealWon` step (which now creates `status='draft'` with no event and a pending approval row) and the adapter worker poll step. Also explicitly preserves the Phase 3-8 §5.7 contract ("journal stays at `pending_approval`; journal posting is NOT a Slice 2 deliverable"). (f) §5.4 Slice 2D Codex-flagged bullet rewritten and expanded into two bullets: bullet 1 — `simulateDealWon` inserts draft row + emits NO `sync_queued`; adapter_queue projection has no observable change; bullet 2 — `approveFinanceAction()` against the linked approval promotes `draft → queued` + emits one `sync_queued`; adapter_queue projection then surfaces the job in `queued` within one runner dispatch cycle. Replay parity bullet expanded to note the absence of `sync_queued` for draft-but-never-approved jobs (the row exists in the table but contributes no event). The doc is now internally consistent across every place that attributes producers; the Slice 2A/2B/2C parallel-safety claim still holds because every producer-chain mention agrees on `approveFinanceAction()` as the `sync_queued` producer. Process lesson re-banked: the Phase 3-8 "stale-row-after-fix" pattern (grep whole doc + re-read summary tables on every contract correction) bit again because the original P1+P2 fix at `0e246ff1` only updated §4.1, §4.7 detail, and §5.2 without sweeping for downstream producer-attribution claims. Doc-only — no code change shipped, no migration, no env var change. `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged. `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged. Production out of scope.
- **Finance Ops Slice 2-0 — lifecycle correction + Q5 resolution (code review P1 + P2) (`docs/architecture/finance/slice-2-adapter-runtime-design.md`)**: Codex review of `f94f7712` + `436e8919` caught a real architectural error in the Slice 2 design. **P1 — adapter-job lifecycle missed the `draft` pre-approval state**: the actual `finance.adapter_jobs.status` enum in migration 172 + `simulateDealWon` (`backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js:471-483`) + projection-contracts.md §7 all use `draft` as the canonical pre-approval state, with a `draft → queued` transition triggered by approval. My §4.1 cited `adapter-runtime-contract.md` §3's lifecycle (`queued | running | succeeded | failed | cancelled`) which is the runtime-side view starting at `queued` — but the DB state includes `draft` before that. Slice 2B's `adapterJobEnqueuer` as I designed it would have inserted rows directly in `queued`, making them claimable by the worker **before** the approval gate — a material finance-semantic change that conflicted with the doc's own "no new finance domain semantics" claim. **P2 — internal inconsistency**: §4.1 lifecycle excluded `draft` while §5.2 froze 2B to bypass it; Q5 in §9 deferred "should `approveFinanceAction` create adapter jobs" while §5.2 had already frozen the queueing-bypass behavior. Until the queueing-point decision was resolved, 2B's contract and 2D's integration expectations were not actually parallel-safe. **Fix — substantive design correction**: (1) §4.1 now includes `draft` in the full DB lifecycle with an explicit state diagram and documents the `draft → queued` transition trigger — the trigger is `approveFinanceAction()` calling a new `promoteLinkedAdapterJobs()` helper for any adapter_jobs sharing the approval's `aggregate_id`. (2) The Phase 3-8 §5.7 contract ("approval doesn't auto-post the journal") is explicitly preserved — only the adapter_job transitions, the journal stays at `pending_approval`. (3) §4.7 `sync_queued` event emission clarified: emitted at the `draft → queued` transition (NOT at row INSERT in `draft`); producer is the new `approveFinanceAction` modification, not `simulateDealWon`. (4) §5.2 Slice 2B scope expanded to include the new `adapterJobPromoter.js` helper AND the `approveFinanceAction()` modification; the enqueuer now inserts `status='draft'` with no `sync_queued` emission. New test obligations added for the enqueuer (inserts `draft`, no event), promoter (finds linked jobs by `aggregate_id`, atomically promotes, emits `sync_queued` per promotion), and the modified `approveFinanceAction` (calls promoter, journal status unchanged). (5) §9 Q5 marked **RESOLVED YES** — `approveFinanceAction` modification is part of Slice 2B's frozen scope; explicit scope note clarifies "adapter-job `draft → queued` promotion only, NOT journal `pending_approval → posted`". The Slice 2A/2B/2C parallel-safe claim now holds correctly — 2B's `approveFinanceAction` modification doesn't touch the adapter (2A) or worker shell (2C). Doc-only — no code change shipped, no migration, no env var change. `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged. `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged. Production out of scope.

- **Finance Ops Phase 3-8 — Approval-to-posting path correction + response-shape alignment (code review P2 + P3) (`docs/architecture/finance/staging-smoke-test-results.md`)**: Codex review of commit `213c845d` returned two findings, both substantive. **P2 — checks #7 → #9 assumed an approval-to-posting auto-execution path that the current runtime does NOT implement**: `approveFinanceAction()` at `backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js:596-644` only mutates the approval row (`status`, `approved_by`, `approved_at`) and appends a `finance.approval.approved` event; it does **not** transition the target journal from `pending_approval` to `posted`. `reverseJournalEntry()` requires `original.status === 'posted'` at `backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js:523-526` (throws 409 otherwise). So the #7 → #9 chain my doc described is not a valid smoke path — the simulate-deal-won journal stays at `pending_approval` forever under HTTP-only operator actions, and the reverse endpoint rejects it. The route tests at `backend/__tests__/routes/finance.v2.routes.test.js:101-123` exercise the reverse-success path by calling `service.seedJournalEntry({ ..., status: 'posted' })` directly on the service handle — there is no HTTP equivalent. **Rewrote §5.9** to split into §5.9.a (HTTP-testable 409 rejection path for reversing a non-posted journal, with reject-is-pass framing) and §5.9.b (the success path, explicitly DEFERRED with four remediation paths documented: admin debug endpoint, auto-posting service change, docker-exec workaround, or wait for Slice 2). Updated §5.7 with an "Important — what `approveFinanceAction()` does NOT do" block explaining the contract and pointing at the seed-based test path. Updated §6 pass criteria and §7 stop conditions to match the §5.9 split. Updated §10 evidence pack to pre-mark §5.9.b as DEFERRED with reason. **P3 — multiple response-shape and sample-payload errors**: verified against the actual service / route code: (a) `GET /runtime/status` returns `data.runtime.{mode, persistence, provider_sync, governance}` nested under `data.runtime.*`, NOT top-level `data.mode` / `data.persistence` (per `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:105-123`); (b) `GET /ledger` returns `{ accounts, totals: { debit_cents, credit_cents } }` per `buildLedger()` at `backend/lib/finance/accountingEngine.js:97-120` — NO `tenant_id`, NO five-classification totals (my prior claim was confused with a different endpoint), and `accounts` is always empty under 3-8 conditions because `buildLedger` only includes `posted` entries and nothing reaches `posted` via HTTP; (c) draft-invoice curl payload used `lines` but the service stores `payload.line_items` at `backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js:207` — a `lines` field would be silently dropped; (d) draft-invoice response is `{ invoice, governance_decision, approval_required }` per `:231-235`, NOT `{ invoice, command, decision, event }`; (e) simulate-deal-won response is `{ journal_entry, approval, adapter_job, governance_decision, approval_required }` per `:501-507`, NOT including an `events` field; (f) approve response is `{ approval, governance_decision }` per `:641-644`, NOT including an `event` field; (g) reverse response is `{ original_entry_id, reversal_entry, approval, governance_decision, approval_required }` per `:587-593`, the journal field is `reversal_entry` NOT `journal_entry`; (h) error response shape is `{ status: 'error', message, [governance_decision] }` per `sendError()` at `backend/routes/finance.v2.js:26-33` (which spreads `governance_decision` from `error.decision` when present). Updated §5.1, §5.2, §5.3, §5.6, §5.7, §5.8, §5.9.b to align every expected-response shape and sample-payload field with the verified code references. Doc-only — no code change, no migration, no env var change. `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged. `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged. Production out of scope.

- **Finance Ops Phase 3-6 — Malformed markdown table row from unescaped pipes inside backticked status enum (code review P3) (`docs/architecture/finance/staging-replay-drill-results.md`)**: Codex review of commit `66588e72` caught a markdown rendering bug in the §10 hard-constraints table. The "Only valid `finance.projection_state.status` values are used" row referenced the enum as `` `idle | replaying | degraded` `` with literal pipes inside backticks. Backticks don't protect pipes from being interpreted as table column separators in strict CommonMark, so when Prettier reformatted the table it split that single cell into 5 cells — the row stopped rendering as a 3-column table and the constraint became hard to read in exactly the section meant to be the concise source-of-truth recap. Fix: replaced the literal pipes with escaped pipes (`\|`) so the cell stays one column under Prettier's reflow: `` `idle \| replaying \| degraded` ``. The narrative-prose mentions of the enum elsewhere in the doc (outside tables) are unaffected — pipes in prose don't cause column splits. Doc-only — no worker code change, no migration applied, no env var changed. `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged. `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged. Production out of scope.
- **Finance Ops Phase 3-5 — Two implementation-fact errors in projection_state expectations (code review P2 + P3) (`docs/architecture/finance/staging-worker-activation-log.md`)**: Codex's review of commit `93e16da8` found two doc claims that didn't match the runtime contract. **P2 — empty-stream `finance.projection_state` claim was wrong**: §6.3 claimed "the runner does write an initial first-build cursor row per `(projection, tenant)` the first time it dispatches against an empty stream, so a small number of `finance.projection_state` rows may appear with `cursor_event_id: null`." That's not what the code does. `runProjectionPollCycle()` at `backend/workers/financeProjectionWorker.js:112-171` only iterates events returned by `eventStore.replay()`; with an empty stream the inner `for (const event of events)` body never executes, so `runner.dispatch()` is never called. The runner only persists projection-state rows inside `dispatch()` and `replay()`; there is no empty-stream bootstrap write. §8.5 carried the same error ("the empty-stream first-build wrote any cursor rows"). Updated §6.3 to state explicitly that zero rows are written during 3-5 steady state and rows will only start appearing once events flow (i.e., after Slice 2). Updated §8.5 pass condition to "zero rows is the expected result" with the runtime contract reference. **P3 — `status: 'ok'` is not a valid `finance.projection_state.status` value**: the runtime contract is `idle | replaying | degraded` per `projection-runtime.md` §3; `projectionStore.pg.js:256` persists `state.state ?? 'idle'` (steady state is `idle`). My doc claimed `status: 'ok'`, which doesn't exist. Updated §8.5 to expect `status = 'idle'` for any rows that do exist; `status = 'degraded'` remains the fail signal; added explicit fail for `status = 'replaying'` outside an operator-triggered replay (the worker does not call `runner.replay()`, so `replaying` should never appear in 3-5 steady state). Doc-only — no worker code change, no migration applied, no env var changed. `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged. `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged. Production out of scope.
- **Finance Ops Phase 3-4 — Stale "never opens a DB connection" wording in two YAML comment blocks (code review P3 re-review) (`deploy/coolify/finance-workers.staging.example.yml`)**: Codex re-review of commit `7b9d6f33` found the inline DB-connection comment fix was incomplete — the YAML still had stale "never opens a DB connection" wording in two other comment blocks I missed: the top disabled-by-default summary near the header, and the three-tier enable-gate comment above `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` / `ENABLE_FINANCE_WORKERS` / `ENABLE_FINANCE_PROJECTION_WORKER`. Reconciled both comment blocks to match the accurate inline-comment wording from `7b9d6f33`: the header block now walks the actual boot sequence (boot → pg.Pool construction → disabled gate → idle stub, no pool.query) and notes that `FINANCE_DB_URL` is still required at startup; the three-tier-gate comment now reads "the worker logs `disabled — idling` and returns an idle stub. The pg.Pool object is constructed by the entry block before this gate runs, but no pool.query() is ever called in the disabled state, so no actual TCP connection to Supabase is opened" with a cross-reference to the DB-connection comment. The YAML is now internally consistent across all three places that touch this language. - **Finance Ops Phase 3-4 — Disabled-worker DB-config requirement + self-contradictory §6.2 outcome wording (code review P2 + P3) (`docs/architecture/finance/staging-worker-deployment-log.md`, `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.staging.example.yml`)**: Codex's review of commit `7e769389` found two issues. **P2 — DB requirement documented incorrectly**: the doc/YAML claimed `FINANCE_DB_URL` was "required only when enabled" and that the disabled worker "never opens a DB connection". The standalone entry block at `backend/workers/financeProjectionWorker.js:378-383` resolves `FINANCE_DB_URL || DATABASE_URL` and exits the process unconditionally if neither is set — **before** the disabled gate at `startFinanceProjectionWorker()` line 257 ever runs. So a disabled-by-default Coolify deploy still needs the DB connection string in Doppler `stg_stg` just to boot and log `disabled — idling`. Updated four locations: §6.1 preflight checklist now says Doppler `stg_stg` carries the secrets the worker needs **to boot at all** with the explicit line-number reference; §6.2 outcome paragraph now walks the 5-step boot sequence ending in "no `pool.query()` is ever called, so although the `pg.Pool` object exists, no actual TCP connection to Supabase is opened" — distinguishing "DB env required at startup" (TRUE) from "actual DB connection opened" (FALSE in the disabled state, because `pg.Pool` construction is lazy); §6.3 disabled-and-idling confirmation now precisely says "no actual DB connection is opened" with the pool-construction-lazy mechanism documented; §7 env var table `FINANCE_DB_URL` row now reads "required at process startup". The YAML's DB-connection inline comment now reads "REQUIRED AT PROCESS STARTUP" and explains the entry-block exit / pool-laziness mechanism. **P3 — self-contradictory §6.2 outcome wording**: §6.2 said the expected outcome was "running, healthy, idle" but the same paragraph then explained the disabled path writes no heartbeat → heartbeat-file healthcheck fails. §8.2 correctly said `unhealthy` is acceptable for disabled. Reconciled §6.2 outcome to **"running, unhealthy, idle (acceptable while disabled)"** with explicit "Healthcheck status: unhealthy is expected and acceptable in the disabled state" framing — operators differentiate "disabled and idling correctly" from "enabled and stuck" via log + env signals (the `[finance-projection-worker] disabled — idling` log line plus `ENABLE_FINANCE_PROJECTION_WORKER` unset). The follow-up to emit a one-time `writeWorkerHeartbeat({ status: 'disabled' })` on the idle return path would let the outcome wording move to "running, healthy, idle" — tracked as a follow-up, not a 3-4 blocker. Doc + YAML comment only — no migration applied, no code change to the worker, no environment variable change. `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS` unchanged. `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` unchanged. Production out of scope.
- **Finance Ops Phase 3-3 — §4.5 timing-bucket misclassification + dead forward link to non-existent smoke-test doc (code review P2 + P3) (`docs/architecture/finance/staging-rls-verification-results.md`)**: Codex's review of commit `e1bf362c` found two issues. **P2 — §4.5 timing mismatch**: the §3 timing table and summary text classified §4.5 ("no direct public finance table access") as pre-migration / runnable immediately, but §4.5's own Prerequisite row in §4.5 requires migrations 172 and 175 applied to staging and depends on §4.1.c (which is post-migration). - **Finance Ops Phase 3-1 — two contract-accuracy fixes from code review (`docs/architecture/finance/phase-3-staging-activation-plan.md`)**: Review of the Phase 3-1 baseline doc found two P2 contract-accuracy issues. **P2 #1 — `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` scope misstated**: §7's "Two flags, two scopes" table said the flag is read by "`routes/finance.v2.js`, finance worker" and that the worker "reads the flag but does nothing with it until Slice 2 wires reads". The worker code (`backend/workers/financeProjectionWorker.js`) does not read the flag at all — `buildProjectionRunner` (line 185) unconditionally constructs the runner with `createFinancePgEventStore({ pool })`, and the only env gates the worker reads are `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS`, `ENABLE_FINANCE_WORKERS`, `ENABLE_FINANCE_PROJECTION_WORKER` (the three-tier gate at `isFinanceProjectionWorkerEnabled`) and `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS`. Corrected the table to scope the flag to `routes/finance.v2.js` only, and added a "Why the worker doesn't read this flag" note explaining the practical Phase 3 consequence (with `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS=false` the backend route does not write to `finance.audit_events`, so the worker's polls find empty streams and are no-ops — the expected idle Phase 3 worker behavior). **P2 #2 — worker placement contradicted DEPLOY_TOPOLOGY.md**: §5.3 said "Worker placement (per decision E2 in `worker-service-topology.md`) is VPS-2", but the same doc named [`DEPLOY_TOPOLOGY.md`](docs/architecture/DEPLOY_TOPOLOGY.md) as the source of truth in §5, and topology says app services (including background workers) deploy to **VPS-1 (staging) or Hetzner (production), never VPS-2** — VPS-2 hosts only the control plane (Coolify, Cal.com, Uptime Kuma, Gitea, OneDev). This is the same unresolved tension already carried in `finance-worker-deployment-config.md` §8 (which references E2 but flags "the actual VPS-1-vs-VPS-2 placement must be re-confirmed against DEPLOY_TOPOLOGY.md"); leaving it in the baseline doc would have made Phase 3-4 deploy planning ambiguous. Resolved by stating Phase 3 worker placement is **VPS-1 (staging)** per `DEPLOY_TOPOLOGY.md` (the named source of truth wins), and recording that a follow-up edit to reconcile `finance-worker-deployment-config.md` §8 and `worker-service-topology.md` decision E2 to the VPS-1-staging / Hetzner-production placement is outstanding (deferred — neither is in the Phase 3-1 baseline scope, and Phase 3-4 operates from this doc).
- **Finance Ops Phase 3 Slice 1 — split-brain prevention on the persistent-events path + operator-doc correction (code review P1 + P2) (`backend/routes/finance.v2.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/finance.v2.routes.test.js`, `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.example.yml`)**: Task 7 of Slice 1 wired the Postgres event store into the finance v2 routes behind `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS=true`, but the domain service still maintains an in-memory per-process bucket of journal entries / invoices / approvals / adapter jobs, and every business read (`listJournalEntries`, `listApprovals`, `getLedger`, `getProfitLoss`, `getBalanceSheet`) reads from that bucket — not the event stream. Only `listAuditEvents` reads from the event store. Setting the flag would have routed writes to Postgres while business reads continued to see only the current process's in-memory snapshot — after a restart, business reads return empty alongside a non-zero `audit_events` count, and two backend instances see divergent views. **P1 fix:** `createFinanceV2Routes` now refuses to mount when `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS=true` — it throws a descriptive `Error` at construction time, which propagates up through the unguarded `app.use` call in `server.js` and fails backend startup loud. The `ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS=true` gate already wraps the whole block, so the throw only fires in the genuinely dangerous case (`ENABLE_FINANCE_OPS=true && ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS=true`). Lifting this guard is gated on projection-backed reads landing in Slice 2. The unused `createFinancePgEventStore` import is removed; `opts.eventStore` / `opts.service` test injection still works. **P2 transitive fix:** `/runtime/status` continues to report `persistence: 'in_memory'` — this is now invariantly accurate because the persistent branch is structurally unreachable. **P2 operator-doc fix:** `deploy/coolify/finance-workers.example.yml` previously documented `FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS=` as "leave empty for 'all'", but `parseControlledTenantIds()` in `backend/workers/financeProjectionWorker.js` returns `[]` for empty/unset and the standalone entry block explicitly warns _"enabled but no FINANCE_CONTROLLED_TENANT_IDS configured — poll cycles will be no-ops"_. The YAML comment now states the correct semantics: empty means NO tenants are processed; tenants must be explicitly listed; there is no implicit "process all" fall-through. The comment on `ENABLE_FINANCE_PERSISTENT_EVENTS` in the same file is updated to record that, as of Slice 1, the backend refuses to mount the route when this flag is true. Tests: the previous `selects pg` / `falls back` tests are replaced with two `refuses to mount` tests (with and without pool). 278/278 finance + projection + worker + route tests pass; lint clean.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-11 — audit/evidence builder now supports an async event store (code review P1) (`backend/lib/finance/auditEvidenceBuilder.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/auditEvidenceBuilder.test.js`, `docs/architecture/finance/audit-evidence-layer.md`)**: `resolveEvents` returned `source.replay(tenantId)` / `source.query(...)` directly and the result was immediately `.filter()`-ed. That works for the synchronous in-memory `financeEventStore.js`, but the Postgres adapter `financeEventStore.pg.js` has `async` `replay`/`query` — passing it yielded a `Promise`, and `Promise.filter` is not a function. The module's JSDoc advertised accepting "a finance event store", and `audit-evidence-layer.md` §7 already declared `async` signatures, so the implementation contradicted both. `resolveEvents`, `queryAuditTimeline`, `getReversalChain`, `buildReversalLineage`, and `buildEvidencePack` are now `async` and `await` the event source — working unchanged against both the sync in-memory store and the async Postgres adapter (an `await` on a non-Promise is a no-op). A new test drives a Promise-returning store and asserts the pack matches an array-built pack byte-for-byte (same `pack_hash`). Doc §9.1/§9.5 corrected from "synchronous" to the async contract. 16 audit-evidence tests pass, lint clean.
- **Finance Ops Phase 2B-12 — replay validation harness tenant-isolation proof strengthened (code review P2) (`backend/lib/finance/projections/replayValidationHarness.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/replayValidationHarness.test.js`, `docs/architecture/finance/replay-validation.md`)**: `checkTenantIsolation` detected cross-tenant leakage only via `value.tenant_id === otherTenantId`. Ledger account buckets (`{ account_id, account_name, classification, debit_cents, credit_cents }`) carry no `tenant_id` field, so a bug merging cross-tenant amounts into a shared ledger bucket would pass the scan — the harness gave false confidence on "tenant isolation preserved". Added a value-shape-agnostic **structural** proof: a projection rebuilt from the full interleaved stream must be byte-identical to one rebuilt from only that tenant's events; any divergence is contamination. The `tenant_id` field scan is kept as a fast secondary signal; `detail` now reports `leaks`, `contamination`, and `cursor_issues` separately and `passed` requires all three clean. A new negative test drives a non-tenant-partitioned store provider and asserts the field scan reports zero leaks while the structural check catches the ledger contamination. 16 replay-harness tests pass; 217 finance unit + projection tests pass; lint clean.
- **Finance Ops — adapter-job record shape reconciled across `simulateDealWon`, migration 172, the 2B-10 adapter-queue projection, and `projection-contracts.md` §7 (`backend/lib/finance/financeDomainService.js`, `backend/migrations/172_finance_ops_runtime_scaffold.sql`, `backend/lib/finance/projections/adapterQueueProjection.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/financeDomainService.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/adapterQueueProjection.test.js`, `docs/architecture/finance/projection-contracts.md`)**: Closed the Phase-1 reconciliation gap flagged by the Phase 2B-10 adapter-queue projection — the `adapter_job` record had disagreeing definitions across the domain object, the dev-only table, and the projection. `aggregate_type` / `aggregate_id` is canonical: it is the Track A event-envelope vocabulary already used by `finance.audit_events`, `finance.approvals`, and `financeEventStore`, so the adapter-job record reuses it rather than introducing `object_*` naming drift. `simulateDealWon`'s in-memory `adapterJob` keeps `aggregate_type` / `aggregate_id` and now also carries `operation: 'push_draft'` and `mode: 'draft_only'` (previously omitted entirely), so the `payload.adapter_job` embedded in every `finance.approval.requested` event matches the projection's expected shape. The dev-only `finance.adapter_jobs` table (migration 172) gains `operation` (NOT NULL, enum `pull` / `push_draft` / `sync_status` / `void` / `reconcile`) and `mode` (NOT NULL, enum `read_only` / `draft_only` / `approval_required_write`) columns, and extends the `status` enum to `draft` / `queued` / `running` / `succeeded` / `failed` (adds `running`). `draft` is confirmed a canonical adapter-job status — the pre-approval lifecycle position, kept as the table default — so the pre-approval state needs no separate representation, and the existing `finance.v2.routes.test.js` assertion `adapter_job.status === 'draft'` is unaffected. The 2B-10 adapter-queue projection (`adapterQueueProjection.js`) and its 15-case test, which had been built against `object_type` / `object_id`, now read and emit `aggregate_type` / `aggregate_id`; `projection-contracts.md` §7 (read-model shape, query interface, rebuild algorithm, the "Adapter jobs in draft status" design note, and the implementation-status note) and the `adapterQueueProjection.js` `readAdapterJob()` comment record the gap as closed. This reconciliation is a prerequisite for the not-yet-built `finance.adapter.sync_*` emitter, which can now be written directly against the canonical shape. A new `financeDomainService` test asserts `simulateDealWon`'s `adapter_job` carries `aggregate_type` / `aggregate_id` / `operation` / `mode` and no `object_*` fields. 181 finance unit + projection tests pass, finance route tests pass, lint clean.
- **Finance Ops projection runtime — buffered-store rollback isolation (`backend/lib/finance/projections/projectionRunner.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/projectionRunner.test.js`)**: Follow-up to the Phase 2B-7 per-event buffer. `createBufferedStore.get()` returned live-store values **by reference** when no buffered write existed for the key, so a non-immutable handler that mutated a returned array/object **in place** and then threw would corrupt the live store even though the buffer was discarded — defeating rollback isolation. Added a `cloneValue` defensive deep clone (via `structuredClone`; primitives and `null` pass through unchanged) applied in `get()`, `set()`, and `commit()`. The runtime now enforces rollback isolation regardless of how a handler is written: `get()` never exposes a mutable live-store reference, `set()` never stores a caller-held reference, and a failed handler can never leave a mutation in the live store. 2 new tests — in-place array + object mutation inside a failed handler is fully rolled back (live store, cursor, and degraded state intact); a mutate-then-`set()` is still committed on success. 141 finance tests pass, lint clean.
- **Finance Ops projection runtime — code-review fixes (`backend/lib/finance/projections/projectionRunner.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/finance/projections/projectionRunner.test.js`, `docs/architecture/finance/projection-runtime.md`)**: Three correctness fixes from review of the Phase 2B-7 harness. **(1) [P1]** A degraded projection now **pauses dispatch** for that `(projection, tenant)` — previously `dispatchToWorker` had no `is_degraded` early return, so later events kept being applied and the cursor advanced past the failed event, permanently skipping it and diverging replay from dispatch. Degraded recovery remains operator-triggered replay only. **(2) [P1]** Each event's handler now runs against an **isolated per-event buffer** (a write overlay on the live store) committed all-or-nothing on success — previously the live store was passed straight to `handleEvent`, so a handler that mutated state and then threw left partial, cursor-inconsistent writes visible to readers. A fresh buffer per retry attempt; a `clear()` inside a failed handler is rolled back too. **(3) [P2]** `replay()` now **defensively filters events by `tenant_id`** rather than trusting the event store, so a mixed-tenant result can never bleed into another tenant's projection. `projection-runtime.md` §4/§11/§12 revised — "continues best-effort live dispatch" replaced with the pause-on-degraded contract. 4 new tests cover all three (degraded pause, atomic per-event apply incl. `clear()` rollback, cross-tenant replay filtering); 139 finance tests pass, lint clean.
- **ESLint errors in `ai-autonomous-agent/scripts/` (`eslint.config.js`, `ai-autonomous-agent/scripts/codex-orchestrator.js`, `ai-autonomous-agent/scripts/collect-signals.js`)**: `npm run lint` reported 6 errors. The 4 `'process' is not defined` errors: the flat ESLint config had Node-globals overrides for every Node area (`backend/**`, `braid-llm-kit/tools/**`, root `scripts/**`, etc.) except `ai-autonomous-agent/`, so its Node ESM scripts were linted with browser globals — added an `ai-autonomous-agent/**/*.js` Node-ESM override block mirroring the `braid-llm-kit/tools/**` one. The 2 `Unnecessary escape character: \(` errors: a regex character class `[\({]` escaped `(`, which is already a literal inside `[]` — changed to `[({]` in both files (behaviour identical). `npm run lint` is now clean (0 errors).
- **`npm test` silently skipped the finance unit tests (`backend/package.json`)**: The `test` and `test:coverage` scripts globbed `__tests__/**/*.test.js`, but the backend container's `/bin/sh` is busybox, which does not recurse `**` — it expands the pattern to two-level paths only (`__tests__/<dir>/<file>.test.js`). The three-level `__tests__/lib/finance/` directory was therefore silently excluded, so all 7 finance unit-test files (~107 tests, including the new Phase 2B `financeEventStore.pg.test.js`) never ran under `docker exec aishacrm-backend npm test`. Appended `__tests__/lib/finance/*.test.js` to both scripts — the same explicit-path pattern already used for `lib/care/...`. Verified: the 7 files run 107/107 green in the backend container. Takes effect on the next backend image rebuild (the container runs a baked image; `/app` is not bind-mounted).

- **Finance Ops Phase 2 Track B–F spec docs reconciled with the frozen Track A contract (`docs/architecture/finance/projection-contracts.md`, `audit-evidence-layer.md`, `adapter-runtime-contract.md`, `security-rls-hardening.md`)**: Cross-track review cleanup before implementation merge. (1) Normalized remaining legacy `evt_*` example IDs to bare v4 UUIDs in Track B (consistency model, audit_timeline read model) and Track D (audit_events schema `id` column comment, the §3.3 chain example, §5.2 reversal causation chain, and the §6.2/§6.4 evidence-pack `governance_decisions` entries — which now reference IDs that match the pack's `events` array). (2) Track F §8 audit-event spec no longer uses command names (`PostJournalEntryCommand`, etc.) as `event_type`; `event_type` is now a canonical `finance.*` event name and a new `command_type` field carries the command name in `payload`. (3) `finance.audit.event_appended` documented as a reserved internal infrastructure event, not a business event — removed from Track B's audit_timeline consumed-events list (now opt-in, filtered by default) and from the dispatch-protocol description; Track D §1.2 taxonomy note added. (4) `finance.approval.cancelled` confirmed canonical and wired into the Track B projection contracts: added to the `audit_timeline` and `approval_queue` consumed-events lists, with the `approval_queue` rebuild algorithm, read-model `status` union, and query interface updated so a cancelled approval leaves the `pending` worklist and is retained in `resolved` history (preserving immutable audit history). (5) Track E adapter-runtime contract gained a "Retry idempotency" section documenting at-least-once delivery and idempotent adapter operations.

- **WebSocket server startup crash when Supabase credentials absent (`backend/lib/websocketServer.js`)**: `getSupabaseAdmin()` was called at module scope (line 11), throwing synchronously on import when `SUPABASE_URL`/`SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` are absent (local dev without Doppler). Moved the call inside `init()` with a try/catch so the WebSocket server starts and logs a warning instead of crashing the process. Socket connections are rejected with a descriptive error when Supabase isn't configured. No behaviour change in production where Doppler injects the credentials.

- **`createTenantIntegrationRoutes` crashes when called with `null` pool (`backend/routes/tenant-integrations.js`)**: The function signature used destructuring with `= {}` default, which only fires for `undefined` — not `null`. `server.js` passes `measuredPgPool` which is `null` when no database is configured locally. Changed to `opts || {}` so the null case is handled and defaults are applied correctly.
- **Coolify VPS-1 staging server unreachable — wrong SSH user in Coolify config (`docs/architecture/DEPLOY_TOPOLOGY.md`)**: Coolify's Staging server entry had `user: root` but VPS-1 only authorises `andreibyf`. All 4 staging apps (`staging-app-fast`, `staging-backend-heavy`, `staging-braid`, `staging-litellm`) showed `exited:unhealthy` and Coolify reported `reachable: False`. The Coolify private key was already present in `andreibyf`'s `authorized_keys` — it was simply being presented to the wrong user account. Fixed by PATCHing the Coolify server record (`f7uzrwlbqjtx6qamppma5xsz`) to `user: andreibyf`. All 4 apps immediately returned `running:healthy`. DEPLOY_TOPOLOGY.md updated with SSH user column per host to prevent recurrence.

- **AiSHA side panel width clamped to viewport on load + on viewport resize (4VD-26 follow-up, Codex review) (`src/components/ai/AiSidebar.jsx`, `src/components/ai/__tests__/AiSidebar.windowFeatures.test.jsx` (+2 cases))**: The persisted `aisha:sidebar:width` value was applied to `--sidebar-w` without re-clamping. A width saved on a wide monitor (e.g. 800px) could then render off-screen on a narrower viewport (e.g. 600px), pushing the left-edge resize handle outside the visible area — leaving no in-UI way to shrink the panel. Added a shared `clampPanelWidth` helper sharing bounds with the drag-resize logic (`320 .. min(900, vw - 60)`) and applied it in the `useState` initializer. Added a `window.resize` listener that re-clamps on shrink and persists the clamped value back to `sessionStorage` so subsequent reloads on the same viewport don't overshoot again.

- **AiSHA conversational form: required-asterisk falls back to step-level `required` when per-field flag is absent (4VD-26 follow-up, Codex review) (`src/components/ai/ConversationalForm.jsx`, `src/components/ai/__tests__/ConversationalForm.test.jsx` (+3 cases))**: Switching the asterisk condition from `currentStep.required` to `normalized.required` removed required markers for fields in steps that gate Next via a step-level `validate` function but don't carry per-field `required` metadata (e.g. `lead-name` requiring both first + last). Users could be blocked by validation on fields that visually appeared optional. Resolution: if `normalized.required` is undefined, fall back to `currentStep.required`; explicit `required: false` at the field level still wins (preserves the DBA / Trade-name "optional inside a required step" pattern).

- **`usePersistedFilters` rehydrates when `storageKey` changes after mount (4VD-59 follow-up, Codex review) (`src/hooks/usePersistedFilters.js`, `src/hooks/__tests__/usePersistedFilters.test.js` (+4 cases, now 17 total))**: The original implementation only read sessionStorage in the `useState` initializer, so when the hook mounted with a `null` key (tenant/user context not yet resolved) and the key later flipped to a real value, the saved filters were never restored. Same bug on tenant switch: previous in-memory filters leaked across keys until manually changed or reset, breaking the intended per-tenant/user isolation. Added a `useEffect` keyed on `storageKey` that compares against a `hydratedKeyRef` and re-reads from sessionStorage (or resets to defaults if the new key isn't ready, e.g. on logout). New tests cover: null→real key transition rehydrates from existing sessionStorage entry, real→real key transition (tenant switch) rehydrates from the new key's saved state, real→null transition (logout) resets to defaults, and null→real transition with no saved state under the new key falls back to defaults.

### Added

- **Collapsible left navigation sidebar (`src/pages/Layout.jsx`, `src/components/layout/SidebarContent.jsx`)**: Added a `ChevronLeft` collapse button to the Navigation section header in the sidebar. Clicking it hides the 256px aside entirely and removes the `lg:pl-64` padding offset from the main content wrapper so the full screen width is available. Collapsed state persists in `localStorage('nav:collapsed')` so it survives page reloads. When collapsed, a 28px × 56px `ChevronRight` floating button is pinned at `fixed left-2 top-1/2` to allow re-expanding without needing the sidebar visible. Both transitions use `transition-[padding]/transition-[width] duration-300` for a smooth animation. The `SidebarContent` component is unmounted when collapsed (avoids dead event listeners). Props `onToggleCollapse` and `isCollapsed` are passed through from Layout but remain optional so the component renders safely in all existing tests without changes.

- **AiSHA side panel window controls — minimize, resize, pop-out (4VD-26 / 4VD-45) (`src/components/ai/AiSidebar.jsx`, `src/components/ai/__tests__/AiSidebar.windowFeatures.test.jsx` (NEW, 13 cases))**: Three window-management controls added to the AiSHA sidebar header. **Minimize** (`Minus` icon): collapses the panel to a 52px icon rail showing the AiSHA sparkle logo and a vertical "AiSHA" label; clicking the rail restores the full panel. Minimize state is entirely in-component — no chat history or context is lost. **Pop-out** (`Maximize2` icon): detaches the panel from the right-edge dock and renders it as a floating window at `position: fixed` (default: top-right of viewport). The pop-out panel can be repositioned anywhere on screen by dragging the `GripVertical` handle in the header; drag coordinates are tracked via `document.addEventListener('mousemove')` with stable refs so the effect never tears down. Clicking "Dock panel" (same button, now highlighted indigo) re-attaches to the right-edge dock. **Resize** (drag the 4px left edge): drag left to widen the panel (max 900px), right to narrow (min 320px); new width persisted to `sessionStorage('aisha:sidebar:width')` on `mouseup` and restored on next mount. The `--sidebar-w` CSS custom property is set via inline style on the outer container so all dependent rules (`.aisha-sidebar.open`, `.sidebar-panel`, `.sidebar-backdrop` calc) respond automatically. Minimized state uses a pair of CSS classes (`minimized` / `popped-out`) on the outer container that toggle `.sidebar-panel-content { display: none }` and `.sidebar-minimized-strip { display: flex }` via the inline style block — no extra layout thrash. Resize and pop-out drag share a single `useEffect` that registers global mouse handlers once on mount, using `panelWidthRef`/`popoutDragStartRef` for closure-safe access to current values without re-registering the effect. No backend changes; no new routes. **Test coverage** (13 cases in `AiSidebar.windowFeatures.test.jsx`): component renders, minimize/pop-out buttons present, resize handle in DOM, clicking minimize adds `minimized` class, minimized strip appears, restore strip removes `minimized` class, clicking pop-out adds `popped-out` class, drag handle appears when popped out, dock button removes `popped-out` class, drag widens panel CSS var, width clamped ≥320px, width persisted to sessionStorage on mouseup.

- **Filter state persistence across navigation for all 7 entity list pages (4VD-59) (`src/hooks/usePersistedFilters.js` (NEW), `src/hooks/__tests__/usePersistedFilters.test.js` (NEW, 13 cases), `src/pages/Leads.jsx`, `src/pages/Contacts.jsx`, `src/pages/Accounts.jsx`, `src/pages/Opportunities.jsx`, `src/pages/Activities.jsx`, `src/pages/BizDevSources.jsx`, `src/pages/Customers.jsx`)**: Navigating to a detail panel and back no longer resets the user's search/filter/sort state. Backed by `sessionStorage` so filters survive in-tab navigation but clear automatically when the tab is closed — preventing stale filters from surfacing in future sessions or leaking across tenants. Storage key format: `aishacrm:filters:{tenantId}:{userId}:{entity}`. Tenant and user IDs in the key enforce multi-tenant isolation: different tenants on the same machine, different users on a shared machine, and superadmin switching tenant context each get a fresh filter set. Key is set to `null` when tenant/user context is not yet resolved — the hook silently falls back to defaults and skips all sessionStorage reads/writes until the key is valid. New `usePersistedFilters(storageKey, defaults)` hook returns `[state, setFilter(field, value), resetFilters()]`; `resetFilters()` clears state to defaults AND removes the sessionStorage entry. Saved state is merged with current defaults on restore, so new filter fields added to a page never produce `undefined` for existing sessions. Each page's `handleClearFilters` now delegates to `resetFilters()` rather than resetting individual states. BizDevSources's separate `searchInput` controlled-input state is initialized from the restored `searchTerm` and reset to `''` alongside `resetFilters()` on clear. All 13 test cases pass; full suite: 88 files / 821 tests, 0 failures.

- **Fix staging-app-fast deploy timeout in deploy-staging.yml (`.github/workflows/deploy-staging.yml`)**: `staging-app-fast` was timing out after 600s (40 polls × 15s) when following a `staging-backend-heavy` deploy — Vite build on CPU-capped VPS-1 exceeds 10 min in that scenario. Increased `poll_max_attempts` to 72 (18 min polling window) and `timeout-minutes` to 25 for the `deploy-app-fast` job.

Replaced with the correct policy matching AGENTS.md and .warp/rules.md: push to `github` only.

- **CI/CD remotes section corrected in pipeline doc + GITEA_TOKEN documented (`docs/developer-docs/CICD_PREPUSH.md`, `.github/SECRETS.md`)**: The Remotes section previously said "push to each separately" — corrected to match AGENTS.md policy (push to `github` only; `mirror-to-gitea` GitHub Action syncs to Gitea automatically). `GITEA_TOKEN` added to SECRETS.md quick-reference table and detailed section.
