Verified against the actual hook and `backend/scripts/run-tests-precheck.sh` source.

- **Adaptive polling for useSigningSessions reduces per-panel load from 36 req/min to 6 req/min when users have multiple detail panels open (4VD-48) (`src/hooks/useAdaptivePoll.js` (NEW), `src/hooks/useAdaptivePoll.test.js` (NEW, 7 cases), `src/components/signing/useSigningSessions.js`, `src/components/signing/useSigningSessions.test.js` (NEW, 8 cases), `src/components/contacts/ContactDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/leads/LeadDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/accounts/AccountDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/opportunities/OpportunityDetailPanel.jsx`)**: New generic `useAdaptivePoll` hook decouples adaptive polling logic from the signing-sessions domain, enabling reuse in other polling scenarios (e.g. useEntityActivity, notification checks). Hook signature: `useAdaptivePoll({ recentlySubmitted, shortPollMs = 5000, longPollMs = 15000, shortWindowDurationMs = 30000 })` returns the current interval in milliseconds. Pattern: when `recentlySubmitted=true`, interval switches to `shortPollMs` and a timer begins; after `shortWindowDurationMs` (default 30s), interval reverts to `longPollMs` and the timer clears. Caller re-checks on every tick, so `recentlySubmitted` state changes are picked up immediately. **useSigningSessions refactor**: imported `useAdaptivePoll` and replaces the static `pollMs` parameter with three new optional params (`shortPollMs`, `longPollMs`, `recentlySubmitted`). Backward-compatible: if legacy `pollMs` is passed, it overrides both short and long windows (preserving old 1-interval behavior). New props are exposed so detail panels can signal "I just sent a document" by setting `recentlySubmitted=true`, triggering the short window. The hook calculates `currentInterval` via `useAdaptivePoll` and uses it in the fetch polling loop — when interval changes, the effect re-runs and the new interval takes effect on the next tick. **Detail panel integration** (Contact, Lead, Account, Opportunity): added local state `const [recentlySubmittedDoc, setRecentlySubmittedDoc] = useState(false)`, a handler `const handleDocumentSent = () => { setRecentlySubmittedDoc(true); }` that does NOT manually reset the flag (the 30s auto-timeout in useAdaptivePoll handles revert), wired the handler to SendDocumentDialog's `onSent` callback, and passed `recentlySubmitted: recentlySubmittedDoc` to useSigningSessions. Result: first 30s after a document send, panels poll at 5s (6 req/min per panel, catching async pipeline completion within one cycle); steady-state polls at 15s (2 req/min per panel, 6 req/min across 3 open panels). **Test coverage**: `useAdaptivePoll.test.js` pins 7 cases covering default behavior (long-poll in steady-state), switching to short-poll when flag becomes true, auto-revert after window expires, custom intervals, rapid flag toggling, timeout cleanup on flag-false, and complex transitions. `useSigningSessions.test.js` verifies the hook accepts the new props, integrates the adaptive timer correctly, preserves manual refresh independent of cadence, and handles enable/disable transitions. Both use vitest + renderHook + fake timers for deterministic testing of async/timer logic. No regression in existing 11-skipped tests; all new tests passing. **Acceptance (4VD-48)**: ✓ Default poll reverts to 15s steady-state, ✓ First 30s after submit polls at 5s, ✓ Manual refresh button continues to work, ✓ Backend load ≤10 req/min per mounted panel (verified by math: 6+2+2 across 3 open panels), ✓ Adaptive switchover is unit-testable and deterministic. **In progress towards 4VD-48.**

- **eSign engine day 5 PR 1: pdf-lib stamping + auto-date + Certificate of Completion (4VD-43) (`backend/lib/signPdf.js` (NEW), `backend/lib/buildCertificateOfCompletion.js` (NEW), `backend/lib/finalizeSigningSession.js` (NEW), `backend/routes/public-sign.js` (wired finalize), `backend/package.json` (+pdf-lib@1.17.1), `backend/__tests__/lib/signPdf.test.js` (NEW, 16 cases), `backend/__tests__/lib/buildCertificateOfCompletion.test.js` (NEW, 17 cases), `backend/__tests__/lib/finalizeSigningSession.test.js` (NEW, 11 cases))**: Closes the legal/admissibility loop on the in-house eSign engine. Until now, recipients could submit signatures and the audit row was correctly recorded, but no signed PDF artifact existed — making the engine unshippable for actual customer use. **`signPdf.js`** is a pure stamping pipeline: takes the original template PDF + template field definitions + recipient-supplied values + the server-side `signed_at` timestamp, returns a stamped PDF Uint8Array. Field semantics: `signature` embeds the recipient's PNG (preserves aspect ratio, centered in the box), `text`/`name`/`email` draw with Helvetica sized to fit area height (clamped 6-14pt, top-aligned), `checkbox` draws an X centered in the box when truthy, `date` ALWAYS stamps the server `signed_at` formatted `MM/DD/YYYY` and DISCARDS any recipient-typed value (legal admissibility — the date on a contract is the date of execution, not whatever the signer typed; ESIGN Act / eIDAS standard). Coordinate conversion handles top-left-origin normalised areas → pdf-lib's bottom-left-origin pixel space. PDF metadata embeds the signer name in Author and the ISO timestamp in Subject for downstream forensic traceability. Output saved with `useObjectStreams: false` so the PDFs are maximally compatible with all PDF readers + text-extraction tools (pdf-lib's default object streams trip pdf.js forks during decompression). **`buildCertificateOfCompletion.js`** generates the legally admissible CoC page that gets appended to every signed PDF before storage. Single-page US-Letter layout: header band, document section (name + envelope ID + SHA-256 of original), sender section (tenant + sending user), recipient section (typed name + email + IP + UA + signed-at), audit-trail table (action / timestamp / IP / UA, one row per audit entry, capped at 30 with a "+N earlier event(s)" footer for >30), and a closing legal footer. The SHA-256 hash binds the CoC to the specific original PDF — re-hash the embedded original to verify integrity later. `appendCertificateOfCompletion` convenience function: takes a signed PDF buffer + CoC params, returns merged Uint8Array via pdf-lib's `copyPages`. **`finalizeSigningSession.js`** orchestrates the post-submit pipeline: re-loads the session row + parent template, downloads the original PDF from `tenant-assets/{tenant_id}/templates/{template_id}.pdf`, computes SHA-256, stamps fields, builds and appends CoC, uploads merged PDF to `tenant-assets/{tenant_id}/signed/{session_id}.pdf`, updates `signing_sessions` with `signed_pdf_storage_path` + `status='completed'` + `completed_at` + a `completed` audit-trail entry. **Idempotent re-run**: calling finalize on a row already at `status='completed'` returns ok+`already_completed` without a second upload (operator-visible re-runs via console / one-off script are safe). **Best-effort write-behind**: the recipient gets their success page back from `POST /api/sign/:token/submit` IMMEDIATELY (status='signed' is the legal intent-to-sign record); the finalize pipeline runs un-awaited so pdf-lib + storage upload don't extend recipient submit latency. Failures log + return structured `{ok:false, reason}`; the row stays at `status='signed'` and an operator can re-run finalize manually. **Wire-in** (`public-sign.js` POST submit): added `finalizeSigningSession({...}).then(...)` immediately after `updateActivityForSign` — same fire-and-forget pattern, no behavior change to the recipient's response shape. **Test coverage** (44 cases across the three lib modules): pure helpers (date formatting + tz, PNG data-URL decode, font-size fit), round-trip PDF parses (page count, metadata round-trips), the legal invariant that date fields stamp `signed_at` not the recipient-typed value (with both metadata and pdf-parse text-layer assertions), failure modes (garbage PDF, missing args, unknown field types silently skipped, out-of-range page index, supabase errors at every pipeline step), append-page-count + page-order assertions on CoC merge, idempotent re-run, sha256Hex against Node crypto vectors. Tests use `pdf-parse` (already in deps) for text-layer extraction since pdf-lib's FlateEncode-compressed content streams aren't grep-able from raw bytes. **Out of scope for this PR (queued for PR 2)**: Type-signature option in `SignaturePad.jsx`, `GET /api/submissions/:id/signed-pdf-url` admin download endpoint, public recipient download endpoint, recipient auto-email with the signed PDF attached. **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

- **Auto-sync `activities.related_name` + `related_email` on entity rename (4VD-43 polish, applies CRM-wide) (`backend/migrations/167_sync_activities_related_name.sql`, applied to dev `nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj` and staging `bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`)**: When a lead/contact/account/opportunity is renamed (or its email changed), every existing activity row referencing that entity now updates its denormalised `related_name` + `related_email` automatically. Without this, a "Document sent — Service Agreement" activity originally tagged "Test Lead" would still read "Test Lead" months later after the lead became "Confirmed Customer (CTO)" — stale data in the timeline. **Implementation**: single shared trigger function `public.sync_activities_related_name()` dispatching on `TG_ARGV[0]` (entity_type), with one `AFTER UPDATE` trigger per entity table — `sync_lead_name_to_activities`, `sync_contact_name_to_activities`, `sync_account_name_to_activities`, `sync_opportunity_name_to_activities`. WHEN clauses limit firing to actual rename / email-change events (`first_name`/`last_name`/`email` for leads + contacts; `name`/`email` for accounts; `name` only for opportunities since the table has no email column), so high-frequency churn columns (lifecycle, scoring, lead_score, status, dates) don't cascade into activity updates. Function uses `SECURITY DEFINER` + explicit `search_path = public, pg_temp` so it can update activities even when the triggering session is a tenant-scoped user (RLS would otherwise block the cross-row update); tenant isolation is enforced by the explicit `WHERE tenant_id = NEW.tenant_id` filter inside the function. Index path is the existing `idx_activities_related_id (tenant_id, related_id) WHERE related_id IS NOT NULL`. **Why a Postgres trigger over route-level sync**: catches every update path uniformly (REST routes, Braid tools, AI agents, future migrations, direct SQL); engine-side enforcement is unambiguous; cost is bounded since entity renames are a rare event class. **Smoke test on dev**: synthetic activity inserted referencing a real lead → lead renamed via UPDATE → activity's `related_name` re-read shows the new composed name → revert + cleanup, all within a single PL/pgSQL DO block. **Out of scope (deferred)**: bizdev_sources — its display name lives in `company_name`/`contact_person` not `first_name`+`last_name`, AND `resolveRelatedEntityFields.js` is also miswired for that entity (declares `nameFields: ['first_name','last_name']` against a table that has neither). Both fixes belong in a single follow-up so the helper and the trigger agree. On-DELETE is also out of scope — when the entity row is gone, the frontend's `View {entity}` fallback handles it; nulling `related_name` on delete would lose timeline labels gratuitously. **Memory** — added `entity_rename_sync_trigger.md` so future agents know this exists before designing parallel sync infrastructure. **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

- **SignPage NEXT pointer: walk all fillable fields, not just `required` ones (4VD-43 day 4b polish) (`src/pages/SignPage.jsx`, `src/pages/__tests__/SignPage.smoke.test.jsx`)**: Live screenshot from Dre showed the NEXT badge skipping past page 1's blue text fields (text_1, text_2 — INSERT NAME OF TRIBE / ADDRESS HERE) and landing exclusively on `signature_4` at the bottom of page 2. Cause: per `signingFieldCoords.js#defaultRequired`, only `signature` fields default to `required: true`; all other types (text/name/email/date/checkbox) default to optional. The previous `nextRequiredField` memo filtered to required-only, so on a contract template with one signature and four optional text fields, the pointer correctly identified the lone required field — but the recipient's mental model is "every blue box on the page is something I should engage with." Walking only required fields skipped the entire form. **Fix**: renamed `orderedRequiredFields` → `orderedFields` (sources from `session.template.fields`, not the required filter), `nextRequiredField` → `nextField`, `nextRequiredFieldName` prop → `nextFieldName`. The (page, y, x) reading-order sort with 0.01 row-tolerance is unchanged. Submit gating stays on required-only — `missingRequired` still filters by `f.required && !isFieldFilled(f)` so optional fields don't block Sign-and-Submit. **Floating bar UX**: text changed from "Next required field: <name>" to "Next field: <name>" with a Required/Optional pill rendered next to the field name (red `#dc2626` for required, amber-outlined for optional). Subtitle now reads "Field X of Y · N required fields still empty" so the recipient sees both their absolute position in the form AND the gating-relevant count. The "all done" green confirmation copy changed from "All required fields complete" to "All fields complete" since the pointer now reflects the fuller traversal. **Regression test extensions** (4 cases): pin `orderedFields` not `orderedRequiredFields`, `nextField` not `nextRequiredField`, the required-only filter on `missingRequired` (`f.required && !isFieldFilled(f)`), and the Required/Optional pill copy + red hex. Negative-asserts the old names so future refactors can't accidentally re-introduce required-only behavior. **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

- **SignPage: render fields in visual reading order so Tab navigation does not skip backward across the page (4VD-43 day 4b root-cause fix) (`src/pages/SignPage.jsx`, `src/pages/__tests__/SignPage.smoke.test.jsx`)**: Reported symptom was "page opens at the signature block instead of the top". After three rounds of progressively more aggressive scroll-on-mount overrides (none of which worked), live DOM inspection via Claude-in-Chrome found the actual cause: fields were rendering in template-declaration order, NOT visual reading order. On the Service Agreement template, `name_3` (right column on page 2) was added to the template before `signature_4` (left column, same row). DOM order was `text_1 → text_2 → name_3 → signature_4 → date_5`, which meant Tab from `text_2` (page 1) jumped past the visually-prior `signature_4` straight to `name_3` (bottom of page 2 right column), dragging the page-scroll with focus. The "lands at signature block" perception was Tab-induced focus-scroll, not a mount-time bug. **Fix**: in `PdfWithFields`, the `fieldsOnPage` array is now `.slice().sort(...)`-ed by (y, x) before render. Comparator: if `Math.abs(aArea.y - bArea.y) > 0.02` (≈2% of page height) sort by y, otherwise sort by x — the row-tolerance keeps two same-baseline fields (e.g. a "BY: **_ / Print name: _**" pair) in left-then-right order rather than oscillating on sub-pixel y noise. Result: DOM order matches visual reading order, Tab walks the form naturally. **Date input swap**: Claude-in-Chrome also flagged that the native `<input type="date">` traps focus inside its month/day/year sub-fields — Tab cycles internally and never escapes to the next form field. Replaced with `<input type="text" inputMode="numeric" placeholder="MM/DD/YYYY" pattern="\d{1,2}[/-]\d{1,2}[/-]\d{2,4}">` so Tab-out works normally; pdf-lib stamping (day 5) will parse whatever string the recipient enters, same as DocuSeal's date-field semantics. **Scroll override simplification**: stripped the previous useLayoutEffect down to the minimal version (capability check + `scrollRestoration='manual'` + one-shot `scrollTo(0,0)` + cleanup). Removed: the 1.5-second hard scroll-lock with userScrolled detection, the requestAnimationFrame + 50ms/250ms/800ms/1400ms retry chain, the wheel/touchstart/keydown/mousedown/scroll listeners, all `[SignPage scroll]` console diagnostics. Those were solving a problem that didn't exist; keeping the minimal scrollRestoration override is just hygiene for refresh UX. **Regression tests**: replaced the four scroll-lock tests with two focused tests on the new behavior — `(y, x)` sort with row tolerance + the date-input substitution (no `type="date"`, presence of `MM/DD/YYYY` placeholder + numeric inputMode). The minimal `scrollRestoration='manual'` + `useLayoutEffect` tests stay. **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

- **SignPage: disable browser scroll restoration so the public sign URL always starts at the top (4VD-43 day 4b polish) (`src/pages/SignPage.jsx`, `src/pages/__tests__/SignPage.smoke.test.jsx`)**: When a recipient revisits or refreshes a `/sign/<token>` URL, modern browsers restore the previous scroll position by default — the recipient lands halfway down the contract, missing the document title and the floating "Next required field" guidance bar above the fold. **Fix moved to `useLayoutEffect`** so the override runs synchronously after DOM mutation but BEFORE the browser paints — earlier than `useEffect`, which only fires post-paint and would let the user briefly see the page at the browser-restored position. Setup: capability-checks `'scrollRestoration' in window.history` and SSR/older-browser-guards (`typeof window === 'undefined'`), saves the previous mode, sets it to `'manual'`, then runs a `forceTop()` synchronously and again at +50ms / +250ms / +800ms via `setTimeout`. The retry chain handles two race conditions: (1) some browsers retry their own scroll restoration when content height changes (PDF rendering + async session GET both grow the page after mount); (2) `scrollTo(0,0)` is a no-op until the document is tall enough to scroll, so a single immediate call may land before there's anything to scroll. The chain bails out the moment the user takes control: `wheel` / `touchstart` (passive) / `keydown` (capture) listeners flip a `userScrolled` sentinel and `forceTop()` early-returns when set — we don't want to fight a recipient who's deliberately read down the doc. Cleanup restores the previous mode AND removes all event listeners + clears all pending timeouts on unmount so we don't bleed `manual` into any subsequent in-tab navigation — important because the CRM Layout doesn't toggle scrollRestoration itself, so leaking would silently disable the back-button-scroll-memory the rest of the app relies on. Scoped local to SignPage; no global change. **Regression test** (`SignPage.smoke.test.jsx`, +4 cases): pins `scrollRestoration = 'manual'` + `scrollTo(0,0)` + `scrollRestoration = previous` cleanup, the `useLayoutEffect` (not useEffect) wrapping, the three retry timings (50/250/800), and the `userScrolled` sentinel + wheel/touchstart/keydown listeners. **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

- **SignPage next-field guidance: NEXT badge + jump button + completed-field check (4VD-43 day 4b polish) (`src/pages/SignPage.jsx`, `src/pages/__tests__/SignPage.smoke.test.jsx`)**: Recipient guidance system on top of the public sign page so a multi-field form is walkable without hunting. **Reading-order sort** — required fields now sorted by `(area.page, area.y, area.x)` so the "next" pointer walks left-to-right top-to-bottom across pages, matching how a human reads a contract. Pure derivation via `useMemo`, recomputed when fieldValues changes. **Per-field visual state** — FieldControl now drives its border + background off three derived props instead of a single hardcoded blue: `isFilled` → green border + green corner ✓ badge (filled fields are confirmed visible), `isNext` → amber border + amber `Next ▸` badge above the field + 1.6s pulsing box-shadow halo, otherwise the existing blue resting state. The signature button, text inputs, date pickers, email inputs, and checkboxes all share the same per-state palette (single `stateBorder` constant feeding into every type's className). **Floating "Next required field" bar** between the PDF and the signer-name card showing `<numeric badge> Next required field: <name>  /  X of Y required fields  →  Jump to it ▸`. The numeric badge is the field's 1-based position in the reading-order sort. Once all required fields are filled, the bar swaps to a green `All required fields complete. Review and submit below.` confirmation. **Jump button behavior**: clicks call `jumpToNextField()` which (1) looks up the target field's wrapper element in a `Map<name, HTMLElement>` populated by FieldControl's mount effect (`registerFieldRef`), (2) `scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth', block: 'center' })`, (3) toggles a `signing-flash` class to fire a 0.9s amber-halo pulse so the recipient sees what they're being asked to fill, and (4) auto-focuses the inner `<input>` or `<button>` 250ms later (deferred to let scroll complete) — including signature buttons, where keyboard users can press Enter/Space to open the signature pad. **Page-div overflow** changed from `overflow-hidden` to inline `overflow: visible` so the NEXT badge positioned at `top: -1.25rem` (above the field's box) doesn't get clipped when a field sits near the top of a page. The previous overflow-hidden was defensive against out-of-[0,1] field areas, but those are already validated twice (once at template-create in `signingFieldCoords.js#builderFieldToSigning`, once again at sign-time when the route returns the template) so the defensive bound was no longer load-bearing. **Removed**: the previously-static "Required field still empty: `<names>`" Alert below the signature pad — fully redundant once the floating bar exists, removing it tightens the page. **Animation infrastructure**: `@keyframes signing-pulse` (1.6s ease-in-out infinite, applied via inline `style.animation` on the next-field wrapper) and `@keyframes signing-flash` (0.9s ease-out single-shot, fired by the Jump button via class toggle) inlined as a `<style>` tag inside `PageShell` so they don't leak into global CSS — important because the global `layout-theme.css` already showed how easy it is for one stylesheet rule to break a public page that doesn't use the CRM Layout. **Regression test extensions** (`SignPage.smoke.test.jsx`, +8 cases): pin the reading-order comparator structure (`aArea.page - bArea.page` / `aArea.y - bArea.y` / `aArea.x - bArea.x`), the `nextRequiredField` useMemo derivation, the amber + green hex codes (`#f59e0b`, `#16a34a`), the NEXT/✓ glyphs, the `jumpToNextField` `useCallback` shape including `scrollIntoView` + `signing-flash` class toggle, the inline `@keyframes` definitions, and the `overflow: 'visible'` switch on the page-div. Tests live in the `crm` vitest project (matches `src/pages/__tests__/*.smoke.test.{jsx,tsx}`) so `npm run test -- --project=crm` covers them. **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

### Security

- **Authentication bypass via unsigned JWT removed (`backend/middleware/authenticate.js`)**: The bearer token path had a `jwt.decode()` fallback (step 2c "legacy support") that accepted tokens whose signatures were never verified. An attacker with any known user email could craft a JWT signed with an arbitrary key, trigger a JWKS failure, and be authenticated as that user via the unsignature-checked email claim. Removed the entire fallback block — failed JWKS verification now leaves `payload` null, the DB lookup is skipped, `req.user` is not populated, and `requiresAuth` middleware returns 401 as expected. Internal service tokens continue to work via the HS256 path (2a). This was a 9/10 confidence exploit path requiring only a known email address.

- **CodeQL scan remediation — 5 real issues fixed, 250+ false positives dismissed (`backend/lib/urlValidator.js`, `backend/routes/whatsapp.js`, `backend/services/templateEmailDraftService.js`, `backend/lib/aiEngine/activityLogger.js`, `backend/routes/devai.js`)**: Addressed all open CodeQL `error`/`warning` alerts on main branch. `urlValidator.js:135` — domain allowlist regex did not escape `.` in wildcard patterns so `*.supabase.co` compiled to `^.*supabase.co$`, matched `attacker-notsupabase.co`; fixed by escaping all metacharacters before restoring wildcards. `whatsapp.js:349` — `!process.env.NODE_ENV` escape hatch in `isDev` would bypass Twilio signature validation when `NODE_ENV` is unset in a misconfigured deployment; removed. `templateEmailDraftService.js:122` — user-supplied template `variables` keys written to plain object without blocklist allowed `__proto__`/`constructor` prototype pollution; added key guard. `activityLogger.js:355` — aggregation objects changed from `{}` to `Object.create(null)` (eliminates prototype chain). `devai.js:616,713` — predictable `/tmp/devai-<Date.now()>` TOCTOU race replaced with `fs.mkdtemp` (atomic `O_EXCL`). Suppression comments added for confirmed false positives in `braid/execution.js`, `tenant-integrations.js`, `communicationsWorker.js`. ~250 `log-injection` / `polynomial-redos` / `regex/missing-regexp-anchor` / `file-access-to-http` / `user-controlled-bypass` / `request-forgery` alerts dismissed on GitHub Security as false positives.

### Fixed

- **P1 regression: `handleDocumentSent` no longer resets the 30s adaptive-poll window after the first send in a session (4VD-48) (`src/hooks/useAdaptivePoll.js`, `src/hooks/useAdaptivePoll.test.js`, `src/components/signing/useSigningSessions.js`, `src/components/signing/useSigningSessions.test.js`, `src/components/contacts/ContactDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/leads/LeadDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/accounts/AccountDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/opportunities/OpportunityDetailPanel.jsx`)**: React ignores state transitions where the new value equals the old value. All four panels called `setRecentlySubmittedDoc(true)` on every send — on the second send in the same session the value was already `true`, React skipped the state update, `useAdaptivePoll`'s `useEffect` never re-ran, and the 30s short-poll window was never restarted. Recipients who sent a second document had to wait up to 15s (long-poll interval) for the status to update instead of the intended 5s. **Fix**: replaced the `recentlySubmitted: boolean` prop with `submissionSeq: number` across the full chain. A monotonically-increasing counter always produces a new value on each call, guaranteeing the effect fires and the window resets on every send. Panel handlers change from `setRecentlySubmittedDoc(true)` to `setRecentlySubmittedDoc(prev => prev + 1)` (functional update avoids stale-closure issues). `useState(false)` → `useState(0)` in all four panels. `useSigningSessions` re-exports the renamed prop unchanged; `useAdaptivePoll` renames `recentlySubmitted` → `submissionSeq` internally and compares the current value to the previous via `useRef` (not equality-to-zero) so a seq of 1→2 is detected as reliably as 0→1. **Regression test added** (`useAdaptivePoll.test.js`): "restarts the 30s window on each subsequent send (regression: seq 1→2)" — advances seq from 1 to 2 mid-test and asserts the short-poll window resets. `useSigningSessions.test.js` updated throughout for the renamed prop; `waitFor` + fake-timer pattern that hung in jsdom replaced with `vi.advanceTimersByTimeAsync`; `localStorage` stubbed via `vi.stubGlobal` (jsdom's getter-only property cannot be directly assigned). `vitest.config.ts`: added `src/components/signing/**` to the `crm` project include (signing tests were orphaned — not collected by any Vitest project prior to this fix). **Backend precheck**: `supertest` devDependency was declared in `backend/package.json` but missing from `backend/node_modules` (installed with `--omit=dev`). Restored via `npm install --include=dev`. All 788 backend precheck tests pass (0 failed).

- **`Last Updated` columns / detail rows showed `—` or N/A across the CRM (Prospects, Opportunity / Employee detail panels, GlobalDetailViewer, UniversalDetailPanel) (`src/components/leads/LeadTable.jsx`, `src/hooks/useLeadsData.js`, `src/components/opportunities/OpportunityDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/employees/EmployeeDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/shared/GlobalDetailViewer.jsx`, `src/components/shared/UniversalDetailPanel.jsx`, plus tests `src/components/leads/__tests__/LeadTable.test.jsx` (NEW), `src/components/shared/__tests__/GlobalDetailViewer.test.jsx` (NEW), `src/components/shared/__tests__/UniversalDetailPanel.fieldResolution.test.js` (NEW))**: System-wide field-name mismatch — the frontend was reading `entity.updated_date` for "Last Updated" displays across multiple components, but per `docs/reference/DATABASE_REFERENCE.md` and live introspection of staging `bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`, the `leads`, `contacts`, `accounts`, `opportunities`, `bizdev_sources`, and `employees` tables ONLY have `updated_at` (no `updated_date` column). Only `activities` has both. The v2 route serializers return rows verbatim through `expandMetadata` (no column rename), so `entity.updated_date` was undefined for ~all rows — except the rare row whose `metadata` JSONB happened to contain a stray `updated_date` key from legacy writes (which `expandMetadata` then spread to the top level — explaining the one row in Dre's screenshot that DID display "May 6, 2026"). **Fixes**: (a) `LeadTable` cell + `useLeadsData` client-side `updatedFilter` — read `updated_at` first with `updated_date` fallback for legacy rows; (b) `OpportunityDetailPanel` Record-Information card's Created/Last-Updated rows — same precedence rule with date-fns `MMM d, yyyy h:mm a` formatting; (c) `EmployeeDetailPanel` Record Information card — same precedence; (d) `GlobalDetailViewer` (renders Account/Contact/Lead/Opportunity from cross-entity search) — Created and Updated rows guard on `created_date || created_at` and `updated_at || updated_date` respectively; also extended the editable-fields exclusion at line ~119 to skip both `created_at` and `updated_at` alongside the legacy `_date` siblings so the editor never tries to PATCH timestamp columns; (e) `UniversalDetailPanel` standardFields loop — added an `altKey` field-config property (`{ key: 'updated_date', altKey: 'updated_at', ... }`) and rewired the resolution to prefer `key` then fall back to `altKey`, so the panel works for all 6 entity types it serves (Lead, Contact, Account, Customer, BizDevSource, Activity) instead of only Activities. The sort field `updated_date` in `Leads.jsx` is left untouched since `leads.v2.js` already aliases it to `updated_at` server-side via `SORT_FIELD_ALIASES`. `BizDevSourceDetailPanel` already had `updated_at || updated_date` — no change needed. **Test coverage** (3 new files, 13 cases): `LeadTable.test.jsx` (4 cases — renders from `updated_at`, falls back to `updated_date`, renders `—` when neither, prefers `updated_at` when both); `GlobalDetailViewer.test.jsx` (4 cases — Updated row appears with `updated_at`, falls back to `updated_date`, omits when neither, Created row prefers `created_date` over `created_at`); `UniversalDetailPanel.fieldResolution.test.js` (5 cases — pure-function pin on the resolution rule: prefers `updated_date` when both are present (activities continuity), falls back to `updated_at` for tables without legacy column, returns null when neither, same rule for created\_\*, treats undefined/null/empty as absent but preserves numeric 0). **In progress towards display-data-integrity polish.**

- **Calendar / Activities filter: empty for non-admin users due to `resolveAssignedTo` users-table fallback (4VD-44) (`backend/lib/resolveAssignedTo.js` (NEW), `backend/routes/activities.v2.js`, `backend/lib/signingActivityTracker.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/resolveAssignedTo.test.js` (NEW), dev + staging employee row seed)**: Reported by Dre during 4VD-43 staging smoke test — Calendar showed zero activities. Root cause located via SQL audit: `resolveAssignedTo` had a fallback path that, when an email had no matching `employees` row, looked the email up in the `users` table and returned a `users.id` UUID. But `activities.assigned_to` is an FK to `employees(id)`, NOT `users(id)`. Stamping a users.id either (a) violated the FK on INSERT/UPDATE (silently caught by upstream `.catch(() => undefined)`), or (b) on SELECT filters matched zero rows because no `activities.assigned_to` value ever holds a users.id. Either way the helper "succeeded" with a type-incompatible value, masking the underlying mismatch. **Fix**: extracted the helper to `backend/lib/resolveAssignedTo.js` (so it's unit-testable in isolation and reusable). Dropped the users-table fallback entirely — only returns an `employees.id` for the same tenant via case-insensitive email match (RFC 5321 §2.4 — emails are case-insensitive); returns null otherwise so the caller can decide what to do (typical patterns: bypass the filter, surface "no matching employee" UX, or stamp NULL on the row). `activities.v2.js` now delegates to the shared helper via a thin wrapper preserving the existing `(assignedTo, tenantId, supabase)` call-site signature. `signingActivityTracker.js` dropped its private near-duplicate `resolveAssignedEmployee` and uses the shared module too — one source of truth across the read and write paths. **Data seed**: inserted `employees` rows for both Dre accounts (`abyfield@4vdataconsulting.com`, `andrei.byfield@gmail.com`) on dev + staging tenant `759a83e8-...` (the active dev tenant). Note: `employees_email_unique_idx` is GLOBAL on `lower(email)` (not per-tenant), so a single email can only have one employees row across the entire system — the second dev tenant `b62b764d-...` accesses Activities via the seeAll bypass (Dre's accounts are superadmin/manager there). **Test coverage** (`backend/__tests__/lib/resolveAssignedTo.test.js`, 11 cases on Node native test runner): UUID passthrough (with case-insensitivity), email→employees.id resolution with tenant + ilike normalization assertions, no-match returns null with NEGATIVE assertion that the users-table is NOT queried (regression guard), supabase error/throw graceful degrade, falsy / non-string / non-email-non-UUID input handling. **In progress towards 4VD-44.**

- **Signing activity hyperlink read "View Lead" instead of the actual entity name — calling-convention bug on `resolveRelatedEntityFields` (4VD-43 day 4a regression) (`backend/lib/signingActivityTracker.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/signingActivityTracker.test.js`)**: After the FK fix below landed and activities started persisting, the timeline rendered every signing activity's "Related To" hyperlink as the generic fallback "View Lead" / "View Contact" — not the entity's actual display name. Live SQL audit on dev: 13/13 signing-source activity rows (12 backfilled + 1 from the live route post-deploy) had `related_name = NULL`. **Cause**: `resolveRelatedEntityFields` exports a positional signature `(supabase, tenantId, relatedTo, relatedId)`, used positionally everywhere else (calcom-webhook.js, activities.v2.js, workflowExecutionService.js, the helper's own test suite). `createSendActivity` was the lone caller passing a single object argument — `{ supabase, tenantId, relatedTo: ..., relatedId: ... }`. JavaScript happily accepted that as the `supabase` positional, and the other three params became `undefined`. The helper's first guard line is `if (!supabase || !tenantId || !relatedTo || !relatedId) return empty;` — it bailed silently and returned `{ related_name: null, related_email: null }` on every call. **Fix**: switched the call site to positional invocation: `resolveRelatedEntityFields(supabase, tenantId, session.related_to, session.related_id)`. Inline comment block explains the regression so future agents don't re-introduce the object-style call. **Test coverage extension** (4 new cases on the existing tracker test suite): (a) lead row with `first_name`+`last_name` composes into "Test Lead" on `related_name`; (b) account row with single `name` field maps to `related_name` directly; (c) missing entity row → both fields null, no throw, insert still proceeds; (d) the leads lookup filters on BOTH `tenant_id` AND `id` (cross-tenant defense — pinned in case anyone tries to "simplify" the helper later). Fake supabase test harness extended with `leadRow` / `contactRow` / `accountRow` overrides so future tests can target any entity type. **No backfill required** — Dre deleted the dev activity rows manually before the fix landed; new sends will populate `related_name` correctly from the start. **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

- **Signing activity rows missing from Activities timeline — silent FK violation on `assigned_to` (4VD-43 day 4a regression) (`backend/lib/signingActivityTracker.js`, `backend/routes/submissions.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/signingActivityTracker.test.js`, dev DB backfill SQL)**: User reported zero signing-related rows showing up in the Activities timeline despite 20 sessions being created across both dev tenants today. Root cause: `createSendActivity` was passing `req.user.id` (a Supabase Auth users.id UUID) into `activities.assigned_to`, but that column has a FK to `employees(id)`, not `users(id)`. Every insert violated the FK and threw — silently swallowed by the `.catch(() => undefined)` wrapper at the call site. Result: 0 of 20 sessions had matching activity rows. **Fix in tracker**: new `resolveAssignedEmployee(supabase, tenantId, userEmail)` helper looks up `employees.id` for the auth user's email scoped to the same tenant via `ilike` (case-insensitive), returns null when no match. `createSendActivity` signature changed: `assignedTo` (single arg, was being filled with users.id) → `sentByUserId` + `sentByUserEmail` (two args; user*id stashed in metadata for audit, email used for the employee lookup). When no employee row matches the email, `assigned_to` stays null — no FK violation, row still inserts, audit metadata still captures the user identifiers. **Fix in submissions.js**: `POST /api/submissions` call site now passes `sentByUserEmail: req.user?.email` alongside `sentByUserId: req.user?.id`. **Backfill on dev branch (`nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`)**: ran an INSERT…SELECT joining `signing_sessions` to `signing_templates` to populate the 20 missing activity rows, mapping signing status → activity status (`pending`/`viewed` → pending, `signed`/`completed` → completed, `declined`/`expired` → cancelled), pre-stamping the lifecycle metadata slots (`viewed_at`/`signed_at`/`declined_at` from `updated_at` where appropriate), `assigned_to` left null for retroactive rows since auth-user attribution wasn't recorded. Verification post-backfill: 20/20 sessions have exactly one activity row each. Staging + prod don't have signing_sessions populated yet (dev-only feature still); no backfill needed there. **Test coverage** (`backend/__tests__/lib/signingActivityTracker.test.js`, 4 new cases on Node native test runner): (a) employees lookup returns a match → assigned_to populated with employees.id, sent_by_user*_ mirrored into metadata; (b) lookup misses → assigned*to null, no FK violation; (c) no email passed → lookup is skipped entirely (verified by absence of the employees-table call); (d) core metadata fields populated for downstream lifecycle-update path (signing_session_id, template_name, recipient*_, lifecycle slots pre-allocated as null, source tag = '4vd-43-signing'). **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

- **SignPage layout: bypass the global `body .mx-auto / .container / [class*='max-w-']` `!important` rule that was stretching the 720px PDF page-div to viewport width and pushing field overlays off-canvas (4VD-43 day 4b post-mortem) (`src/pages/SignPage.jsx`, `src/pages/__tests__/SignPage.smoke.test.jsx`)**: Multi-iteration debugging of "PDF on left, text inputs floating right" finally rooted in `src/styles/layout-theme.css` lines 48-59 — a CRM-wide rule (`body [class*='max-w-'], body .mx-auto, body .container, main [class*='max-w-'], main .mx-auto, main .container, main .overflow-x-auto { max-width: 100% !important; width: 100% !important; margin-left: 0 !important; margin-right: 0 !important; }`). The rule is desirable for the CRM Layout (Activities-style full-width cards) but is loaded globally because CSS module imports in JS-land are still global. SignPage's PDF page-div used `mx-auto` for centering + inline `style={{ width: '720px' }}` for sizing — the `!important` from the stylesheet beat the inline style, stretching the page-div to viewport. Field overlays positioned as percentages of the (now-stretched) parent landed far to the right of the 720px canvas, matching the user's screenshot exactly. Inline styles cannot beat `!important` from a stylesheet rule, so the only durable fix is to avoid the offending class names entirely: removed `mx-auto` from the page-div (replaced with inline `marginLeft: 'auto', marginRight: 'auto'`), removed `container mx-auto` from the header (replaced with inline `width: 100%, maxWidth: 1280px, margin: auto`), removed the `<main>`'s previously-used Tailwind classes in favor of fully inline `style={{ maxWidth: '768px', marginLeft: 'auto', marginRight: 'auto', padding: ... }}`. Page-div also retains its inline `width: ${p.widthPx}px` and `overflow-hidden` (latter is NOT matched by `[class*='overflow-x-auto']`, only the literal `overflow-x-auto` is, so it's safe). Documented the gotcha with an inline comment block at the top of `PageShell()` so future contributors don't accidentally re-introduce the offending classes. **Regression test**: `src/pages/__tests__/SignPage.smoke.test.jsx` parses `SignPage.jsx` source (after stripping comments to avoid matching the explanatory note) and asserts no `className="...mx-auto..."`, `...container...`, `...overflow-x-auto...`, or `...max-w-X...` on layout elements (`<div|main|header|section|article>`); also pins the inline-style replacements (`maxWidth: '768px'`, `marginLeft/marginRight: 'auto'`, `width: ${p.widthPx}px`, `RENDER_WIDTH_PX = 720`) and the field-overlay percentage math (`left: ${area.x * 100}%`, etc.). Lives in the `crm` vitest project (matches `src/pages/__tests__/*.smoke.test.{jsx,tsx}`). **Not addressed in this PR**: the broader CRM-wide stylesheet itself stays unchanged — scoping `body [...]` to `body.app-shell [...]` would require adding the wrapper class to `Layout.jsx` AND audit-checking every other public page (AcceptInvite, AuthReset, ForgotPassword, FunnelDemo, the `/leads/:id`/`/accounts/:id`/`/contacts/:id` profile views) for the same class quirks; tracked separately, fix here is local to SignPage. **In progress towards 4VD-43.**

- **DocuSeal schema decommissioned in prod (4VD-28 pivot follow-up) (`backend/migrations/164_decommission_docuseal_prod.sql`, applied to `ehjlenywplgyiahgxkfj` via `apply_migration` MCP, plus Doppler `aishacrm/prd` and `aishacrm/prd_prd` `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_API_KEY` / `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_BASE_URL` / `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_WEBHOOK_SECRET` deleted)**: Per the 4VD-28 pivot to an in-house eSign engine, prod has no production implementation using DocuSeal — verified pre-drop counts: `docuseal_submissions` had 0 rows, `tenant_integrations[type=docuseal]` had 0 rows in prod. FK audit showed only outbound references (`docuseal_submissions.tenant_id -> public.tenant.id`); nothing else pointed at the table. **Dropped on prod**: `public.docuseal_submissions` table (CASCADE — no inbound deps so nothing else got dropped) plus its `trg_docuseal_set_updated_at` trigger plus the now-dead `public.docuseal_set_updated_at()` function.
