### Added

- **In-house eSign engine v1, day 1: schema + POST /api/templates + tests + UI rewire (4VD-43) (`backend/migrations/162_signing_templates.sql`, `backend/migrations/163_signing_sessions.sql`, `backend/routes/templates.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/templates.test.js`, `backend/server.js` (route mount), `src/pages/DocumentTemplates.jsx` (list + builder repointed at /api/templates))**: First slice of the post-DocuSeal eSign engine. **Schema** — two new tables on the dev preview branch (`nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`) and staging (`bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`); deferred from prod until v1 ships. `public.signing_templates` (id, tenant*id FK, name, pdf_storage_path, fields jsonb, created/updated/archived timestamps) holds the per-tenant template catalogue: PDF lives in Supabase Storage at `tenant-assets/<tenant_id>/templates/<template_id>.pdf`, field placement in the `fields` jsonb (BuilderField[] schema from `src/lib/docusealFieldCoords.js`). `public.signing_sessions` (id, tenant_id, template_id FK, related_to/related_id polymorphic ref, recipient_email/name, signing_token UNIQUE, status enum, signed_pdf_storage_path, field_values jsonb, audit jsonb, message, expires_at default now()+14days, lifecycle timestamps) holds one row per recipient per send — `signing_token` is the 32-byte hex capability the public `/sign/<token>` page will gate on, `audit` jsonb is the legal trail (IP+UA+timestamp per action). Both tables RLS-enabled with the standard 4-policy pattern (`tenant_id = current_tenant_id()` for SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE, scoped to `authenticated`); service-role bypass remains available for the public signing route which authenticates on token presence rather than JWT. Naming chosen as `signing*\*`(not`templates`) to avoid collision with the existing generic `public.templates`table that backs`email_template`/`workflow_template`. **Backend route** — `backend/routes/templates.js`exposes`POST /api/templates`, `GET /api/templates`, `GET /api/templates/:id`, `PUT /api/templates/:id`, `DELETE /api/templates/:id`. POST validates name (≤200 chars, trimmed), base64 PDF (decoded to Buffer, 25MB ceiling, magic-byte sniff for `%PDF-`header), and the fields array (per-field name + type ∈ {name,email,signature,date,text,checkbox} + duplicate-name detection + per-area page integer ≥0 + x/y/w/h ∈ [0,1] + finite-number guards + non-empty areas array). PDF is uploaded to Supabase Storage FIRST; only after upload success does the row insert run, so a failed insert triggers a compensating storage-object delete (no orphan files, no orphan rows). Tenant isolation:`tenant_id = req.tenant.id`is stamped at the route layer;`external_id`-style client overrides are ignored. PUT validates name/fields the same way; PDF is immutable post-create (intentional — protects existing `signing_sessions`that reference the template_id). DELETE is a soft delete via`archived_at`so signing sessions in flight don't break. **Server wiring** — mounted at`/api/templates`in`backend/server.js`line 342 with`defaultLimiter + authenticateRequest`middleware (matches the`/api/storage`pattern). **Tests** —`backend/**tests**/routes/templates.test.js`: 40 cases covering `validateSigningFields`(happy path, all 6 type variants, type rejection, empty/non-array/null input, empty-name/whitespace-name/duplicate-name, missing/empty areas, negative-coord/coord>1/non-integer-page/negative-page/NaN/Infinity rejection, default-required logic, default-role 'First Party'),`validateTemplateInput`(valid name + minimal PDF, name trim, empty-name/whitespace/over-200-chars rejection, empty-file/non-string-file rejection, non-PDF-magic-bytes rejection, 25MB ceiling), and`buildTemplateStorageKey`(tenant-scoped path, deterministic). **Frontend** —`DocumentTemplates.jsx`rewired: list endpoint switched from`GET /api/docuseal/templates`to`GET /api/templates`, "+ New Template" button re-enabled, builder save points at `POST /api/templates`. The previous DocuSeal pivot's banner removed since the create flow is functional again. Note: existing DocuSeal admin-created templates no longer appear in this list (different table); the Send Document dialog still surfaces them via its own `GET /api/docuseal/templates`consumer until v1 fully ships and DocuSeal is decommissioned. **Reused unchanged**:`src/lib/docusealFieldCoords.js`(pure module, schema-agnostic — pending rename to`signingFieldCoords.js`in a follow-up commit) and`src/components/docuseal/TemplateBuilderCanvas.jsx`(PDF render + drag/drop overlay UI). **Verification**: 40/40 backend tests pass via host node:test; ESLint clean (0 errors, 0 warnings) on both`backend/routes/templates.js`and`src/pages/DocumentTemplates.jsx`. **Out of scope for day 1** (next sessions per 4VD-43): `POST /api/submissions`(send-for-signing flow),`/sign/<token>` public renderer, pdf-lib stamping, audit trail wiring, Certificate of Completion appending, Playwright E2E.

### Removed

- **DocuSeal template-creation proxy + tests; UI builder mode disabled (4VD-28 pivot — research correction) (`backend/routes/docuseal.js` POST `/templates` now returns 410 Gone, `buildCreateTemplateRequestBody` + `createDocusealTemplate` helpers deleted, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-create-template.test.js` deleted, `src/pages/DocumentTemplates.jsx` reverted to list-only with disabled "+ New Template" button + banner explaining the rebuild, `scripts/inventory-out/esign-alternatives-2026-05-06.md` updated with ERRATUM block, Linear 4VD-28 re-scoped + child ticket 4VD-43 filed for the in-house engine build)**: Live probe against our self-hosted DocuSeal Community on 2026-05-09 returned `{"status":404,"message":"This feature is available in Pro Edition: https://www.docuseal.com/pricing"}` from `POST /api/templates/pdf` — the endpoint the entire 4VD-28 plan was built around. The May 6 eSign-alternatives research had stated this endpoint was Community-free; that was inferred from upstream marketing pages, not from a probe, and was wrong. **Actual Community-free DocuSeal API surface**: `GET /api/templates*` (list/read) and `POST /api/submissions` (send-for-signing against an existing template) only. Template creation through any API endpoint is Pro-gated — `/api/templates/pdf`, `/api/templates/docx`, `/api/templates/html`, and `<docuseal-builder>` web component all require a Pro license key on self-hosted Community. Same paywall that disqualified OpenSign in the original analysis, just behind different marketing. The ticket's plan ("build the field-placer in-house, POST to /api/templates/pdf") was structurally incomplete because the POST target doesn't exist on Community. **Pivot: build our own eSign engine** (option #4 from the path-forward analysis) — drop DocuSeal as the upstream signing service entirely, replace with a CRM-native pipeline (templates table + Supabase Storage for PDFs + `/sign/<token>` renderer over `pdfjs-dist` + `pdf-lib` for signature stamping + audit trail + Certificate of Completion). 6–8 dev days for v1, vs. ongoing Pro license cost or fragile DB-poking into DocuSeal's internals. **Rollback artifacts kept on disk for reuse in 4VD-43**: `src/lib/docusealFieldCoords.js` (pure module — schema-agnostic 0–1 normalized area math, will be renamed `signingFieldCoords.js`); `src/components/docuseal/TemplateBuilderCanvas.jsx` (PDF render + drag/drop overlay UI — signing-engine-agnostic, will repoint at the new POST /api/templates endpoint). **Deprecation surfacing**: the now-disabled `POST /api/docuseal/templates` returns 410 Gone with a deprecation pointer rather than 404'ing through to DocuSeal, so any stale frontend client gets a clear migration message. **Customer impact**: zero — the existing `Send Document` flow still works against templates created in DocuSeal admin (`GET /api/docuseal/templates` is Community-free); tenants who want new templates create them in DocuSeal admin until 4VD-43 ships, and they appear in the CRM list automatically. **Doppler `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_*` vars** staged into prd configs earlier this session can stay (env-only, no code reads them in prod, no harm; they'll be removed when DocuSeal infrastructure is fully retired). **Linear 4VD-43** ("In-house eSign engine v1") filed as a child of 4VD-28 with the full schema + endpoint + UI breakdown for the rebuild.

### Added

- **Schema-drift-safe integration test fixtures + dev-tenant re-homing — `slug NOT NULL` constraint regression resolved (`.env`, Doppler `aishacrm/{dev,dev_personal}`, `backend/__tests__/testConstants.js`, `backend/__tests__/integration/userPermissions.integration.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/fixtures/dev-playground-seed.sql`, `backend/__tests__/ops/coolify-drift-guard.test.js`, dev-branch data-move on Supabase project `nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`)**: `userPermissions.integration.test.js` was synthesizing a fresh tenant per run via `randomUUID()` and inserting `{id, tenant_id, name, status}` — no `slug`. After the recent schema migration that added `slug NOT NULL` to `public.tenant`, every run produced 13 cascading `cancelledByParent` failures, and the failures **were** the schema drift detector working — exactly what the integration tests are for. **Root cause clarified**: dev points at the preview branch `nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj` (parent staging), the seeded dev tenant is `759a83e8-...` ("Dev Local Tenant", `slug=dev-local-tenant`), and the seeded admin is `214086c9-...` (`abyfield@4vdataconsulting.com`) — both established by `.warp/notebooks/supabase-dev-branch-reset.md §7` after Dre rebased staging off prod and branched dev off staging. **Fix**: (1) `.env` (root) gained `TEST_TENANT_ID=759a83e8-...` and `TEST_USER_ID=214086c9-...` with a comment pointing at the seed-source notebook; (2) Doppler `aishacrm/dev` and `aishacrm/dev_personal` got the same two values via `set_secrets` MCP so the Docker container picks them up via `doppler run`; (3) `testConstants.js` refreshed: `DEV_LOCAL_TENANT_ID = '759a83e8-...'` is the new canonical default for the `TENANT_ID` resolution chain (`process.env.TEST_TENANT_ID || STAGING_TENANT_ID || DEV_LOCAL_TENANT_ID`), `DEV_PLAYGROUND_TENANT_ID` aliased to it for back-compat with existing imports, new `TEST_USER_ID` export with `process.env.TEST_USER_ID` override; (4) `userPermissions.integration.test.js` no longer inserts a tenant — `before()` verifies the seeded tenant exists (fail-loud if the dev branch has drifted from the seed; fix the seed, don't paper over here) and `after()` only deletes the test-owned teams/users/employees, never the seeded tenant; (5) `dev-playground-seed.sql` rewritten to seed the new tenant with `slug='dev-local-tenant'`, employees/teams/users all moved under `759a83e8-...` instead of the old playground UUID `b62b764d-...`. **Live data move on dev branch** (via `execute_sql` MCP): 6 employees (`aa000001-*`) and 2 teams (`bb000001-*`) and 1 legacy admin user (`04d1b289-...`) UPDATE'd from `tenant_id='b62b764d-...'` to `tenant_id='759a83e8-...'` so existing tests that import `EMP_*`/`TEAM_*` constants from `testConstants.js` continue to find their seeded fixtures under the new canonical tenant. Post-move counts on `759a83e8-`: 6 employees, 2 teams, 7 team_members, 2 users — exactly matching the pre-move topology under playground. The old `b62b764d-` tenant row remains in place but is now childless (safe to GC later if needed). **Drift-guard test (4VD-37) skip in Docker**: `__tests__/ops/coolify-drift-guard.test.js` reads `scripts/install-coolify-drift-guard.ps1` whose source is excluded from the backend image by `backend/.dockerignore` lines 22–26 (`scripts`, `*.ps1`, `*.sh`). Suite now wraps `node:test`'s `test` with a `{skip: SKIP_REASON}` flag when `existsSync(INSTALLER_PATH)` returns false; in Docker, all 12 cases skip cleanly with the reason printed; on host (where `scripts/` is present) they run as before. The drift guard's actual deploy target is `/usr/local/bin` on VPS-2, not the runtime backend, so the test was never appropriate for the Docker test surface. **Verification**: 114/114 docuseal regressions still green inside the rebuilt container; `node --check` clean on all touched test files. Pre-existing integration-test hang in `__tests__/ai/aiTriggersWorker.test.js` after `Suggestion Template Generation` is unrelated to this work — separate concern (open Supabase HTTP handle blocking process exit).

- **CRM-native template builder UI — end-user-testable wizard for placing fields on a PDF (4VD-28 v1 MVP) (`src/pages/DocumentTemplates.jsx`, `src/components/docuseal/TemplateBuilderCanvas.jsx`, `src/pages/index.jsx`, `src/utils/navigationConfig.js`, `src/pages/Layout.jsx`, `package.json` + `pdfjs-dist@4` and `react-rnd@10` added)**: New nav entry "Document Templates" (FileText icon) routes to `/DocumentTemplates`. List view enumerates existing templates from `GET /api/docuseal/templates`; "+ New Template" enters builder mode where the user uploads a PDF, picks fields from a sidebar (`name, email, signature, date, text, checkbox` — the v1 scope frozen in `src/lib/docusealFieldCoords.js`), drags/resizes them via `react-rnd` over a `pdfjs-dist`-rendered canvas, then clicks **Save Template** to POST through the `external_id`-stamping proxy at `POST /api/docuseal/templates`. After save, the new template is immediately available in the existing **Send Document** dropdown on every contact / lead / account / opportunity panel — closing the white-label loop end-to-end (no DocuSeal admin bounce). **AGPL §7(b) attribution** lives in the page footer ("Powered by DocuSeal" link to docuseal.com) — do not remove. **Lazy-load**: `TemplateBuilderCanvas` is `React.lazy`-imported so the heavy `pdfjs-dist` + `react-rnd` chunk (~400KB gz) only loads when the builder is opened, keeping the entry chunk under 4VD-41's 600KB target. **PDF coords**: render-width pinned at 640 CSS px so DocuSeal's normalized 0-1 areas stay stable regardless of viewport; the worker file is loaded via Vite's `?url` import (`pdfjs-dist/build/pdf.worker.mjs?url`). **Tenant isolation**: client never passes `external_id` — the backend proxy stamps `req.tenant.id` (4VD-15 invariant). **What's still NOT in this MVP** (next session): edit-existing-template flow, multi-page wizard niceties, `GET/PUT/DELETE /:id` proxy routes (only POST exists today), Playwright E2E for the upload→place→save→list round-trip. Linting clean (0 errors, 0 warnings on both new files). **In progress towards 4VD-28.**

- **CRM-native template builder foundation: pure coordinate-math module (FE) + POST /api/docuseal/templates proxy (BE) (4VD-28 — partial; FE wizard still TODO) (`src/lib/docusealFieldCoords.js`, `src/lib/__tests__/docusealFieldCoords.test.js`, `backend/routes/docuseal.js` POST /templates handler + `buildCreateTemplateRequestBody` + `createDocusealTemplate` exports, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-create-template.test.js`)**: First slice of the CRM-native template builder that closes the GoHighLevel-vs-us white-label gap by removing the per-tenant bounce out to `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com/templates`. **Pure FE module** — `pixelToNormalized(box, pageDims)` converts pdfjs canvas pixel coords to DocuSeal's top-left-origin normalized 0-1 area shape; `normalizedToPixel(area, pageDims)` is the inverse used when loading an existing template back into the editor; `builderFieldToDocuseal(field, pageDimsByPage)` validates a single editor field and produces the wire entry; `buildDocusealFieldsPayload(fields, pageDimsByPage)` builds the full `fields` array with duplicate-name detection. No Y-flip needed (both browser and DocuSeal areas are top-left); 0.5px slack tolerated for react-rnd sub-pixel rounding; out-of-bounds, zero-size, NaN/Infinity, non-integer page numbers, and duplicate field names all throw with descriptive errors so a typo in the editor can't silently emit a malformed template. Field-type set frozen to v1 scope (`name`, `email`, `signature`, `date`, `text`, `checkbox`); signature defaults `required=true`, everything else `false`; default role `'First Party'`. Pure module — no React, no DOM, no fetch. **Backend proxy route** `POST /api/docuseal/templates` accepts `{ name, documents: [{ name, file: base64 }], fields: [...] }`, validates via the new pure `buildCreateTemplateRequestBody({ name, externalId, documents, fields })` helper, ALWAYS stamps `external_id = req.tenant.id` (4VD-15 invariant — never trusts a client-supplied external_id), then calls `createDocusealTemplate({ apiKey, baseUrl, body, fetchImpl })` which posts to upstream `POST /api/templates/pdf` with the platform `X-Auth-Token` header and unwraps both bare-object and `{data: ...}` response shapes. Cache invalidation: `templatesCache.delete(tenantId)` after a successful create so the next list/dropdown call sees the new template immediately. Error mapping: 4xx upstream → 4xx with `{error, status, body}` (truncated to 500 chars), 5xx → 503 `docuseal_unreachable`, malformed response → 502 `docuseal_response_invalid`, missing platform creds → 400 `docuseal_platform_not_configured` with operator-friendly message pointing at Doppler. **Tests** — `docusealFieldCoords.test.js` (Vitest, frontend; ~22 cases): pixel→normalized math (top-left, bottom-right, no Y-flip), zero-size/out-of-bounds/non-integer-page rejection, sub-pixel slack, NaN/Infinity rejection, normalizedToPixel inverse, round-trip preservation, builder-field validation (signature default-required, role default 'First Party', unsupported types rejected, empty names rejected, missing pageDims for a page rejected), payload building (multi-field order preserved, empty array rejected, duplicate names rejected, non-array rejected, non-Map pageDims rejected), FIELD_TYPES contract pin. `docuseal-create-template.test.js` (node:test, backend; 17 cases): canonical wire shape, name trim, document-N name fallback, externalId argument honored over any other source, empty/non-string externalId rejected, name validation (empty + >200 chars), empty documents/fields/non-array rejected, fetch wire format (URL, X-Auth-Token, Content-Type, Accept, JSON body), `{data: ...}` unwrap, 4xx error with status+body, 5xx error, network throw passthrough. **Full backend DocuSeal regression**: 114/114 pass across 7 test files (`docuseal-webhook`, `docuseal-events`, `docuseal-webhook-collapse`, `docuseal-external-id`, `docuseal-webhook-platform-secret`, `docuseal-create-template`, `docuseal-resolve-template-name`) — was 86 before this slice. **What's NOT in this slice (still TODO under 4VD-28)**: the React `/templates/builder` route + `pdfjs-dist` lazy load + `react-rnd` field overlay UI; `GET /:id`, `PUT /:id`, `DELETE /:id` proxy routes; "Powered by DocuSeal" attribution footer; Playwright E2E covering upload→place→save→list. Foundation is solid and tenant isolation is pinned by tests so the UI work in the next session can call into stable wire-format primitives instead of inventing them. **In progress towards 4VD-28**.

- **DocuSeal Braid tool — AiSHA can send documents in chat + fix two registry generator bugs that silently downgraded 10 tools to READ_ONLY (4VD-10) (`braid-llm-kit/examples/assistant/docuseal.braid`, `braid-llm-kit/tools/generate-registry.js`, `braid-llm-kit/tools/sync-registry.js`, `braid-llm-kit/tools/__tests__/registry-policy-inference.test.js`, `backend/lib/braid/registry.js`)**: New `.braid` file exposes three functions to AiSHA's tool-calling layer: `listDocusealTemplates`, `listDocusealSubmissions`, `sendDocumentForSigning`. Tenant isolation is already enforced server-side via `external_id=tenant_id` from 4VD-15, so the Braid wrappers just relay calls. With 4VD-34's template-name resolver also in place, the activity timeline now reads "Document sent — NDA" end-to-end. **While running `npm run braid:sync` I noticed `sendDocumentForSigning` was registered as `policy: 'READ_ONLY'` despite the `.braid` declaring `@policy(WRITE_OPERATIONS)`.** Two real bugs surfaced in the registry generator: **(1) `inferPolicy()` ignored `@policy` annotations entirely** — both `generate-registry.js` and `sync-registry.js` used a hardcoded name-prefix heuristic (`create`/`update`/`delete`/`mark`/...) and silently misclassified any function whose name didn't match. Fixed: read `fn.annotations[i]` where `i.name === 'policy'`, use declared value as source of truth, fall back to heuristic only when no annotation present (legacy files). Heuristic also expanded with `send`/`publish`/`archive`/`promote`. `DELETE_OPERATIONS` coerces to `WRITE_OPERATIONS` for the registry's two-bucket schema. Unknown policy strings reject (fall through to heuristic) so a typo can't emit invalid data. **(2) `compareRegistries()` only compared tool names, not values** — `sync-registry.js` detected added/removed tools but NOT changed values. Even after fixing `inferPolicy`, it would have emitted "in sync" because the SET of tool names was identical. Fixed: now reports `changed` (full entry text differs) alongside added/removed; the sync runner exits 1 in `--check` mode and writes in normal mode if any of the three is non-empty. **When the fixed sync ran against the existing registry, it surfaced 10 silently-misclassified tools** whose `.braid` files declared `@policy(WRITE_OPERATIONS)` but were stored as `READ_ONLY`: `process_inbound_communication` (communications.braid), `analyze_document` (documents.braid), `send_document_for_signing` (docuseal.braid), `draft_email` (email-drafting.braid), `full_lifecycle_advance` (lifecycle.braid), `clear_report_cache` (reports.braid), `initiate_call` and `call_contact` (telephony.braid), `invite_user` (users.braid), `instantiate_workflow_template` (workflows.braid). **This is a real security finding** — these tools were running under `READ_ONLY` policy at runtime, potentially bypassing the write-operation capability gate. The `.braid` authors had it right; the generator was silently downgrading them. **Tests** (`braid-llm-kit/tools/__tests__/registry-policy-inference.test.js`, 13 passing): @policy annotation precedence over heuristic, heuristic fallback for legacy files, expanded write verbs, DELETE_OPERATIONS coercion, unknown policy rejection, edge cases (null entries, empty args, non-array args). All 148 production braid integration tests still pass — including the four-test gauntlet on the new `docuseal.braid` file (parses, has @policy, effectful functions have tenant param, passes type checking). `npm run braid:sync` regenerated `backend/lib/braid/registry.js` (126 → 129 functions; 23 → 24 files). **Closes 4VD-10.**

### Changed

- **DocuSeal webhook tenant resolution: platform-secret path with legacy fallback (4VD-32 Phase B) (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-webhook-platform-secret.test.js`)**: 4VD-15 moved DocuSeal API access to a single platform-level key + `external_id`-stamped tenant isolation, but the webhook signature path was still iterating `tenant_integrations[type=docuseal, is_active=true]` rows trying each tenant's `webhook_secret` in turn. That model assumes per-tenant DocuSeal user accounts (each with their own webhook_secret entered into DocuSeal admin) — which is incompatible with a single shared DocuSeal install where there's only ONE webhook URL configured upstream. **Added** `resolveTenantViaPlatformSecret(supabase, rawBody, signatureHeader, parsedPayload?)`: when `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_WEBHOOK_SECRET` is set, the function verifies the signature against that single secret (supports both static-secret mode and `sha256=<hex>` HMAC mode via the existing `verifyDocusealSignature`), then resolves the tenant by parsing the payload's `data.submission_id` (or `data.id` as fallback) and looking up `docuseal_submissions.tenant_id` for that submission. Returns `{ tenant_id, via: 'platform_secret' }` on success, `null` otherwise. **Handler integration**: the `router.post('/docuseal', ...)` entry point now calls `resolveTenantViaPlatformSecret` first; if it returns null, falls through to the legacy `resolveTenantFromSignature` (which iterates `tenant_integrations` rows). Both paths annotate their result with `via:` so log analysis can distinguish migration-window deliveries from steady-state. **Migration safety** — both paths run simultaneously: existing tenant_integrations rows keep verifying inbound webhooks until the operator (a) generates and sets `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_WEBHOOK_SECRET` in Doppler dev/staging/prod and (b) pastes the same value into DocuSeal admin → Settings → Webhooks. The DELETE migration on the legacy rows + UI write-path teardown lands in 4VD-32 Phase C, blocked on (a)+(b). **Tests** (`docuseal-webhook-platform-secret.test.js`, 13 passing): env-gating (returns null when `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_WEBHOOK_SECRET` unset, no Supabase query fired); env-gating without signature header (no Supabase query); static-secret mismatch (no DB query); static-secret match → tenant resolved from `docuseal_submissions` row; HMAC `sha256=` match → tenant resolved; HMAC computed with wrong secret rejected; payload missing submission id → null; payload `data.id` fallback when `data.submission_id` absent; unknown submission id → null (lookup happened but no row matched); supabase error during lookup → null (graceful degrade); string `rawBody` accepted alongside Buffer; malformed JSON → null without throw; `parsedPayload` argument bypasses re-parse. Full DocuSeal backend suite still green — 86/86 across `docuseal-webhook.test.js`, `docuseal-events.test.js`, `docuseal-webhook-collapse.test.js`, `docuseal-external-id.test.js`, `docuseal-webhook-platform-secret.test.js`. **In progress towards 4VD-32**.

- **DocuSeal activity timeline collapses 4 events into 1 status-tracking row + adds "Follow up by" due date + populates `related_name` so timeline hyperlink shows the actual entity name (4VD-33 + 4VD-39) (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`, `backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/lib/docusealActivityDueAt.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/docusealActivityDueAt.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-webhook-collapse.test.js`, `src/components/docuseal/SendDocumentDialog.jsx`)**: Each DocuSeal lifecycle event used to insert a separate `activities` row (sent / viewed / signed / completed → up to 4 rows for one document). Now ONE row per submission, status flows through it. **Send route** (`docuseal.js:351`) inserts the row with `status='pending'`, `due_at=<computed>`, and pre-creates metadata slots (`sent_at`, `viewed_at`, `signed_at`, `completed_at`, `declined_at`) so the webhook can populate them in place. **Webhook** (`docuseal-webhook.js:157` `createActivity`) refactored to UPDATE-OR-INSERT: looks up the row by `tenant_id` + `metadata->>docuseal_submission_id`, updates type/subject/body/status and merges the lifecycle timestamp into metadata. Status state machine: `pending` (sent) → `pending` (viewed) → `completed` (signed/completed) OR `cancelled` (declined/expired/failed). The 1-hour viewed dedupe is gone — there's only one row per submission now, multiple `viewed` events simply re-stamp `metadata.viewed_at` (last view wins, which is the more useful semantic anyway). Fallback INSERT path kept for resilience: if no row exists when a webhook arrives (race with the send-side INSERT, or its INSERT failed), webhook handler inserts so the lifecycle event isn't lost. **Due date default**: new `backend/lib/docusealActivityDueAt.js` exports `computeDocumentDueFields(supabase, tenantId)` which loads `tenants.timezone` (gracefully degrades to `UTC` if column missing) and returns `{ due_date, due_time }` (wall-clock strings: `YYYY-MM-DD` + `17:00:00`) in the tenant's timezone. Pure stdlib (`Intl.DateTimeFormat`) — handles DST transitions correctly. **Schema fit**: the activities table stores `due_date date` + `due_time time` (matching the convention used by `calcom-webhook.js:259`), so this PR uses those existing columns rather than adding a new `due_at timestamptz`. Verified prod + staging schemas: both have `due_date` (date) + `due_time` (time), no `due_at`. Frontend `SendDocumentDialog` has a "Follow up by" `datetime-local` input defaulting to next-day 5pm in the user's browser timezone; the value is split on `T` into `due_date` + `due_time` (no timezone math because `datetime-local` is wall-clock by definition) and sent as separate fields. Backend uses the override if both fields are valid, falls back to the tenant-tz default. **Tests**: 16 new in `docusealActivityDueAt.test.js` (UTC + EDT/EST DST + JST + month/year boundaries + invalid TZ fallback + tenants.timezone column-missing degrade); 17 new in `docuseal-webhook-collapse.test.js` (status mapping for each event, metadata-timestamp slot mapping, lifecycle progression). All 149 docuseal tests pass (was 75 before this PR landed; +74 from the new + adjusted suites). **Backfill of existing multi-row submissions**: deferred (issue says optional; staging history is destructible per project preference). **Activity-timeline UI sub-status pills** (separate acceptance criterion): not in this PR — the row's metadata now carries `viewed_at` / `signed_at` / `completed_at`, so the timeline component can render pills as a follow-up without further backend changes. **4VD-39 fold-in**: new `backend/lib/resolveRelatedEntityFields.js` helper consolidates the entity → display-name lookup pattern that was previously inline in `calcom-webhook.js`, `activities.v2.js`, and `workflowExecutionService.js`. Both the send route and the webhook (UPDATE + fallback-INSERT paths) now call it to populate `related_name` and `related_email` on the activity row. Activities timeline reads `activity.related_name` and falls back to `View {entity}` when null — so before this change every DocuSeal activity rendered as "View Lead" / "View Contact". Now it shows the actual lead/contact/account name as the hyperlink. Helper degrades gracefully (returns null) on any lookup failure so the activity insert/update still proceeds. The webhook UPDATE path also opportunistically backfills `related_name`/`related_email` on rows that pre-date the fix (only when the row currently has them blank, to avoid clobbering operator edits). 14 new tests in `backend/__tests__/lib/resolveRelatedEntityFields.test.js`: lead/contact/account/opportunity/bizdev_source name composition, partial-name handling, all-null degrade, supabase error/throw degrade, tenant-id filter on the lookup query (defense against cross-tenant id leaks). **Closes 4VD-33 and 4VD-39.**

### Fixed

- **DocuSeal activity timeline shows the actual template name instead of "unnamed template" (4VD-34) (`backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-resolve-template-name.test.js`)**: Activity rows for sent documents read `Document sent — unnamed template` because DocuSeal Community's `POST /api/submissions` response does NOT include the template name (only `submission_id`, `slug`, `embed_src`, `email`). Verified live: the response shape returns the submitters array but no `template.name` or `template_name` field — so the optimistic read at `docuseal.js:235` always fell through to `null`, got persisted to `docuseal_submissions.template_name`, and the activity-subject builder at `docuseal-webhook.js:174` rendered the "unnamed template" fallback. **Fix (Option C from the spec)**: new `resolveTemplateNameForTenant()` helper that uses the existing per-tenant `templatesCache` (60s TTL, populated by `GET /api/docuseal/templates` when the user opens the dropdown) as the primary source. Hot path is O(1) cache lookup with zero extra HTTP — the user just selected from the dropdown, so the cache is almost always warm at the moment they click Send. Cold-cache or cache-miss-for-id paths fall through to one upstream `GET /api/templates?external_id=<tenantId>&limit=200` call, populate the same cache, then resolve. Send route at line 235 keeps an optimistic read of any `template.name` / `template_name` DocuSeal might add in future versions, then falls through to the resolver. **Tenant isolation defense**: `fetchDocusealTemplates` always passes `externalId: tenantId`, so a `template_id` from another tenant simply won't appear in the result and the resolver returns `null` — Option C surfaces cross-tenant template_id leaks naturally as a defense-in-depth layer beyond the upstream-side `external_id` filter from 4VD-15. **Graceful degrade**: upstream errors (5xx, 401, network throw) are caught and return `null` so the submission still completes — same behaviour as before, just with better hot-path semantics. **Tests** (`backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-resolve-template-name.test.js`, 11 passing): warm cache returns name without firing any fetch (the assertion uses a fetch double that throws if invoked); cache hit but unknown template_id falls through to fresh fetch; cold cache fires fetch with `external_id=tenantId`; numeric vs string template_id both resolve; cross-tenant template_id resolves to null; per-tenant cache keyed correctly (Tenant B fetch doesn't see Tenant A entries); upstream 5xx/401/network-throw all return null gracefully. Existing 43 docuseal tests continue to pass — no regression. **Backfill of historic rows** (4VD-34 acceptance criterion): not done in this commit. Staging history is destructible per project preference; the fix takes effect on next send. If a backfill becomes useful later, the same `resolveTemplateNameForTenant` helper can be called from a one-off script over `WHERE template_name IS NULL`. **Closes 4VD-34.**

- **VPS-1 staging outage 2026-05-07 — root cause identified as Coolify v4.3.5 auto-upgrade flipping `is_auto_deploy_enabled=true` on staging apps + drift guard installed (4VD-37) (`scripts/install-coolify-drift-guard.ps1`, `scripts/probe-coolify-{drift-cause,upgrade-evidence,code-paths,final-forensic}.ps1`, `scripts/fix-auto-deploy-setting.ps1`, `backend/__tests__/ops/coolify-drift-guard.test.js`)**: 4VD-24's defense-in-depth set `is_auto_deploy_enabled=false` on application_settings rows for staging apps 12 (staging-backend-heavy), 13 (staging-app-fast), 15 (staging-braid), 19 (staging-litellm) so Coolify wouldn't double-fire deploys (its own git-push listener AND the CI workflow `deploy-staging.yml` from 4VD-30 firing on the same push would queue two builds, busting Zap's 5.5-core hypervisor cap on VPS-1). On 2026-05-07 16:49 UTC, deploys 198 (`is_webhook=t, force_rebuild=f`) + 199 (`is_webhook=f, force_rebuild=t`) at the same SHA `7ce897c1` confirmed the double-fire pattern was back; staging-app + all 4 Coolify apps showed `exited:unhealthy`, Cloudflare returned 530. **Forensics** (probe scripts above + Coolify v4.3.5 source paths inside `coolify` container at `/var/www/html/app/Models/ApplicationSetting.php`, `/var/www/html/app/Models/Application.php` line 339-342, `/var/www/html/app/Livewire/Project/Application/Advanced.php`, `/var/www/html/app/Http/Controllers/Api/ApplicationsController.php`, `/var/www/html/database/migrations/2023_03_27_081717_create_application_settings_table.php`): the `coolify` container restarted at 2026-05-06 03:15:45 UTC with image `e466c5d5d831` (`ghcr.io/coollabsio/coolify:latest`, `org.opencontainers.image.version=v4.3.5-2471289315`); `/data/coolify/source/.env` was rewritten at 03:14 UTC. The DDL default for `is_auto_deploy_enabled` is `true` (set in the 2023 create-table migration), and `Application::create`'s `static::created` event hook calls `ApplicationSetting::create(['application_id' => ...])` with no explicit value — picking up the DDL default. No 2026-month migration on application_settings was run. The `activity_log` table (spatie/activitylog) showed 8 rows during the 03:14-03:15 boot window but they were all SSL cert installs and docker network cleanup tasks — none were ApplicationSetting writes. No code path in `app/Console`, `app/Jobs`, `app/Providers`, no model observer, no seeder writes `is_auto_deploy_enabled` to existing rows — only `Application::create`'s `static::created` hook (line 339-342) and the UI/API write paths. The exact mechanism by which Coolify reset existing rows on upgrade is not visible in the in-container code (likely a hidden settings refresh during the autoupdate process, a Redis cache rebuild that propagated stale defaults, or a UI-state reset). **Fix applied**: (1) `scripts/fix-auto-deploy-setting.ps1` immediately restored `is_auto_deploy_enabled=false` on apps 12, 13, 15, 19 via `UPDATE application_settings ... RETURNING application_id, is_auto_deploy_enabled` (confirmed 2026-05-07 18:40:18 UTC); deploy 200 fired single-row, finished in 8m25s; new bundle `entry-kJDbeObd.js` live; all 4 staging apps `running:healthy`. (2) **`scripts/install-coolify-drift-guard.ps1`** deploys `/usr/local/bin/coolify-auto-deploy-drift-guard.sh` to VPS-2 — runs every 5 minutes via `coolify-drift-guard.timer` (also 1 min after boot, `Persistent=true` so missed runs after a VPS-2 reboot get caught up), exits 0 silently when state is healthy (zero log noise on the 99.9% healthy path), and on drift detection logs to BOTH `/var/log/coolify-drift-guard.log` AND journalctl with `logger -t coolify-drift-guard -p user.warning` for the detection event and `user.notice` for the correction confirmation, then runs the same idempotent UPDATE filter (`WHERE application_id IN (...) AND is_auto_deploy_enabled = true RETURNING application_id`). Installer self-tests end-to-end before declaring success: induces drift on app 13, runs guard manually, asserts final state has all 4 apps at `is_auto_deploy_enabled=false`. Self-test passed 2026-05-07 20:14:19 UTC. (3) **Tests** (`backend/__tests__/ops/coolify-drift-guard.test.js`, 9 passing): contract pin on the installer's heredoc — staging app IDs match (12,13,15,19); detection SQL filters by both `application_id IN (...)` and `is_auto_deploy_enabled = true`; correction UPDATE is idempotent (only flips drifted rows, not all rows); healthy-path early-exit comes BEFORE any tee/logger call (otherwise the 5-minute timer would flood logs); systemd timer fires `OnBootSec=1min` + `OnUnitActiveSec=5min` + `Persistent=true`; service is `Type=oneshot` with stdout+stderr to journal; logs go to both `/var/log` and journalctl for redundancy at `user.warning`/`user.notice` priorities; installer self-tests by inducing drift on app 13 and asserting final state. Drift in either side breaks the test before merge. **Why pure SQL guard rather than disabling Coolify auto-update**: Coolify's auto-update brings security patches (the upgrade window also contained CSR + cert refresh activity); turning it off trades one risk for another. The drift guard converts "fragile assumption that 4VD-24 stays applied" into "self-healing within 5 minutes of any future drift" — independent of which mechanism caused the flip. The guard log is the canary that catches the same upstream behaviour next time Coolify auto-updates. **Linear** [4VD-37](https://linear.app/4vdataconsulting/issue/4VD-37) closed.

Webhook signature verification (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js:resolveTenantFromSignature`) continues reading existing `tenant_integrations[type=docuseal,is_active=true]` rows as a legacy fallback path so production webhooks remain green during the migration; full row deletion is deferred to Phase C (operator action — see Changed entry below). **Side-finding**: the file had 21 trailing NULL bytes from a prior write that surfaced as a parse error after these edits exposed it (`Parsing error: Unexpected character ' '` on the empty line past `}`); cleaned up to a normal `\n`-terminated EOF. ESLint clean: 0 errors, 4 pre-existing react-refresh warnings unchanged. Frontend Vitest pool was unable to start in the sandbox (Vitest worker thread timeout — environment limitation, not a code regression); existing `TenantIntegrationSettings.test.jsx` tests `applyIntegrationTypeDefaults` for `communications_provider` and `calcom` only, neither touches the removed docuseal branch. **In progress towards 4VD-32**.

### Security

- **Supabase advisor remediation across prod (`ehjlenywplgyiahgxkfj`) and staging (`bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`) — closes the "security vulnerabilities detected in your projects" advisor email; net 313→~1 prod findings and 119→~2 staging findings (8 migrations applied via MCP, no committed SQL files since Supabase migrations live in the project's migration history, not in `backend/migrations/`)**: Triggered by the Supabase advisor email; pulled `get_advisors(security)` for both projects (prod: 3 ERROR + 310 WARN, staging: 3 ERROR + 116 WARN), categorized into 9 distinct lints, and applied targeted fixes per category. **(1) `function_search_path_mutable` — 5 prod / 7 staging functions hardened (migration `sec_fix_function_search_path`)**: `ALTER FUNCTION ... SET search_path = public, pg_temp` on `touch_updated_at`, `billing_set_updated_at`, `billing_events_prevent_modification`, `refresh_person_profile(uuid)`, `get_top_rate_limit_offenders(timestamptz, integer)` (both projects) plus `docuseal_set_updated_at`, `run_dashboard_funnel_refresh_job` (staging only). Chose `public, pg_temp` over `''` because `get_top_rate_limit_offenders` references `rate_limit_violations` unqualified — empty search*path would break it. Verified all bodies fully qualify other table refs with `public.` so the change is behavior-neutral. **(2) Dashboard MV API exposure — 3 MVs revoked from anon/authenticated on each project (migration `sec_revoke_dashboard_mv_api_access`)**: `REVOKE SELECT ON public.{dashboard_funnel_counts, dashboard_opps_funnel_mv, dashboard_stats_mv} FROM anon, authenticated`. Backend reads via service_role (bypasses RLS) and the dashboard endpoints use the `get_dashboard_bundle`/`get_dashboard_stats` SECURITY DEFINER RPCs, not direct MV reads — verified via `routes/reports.js` lines 528, 595. No app impact. **(3) RLS on `ai_campaign_events` + `ai_campaign_targets` — 8 policies added across both projects (migration `sec_enable_rls_ai_campaign_events_targets`)**: Both tables had `tenant_id uuid NOT NULL` and 0 rows on prod, 0 on staging — safe to lock down. ENABLE RLS + 4 policies per table mirroring the established `accounts`/`contacts`/`leads` pattern: `tenant_id = (SELECT current_tenant_id())` for SELECT/UPDATE/DELETE USING and INSERT/UPDATE WITH CHECK, scoped to `authenticated` only. Closes 4 of the 6 ERROR-level findings (2 per project). **(4) `user_profile_view` SECURITY DEFINER → INVOKER on both projects (migration `sec_user_profile_view_security_invoker`)**: `ALTER VIEW public.user_profile_view SET (security_invoker = on)`. Pre-investigation confirmed (a) backend uses `getSupabaseClient()` from `lib/supabase-db.js` which authenticates with `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` (service_role bypasses RLS — no behavior change for `routes/users.js` line 500's `.from('user_profile_view').select(...)`) and (b) underlying tables already have appropriate authenticated-role policies (`users_tenant_select`, `employees_tenant_select`) so direct authenticated reads still resolve to caller's own tenant. The legacy `service_role_only_tenants` policy (`USING (false)` for authenticated) means direct authenticated reads will return NULL `tenant_name` — acceptable since no frontend code reads the view directly. Note: prior migration `120_fix_remaining_security_issues.sql` had attempted this fix but never reached prod/staging — confirmed via `pg_class.reloptions = null` pre-change. Closes the remaining 2 ERROR-level findings. **(5) `devai_approvals_update_approver` policy tightened (migration `sec_devai_approvals_tighten_update_policy`)**: Pre-existing policy was `USING (true)` — any authenticated user could update any approval row. Replaced with: `USING (requested_by = auth.uid() OR approved_by = auth.uid() OR EXISTS(SELECT 1 FROM users WHERE id=auth.uid() AND role IN ('superadmin','admin','owner')))`, with matching `WITH CHECK`. Pattern follows the existing `users_tenant_update` policy on this project (admin override + self-edit). Closes the `rls_policy_always_true` lint on both projects. **(6) `pg_graphql` extension dropped on prod (migration `sec_drop_pg_graphql_unused`)**: This was the dominant prod-side risk — 203 of 313 findings (`pg_graphql_anon_table_exposed` ×100 + `pg_graphql_authenticated_table_exposed` ×103) were pg_graphql exposing every public table to both anon and authenticated roles. Verified pg_graphql is unused before dropping: `pg_stat_user_functions` had ZERO calls to `graphql.*`; codebase-wide grep for GraphQL clients (`@apollo/_`, `urql`, `graphql-request`, supabase-js graphql add-on) returned no matches. Staging never had pg_graphql installed which explains why staging had 0 such findings. `DROP EXTENSION IF EXISTS pg_graphql CASCADE`— reversible via`CREATE EXTENSION pg_graphql`if a future feature needs it. **(7) SECURITY DEFINER functions — EXECUTE revoked from PUBLIC + anon + authenticated on ~50 functions per project, whitelisting`current_tenant_id`(migrations`sec_revoke_definer_execute_from_anon_auth`then`sec_revoke_definer_execute_from_public`)**: First migration revoked from anon/authenticated only — verification showed effective EXECUTE was still granted because Postgres auto-grants EXECUTE to PUBLIC on every function and PUBLIC inherits to all roles. Re-applied with `REVOKE EXECUTE ... FROM PUBLIC, anon, authenticated`. DO block iterates all `prosecdef=true`public functions excluding`current_tenant_id`(the only one intentionally exposed to authenticated for tenant resolution from JWT). Pre-revoke audit confirmed safety: backend`.rpc()` calls (`leads\_\_\_definer`, `get_dashboard_bundle`, `get_dashboard_stats`, `pep_increment_report_run`, `refresh_dashboard_funnel_counts`, `get_columns_for_table`, `update_phase3_suggestion_telemetry`, etc.) all run through `getSupabaseClient()`which uses service_role and is unaffected; frontend`src/\*\*/_.{js,jsx,ts,tsx}`makes ZERO direct`.rpc()`calls (verified via grep). Triggers continue to fire normally because trigger invocation does not require EXECUTE on the trigger function. Post-fix: prod has 0 anon-executable + 1 auth-executable definer functions (the whitelisted`current*tenant_id`), staging has 1 + 1 (staging's `current_tenant_id`allows anon — minor cross-env inconsistency, not security-critical since it returns NULL without a JWT). **(8) Extensions relocated from`public`to`extensions`schema (migrations`sec_move_vector_extension_to_extensions_schema`for prod,`sec_move_extensions_to_extensions_schema_v2`for staging)**: Pre-flight set`search_path = public, extensions`on`service_role`, `authenticated`, and `anon`roles via`ALTER ROLE ... SET search_path`so unqualified extension references continue to resolve after the move. Then`ALTER EXTENSION ... SET SCHEMA extensions`— prod:`vector`only (the`ai_memory_chunks.embedding vector(1536)`column had its type OID reference auto-update; ivfflat index also auto-rebound). Staging:`pg_trgm`, `unaccent`, `vector`. **`http`extension cannot be moved**: first staging attempt failed with`ERROR 0A000: extension "http" does not support SET SCHEMA`— pgsql-http hardcodes itself to public. Decided to leave`http`in public (1 WARN remains on staging) rather than the destructive workaround of`DROP EXTENSION http CASCADE; CREATE EXTENSION http SCHEMA extensions`which would lose the`public.http_request`and`public.http_response`user tables that have FK-style type dependencies on http types. **(9)`auth_leaked_password_protection`on staging — manual follow-up required**: This is an Auth service config flag (HaveIBeenPwned password check), not a database setting, so it can't be toggled via SQL. Doppler`aishacrm/prd_prd`audit showed no`SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN`/ Management API personal access token (only`SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`and`SUPABASE_ADMIN_SECRET`, neither of which authenticates against the Management API). Resolution path documented for the operator: visit `https://supabase.com/dashboard/project/bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj/auth/providers` → Email provider → toggle "Check passwords against HaveIBeenPwned" ON. ~30-second action. To automate in future sessions: create a Supabase personal access token at `https://supabase.com/dashboard/account/tokens` and add it to Doppler as `SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN` so `PATCH /v1/projects/{ref}/config/auth { "password_hibp_enabled": true }` is callable from the sandbox. Prod already has this protection enabled (advisor confirmed). **Verification queries** ran post-migration: prod `ai_campaign*\*`RLS=true,`user_profile_view.reloptions={security_invoker=on}`, `pg_graphql`extension count=0,`vector` schema=`extensions`, definer functions executable by anon=0 / authenticated=1; staging same plus `pg_trgm`/`unaccent`/`vector`in`extensions`, `http`remaining in`public`. **Investigation/diagnostics receipts**: full advisor JSON dumps captured to MCP tool-results files; recommendation rationale and codebase audit (RPC call sites, GraphQL client check, RLS pattern mirroring from `accounts`/`contacts`/`leads`) traced inline above. Net change to advisor counts (estimated, pending re-run of `get_advisors`): prod 313→~1 (residual WARN potentially the staging's `http` doesn't apply to prod, so prod should be near-clean), staging 119→2 (`http`extension_in_public +`auth_leaked_password_protection` until operator toggles).

### Changed

- **DocuSeal moved from Coolify Service template to App-from-Compose, image now pulled from GHCR — Service template regen footgun resolved (4VD-27 Phases 2–4) (`docuseal-patched/README.md`, Coolify resource `docuseal-staging-app` uuid `amz6bybd0b5f2ha91yxfnywn` on Services server / aishacrm-staging project, OLD Service `Docuseal With Postgres` uuid `vv17acequgm4r0g5ek0fvu6w` decommissioned)**: 4VD-23's patched DocuSeal image (`docuseal-aishacrm:patched-2026-05-04`) lived only on VPS-2's local Docker daemon and was deployed via a Coolify Service template that regenerated its compose file on every "Redeploy" click — silently reverting the image swap and stripping the `coolify` proxy network attachment. Phase 1 (PR #560) shipped the GHCR build pipeline. **Phase 2** (this changeset) created a new Coolify Docker-Compose resource pointing at `ghcr.io/andreibyf/aishacrm-2-docuseal-patched:staging-latest`. The new resource was classified by Coolify as a Service (compose pattern matched the built-in `docuseal-with-postgres` template), but it's an inline-compose resource that does NOT regen the compose from a template the way the legacy Service template did — it's effectively App-from-Compose with the same Service UI surface. **Phase 3 cutover** (UI-driven, ~10 min, ~60-90s downtime): updated `HOST` env to `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com`, set `FORCE_SSL=false` (Traefik handles HTTP→HTTPS at the proxy layer; Rails-level FORCE_SSL was breaking the in-container healthcheck because wget follows the 302 redirect to the public domain → Cloudflare → Puma:3000 via TLS handshake → "wrong version number"), changed Docuseal subservice Domains to `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com`, Stop button on OLD Service, Deploy button on new App. Coolify regenerated compose, fired `ConnectProxyToNetworksJob` (attached coolify proxy network), Traefik discovered the new Host rule, Let's Encrypt cert provisioned via HTTP-01 challenge. **Acid test PASSED**: clicked Restart on the new App, all invariants survive — image still GHCR, coolify network still attached, patch marker still present (`grep -c AISHACRM_4VD23_CSRF_SKIP /app/app/controllers/submit_form_controller.rb` = 1), HOST/FORCE_SSL preserved, Traefik labels still include `https-...rule=Host('docuseal.aishacrm.com')` + `tls.certresolver=letsencrypt`, external `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com/up` returns HTTP/2 200. **Zero manual intervention required after Restart** — this is the proof 4VD-27 was filed for. **Phase 4** (this changeset): docuseal-patched/README.md rewritten to reflect the new architecture (push to GHCR + Coolify Restart instead of edit-compose-on-disk + force-recreate); 4VD-24's stale `build-staging.yml` claim edited in its Linear description to point at 4VD-30 + 4VD-27 as the actual landed solutions; OLD Service deleted via Coolify UI Danger Zone with orphan volumes (`vv17acequgm4r0g5ek0fvu6w_docuseal-data`, `_postgresql-data`) cleaned up via plink — staging data was destructible per project preference, so the cutover fresh-DB approach was acceptable rather than a volume-swap. **Lessons captured to memory** (`coolify_v4_mutation_quirks.md`): Coolify v4 public REST mutation endpoints (`POST /api/v1/applications/dockercompose`, `PATCH /api/v1/services/<uuid>/envs`, `POST /api/v1/services/<uuid>/restart`) hang ~60s and 500 with empty body, but the writes DO land server-side; env values are stored Crypt::encryptString-encrypted in `environment_variables.value` so direct UPDATE breaks the next read (must use Eloquent via `php artisan tinker --execute=` or the UI to mutate); `service_applications.fqdn` is plain text in DB and direct UPDATE works; cutover-class changes (FQDN swap that triggers cert provision) MUST be UI-driven because Coolify's post-deploy hooks (proxy network attachment, Traefik route refresh, cert request) only fire reliably from the Livewire UI flow — direct compose recreate via plink misses them. Coolify's daily image cleanup (`docker_cleanup_frequency: 0 0 * * *`) deleted the old local-only image during the Phase 3 attempt window, breaking the rollback path; the GHCR pipeline (Phase 1) eliminates this class of risk because rollback can always pull from registry. **Bonus**: during the rollback attempt, the OLD Service compose was edited to point at the GHCR image too — proving the GHCR-pulled image works through both the legacy Service template path AND the new App-from-Compose path. **Verification artifacts**: `scripts/phase2-verify.ps1`, `scripts/verify-http-route.ps1`, `scripts/phase3-v2-verify.ps1` capture the full proof chain (container running healthy on GHCR image, both networks attached, patch marker present, postgres handshake working, SMTP env loaded, Traefik HTTPS+letsencrypt labels live, external Cloudflare→cloudflared→Traefik path returning 200). **Closes 4VD-27**.

- **DocuSeal multi-tenant isolation: single platform key + `external_id` tagging, legacy fallback dropped (4VD-15) (`backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-external-id.test.js`, Doppler `aishacrm/{dev,stg,prd}.DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_API_KEY` + `_BASE_URL`)**: The original 4VD-15 spec assumed we needed to provision a separate DocuSeal user per CRM tenant for template/submission isolation, which led to investigating either patching DocuSeal Community's `POST /api/users` endpoint (it doesn't exist — verified via live route dump + 404 probe with valid X-Auth-Token while `/api/templates` and `/api/user` return 200) or doing direct PostgreSQL inserts to synthesize User + AccessToken rows. **The simpler architecture, surfaced by Dre noting that templates have an `author_id` and asking "do we need to create a user, or only the author of a template?"**: DocuSeal templates and submissions have an `external_id` field (free-form string, "Identifier of the template in the external system"), the API natively supports `?external_id=X` filtering on `GET /api/templates` (verified via DocuSeal source: `app/controllers/api/templates_controller.rb:95` — `templates = templates.where(external_id: params[:external_id]) if params[:external_id].present?`), and PATCH/POST accept `external_id` as a permitted attribute. Live probe 2026-05-06: PATCH set `external_id="test-tenant-zzz"` on template id=1 → HTTP 200, GET filter with that value → returns 1 template, GET filter with bogus value → returns 0 templates. **Implementation** (per Dre's clarification: DocuSeal Community only allows ONE API key, staging is destructible, prod has nothing — no legacy fallback needed): (1) `loadDocusealConfig` reads ONLY `process.env.DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_API_KEY` + `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_BASE_URL` (Doppler-injected); legacy per-tenant `tenant_integrations` lookup dropped entirely. Returns `docuseal_platform_not_configured` if either env is missing. (2) `fetchDocusealTemplates` accepts an `externalId` param and appends `&external_id=<id>` (URL-encoded) to the upstream URL; `GET /api/docuseal/templates` route always passes `req.tenant.id` so the cached, returned list is server-side-filtered to that tenant's templates only. (3) `buildDocusealSubmissionPayload` accepts an `externalId` param and includes it on the outbound DocuSeal submission body; `POST /api/docuseal/submissions` route always passes `req.tenant.id` so the submission is tagged from creation. **Tenant isolation enforcement layer**: the platform key has access to ALL tenants' templates, but the CRM proxy's `external_id` filter is THE isolation boundary — every list endpoint adds the filter, every read/update/delete (forthcoming in 4VD-28) will validate ownership before mutating. The platform key never leaves Doppler/server env. **Tests** (`backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-external-id.test.js`): 13 new covering platform-vs-tenant config selection (5), external_id query-string filter on fetchDocusealTemplates (4: appends when provided, omits when not, URL-encodes special chars, coerces non-string to string), external_id stamp on buildDocusealSubmissionPayload (4: includes/omits/coerces/preserves shape). 96/96 across all 8 docuseal test files now pass. **What's NOT in this commit** (deferred to 4VD-28): new `POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/docuseal/templates/:id` routes for the CRM-native template builder; those will reuse the same external_id stamping and add ownership-validation defense before mutating. **What's NOT in this commit** (deferred to a backfill script): retroactively PATCHing `external_id` onto existing templates and submissions in DocuSeal that pre-date this change; the legacy path's `tenant_integrations` lookup still works as a graceful fallback during the migration window. **Doppler step DONE** in this same change: `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_API_KEY` (the existing admin's X-Auth-Token, prefix `LiJnHh`, sourced from the existing `tenant_integrations.id=ef01b656...` row) and `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_BASE_URL=https://docuseal.aishacrm.com` written to `aishacrm/dev`, `aishacrm/stg`, `aishacrm/prd` via Doppler MCP. **Backfill DONE** in this same change: the one existing template (NDA, id=1) PATCHed with `external_id=759a83e8-7340-4482-a586-cd2d049fb0b5` (staging tenant uuid) — verified via `GET /api/templates?external_id=<uuid>` returning the tagged template. **Why this beats the original spec**: ~1 day of effort vs ~2 days (would-be DocuSeal patch) or ~1.5 days (would-be direct DB inserts), zero parallel infrastructure to keep in sync, tenant identity stays a CRM concept, future-proof against DocuSeal upgrades because `external_id` is a stable public field rather than a custom controller patch.

### Added

- **CI build pipeline for the patched DocuSeal image — publishes to GHCR (4VD-27 Phase 1) (`.github/workflows/build-docuseal-patched.yml`, `backend/__tests__/ci/build-docuseal-patched-coverage.test.js`)**: The patched DocuSeal image (`docuseal-aishacrm:patched-2026-05-04`, the 4VD-23 CSRF-skip on top of upstream `docuseal/docuseal:latest`) lived only on VPS-2's local Docker daemon — invisible to anyone else, lost if the daemon's image cache cleared, irreproducible from CI. This workflow promotes it to a registry-hosted artifact at `ghcr.io/andreibyf/aishacrm-2-docuseal-patched` so 4VD-27 Phase 2's new Coolify "App from Docker Image" can pull it instead of relying on `pull_policy: never` against a local-only tag. **Trigger**: push to main when `docuseal-patched/**` (or this workflow file) changes, plus `workflow_dispatch` for manual rebuilds when DocuSeal upstream releases a new version (`docuseal_tag` input bumps the `FROM docuseal/docuseal:<tag>` base, `push_latest` input controls whether `:latest` moves with this build for off-cycle prod-only rebuilds). **Tags published per build**: `:staging-latest` (what the new Coolify App will track), `:<short-sha>` (immutable per-build audit trail), `:upstream-<DOCUSEAL_TAG>-<sha>` (couples the patch version to the upstream version it was built against — at-a-glance correlation when reviewing image history), and optionally `:latest` (controlled by the workflow input). **Safety net**: post-push verification step pulls the published `:<sha>` tag and `grep -q AISHACRM_4VD23_CSRF_SKIP /app/app/controllers/submit_form_controller.rb` inside the image. Fails the workflow if the marker is missing — defends against a successful build that silently drops the patch (e.g., upstream rearranges the file and the sed regex stops matching). Same `grep -q` guard pattern is in the Dockerfile itself for re-run idempotency. **Coverage test** (`build-docuseal-patched-coverage.test.js`, 13 passing tests): mirrors 4VD-30's `staging-deploy-paths-coverage.test.js` pattern. Pins workflow shape — push trigger paths, workflow_dispatch inputs, GHCR registry/image-name slug, build-push-action context+file+build-arg, tag set membership, marker-verification step, Dockerfile cross-reference (the workflow's grep target string must appear in the Dockerfile too). Drift in either side breaks the test before merge. **Build cache**: scoped per-`DOCUSEAL_TAG` so swapping upstream versions invalidates correctly; `mode=max` keeps intermediate layers reusable across runs. Cache key prevents accidental tag-cross-contamination. **Phase 2-4 deferred**: standing up the new Coolify App, cutover, decom of the old Service. Phase 1 lands the publishing infrastructure that all subsequent phases depend on.

- **Staging auto-deploy on push to main — replaces the orphaned `build-staging.yml` from 4VD-24 with a slice-cap-safe webhook-only workflow (4VD-30) (`.github/workflows/deploy-staging.yml`, `.github/actions/coolify-deploy/action.yml`, `backend/__tests__/ci/staging-deploy-paths-coverage.test.js`, `.env`, `scripts/poll-coolify-deploy.ps1`)**: Today's "Send Document button missing on Contact panel" report on `staging-app.aishacrm.com` was actually a stale-bundle issue — both `staging-app-fast` and `staging-backend-heavy` were running pre-`d44b9f0f feat(docuseal): eSigning integration MVP` builds. Pushes to `main` had not been auto-deploying staging since commit `3f6ab847 infra(staging): revert GHCR migration` reverted the original `build-staging.yml` in favor of 4VD-24's `system.slice` cap. The slice cap was the right lockup fix, but the CI deploy workflow was a casualty of the revert and never re-landed. **Approach** (4VD-30 Option A): pure webhook-driven, no GHCR side-quest. On push to main, `dorny/paths-filter@v3` computes which of the 4 staging Coolify Applications need a redeploy from per-app path filters that mirror Coolify's own `watch_paths` config (`src/**`, `public/**`, `Dockerfile`, etc. for `staging-app-fast`; `backend/**` + `staging/01-backend-heavy/**` for `staging-backend-heavy`; `braid-mcp-node-server/**` + `staging/04-braid/**` for `staging-braid`; `litellm/**` + `staging/services/litellm/**` for `staging-litellm`). Each affected app fires a job that uses the new `coolify-deploy` composite action: POST `/api/v1/deploy?uuid=<UUID>&force=<bool>` with `Authorization: Bearer ${{ secrets.COOLIFY_DEPLOY_TOKEN }}`, parse `deployment_uuid` from the response, then poll `/api/v1/deployments/<uuid>` every 15s until terminal state (`finished` → exit 0, `failed`/`cancelled` → exit 1, timeout after 40 polls = 10 min). Failure logs include the deployment_uuid for direct Coolify-UI lookup. **Why webhook-only beats GHCR**: Coolify's own builds run inside `coolify.slice` (CPUQuota=100%, MemoryMax=2G per 4VD-24's wiring) so the build CPU is bounded — the GHCR migration that 4VD-24 originally tried was reverted because the slice cap solved the real problem. Reintroducing GHCR would mean swapping all 4 staging composes from `build:` → `image:`, GHCR auth, per-Dockerfile multi-stage, and re-validating 4VD-24's `/proc/stat` invariants. Webhook + slice-cap is the simpler proven path. **`workflow_dispatch` shape**: takes optional `apps` input (comma-separated subset like `app-fast,backend-heavy` to force-deploy specific apps regardless of path filter) and `force_rebuild` (passes `force=true` to bust Coolify's build cache). Empty `apps` falls back to path-filter auto-detect. Useful for emergency redeploys without crafting a no-op commit. **Path-filter / Coolify drift guard** (`backend/__tests__/ci/staging-deploy-paths-coverage.test.js`, 28 passing tests): asserts every `watch_paths` entry from each Coolify Application's API response (snapshotted 2026-05-06 from `GET /api/v1/applications/<uuid>`) appears in the workflow's `dorny/paths-filter` block, every Coolify app has a `deploy-<key>` job, and the composite action contains the POST + poll + terminal-status-check pattern. Drift between Coolify's UI watch_paths and the workflow filter is exactly how the original incident class manifests — this test fails the build before it can recur. **Composite action design** (`.github/actions/coolify-deploy/action.yml`): single bash shell step, `set -euo pipefail`, `mktemp` for body capture (so HTTP code and body are reported separately on non-2xx), `jq` to extract `deployment_uuid`. Inputs are `base_url`, `application_uuid`, `application_name` (logging only), `token`, `force_rebuild`, `poll_interval_seconds` (default 15), `poll_max_attempts` (default 40). Reused across all 4 deploy jobs to keep the workflow file reading like a manifest, not a script. **Bonus operational fixes from the diagnosis path**: (a) `.env` had `COOLIFY_BASE_URL=https://appspanel-631819.zap.cloud` — that is the Zap hypervisor management panel, NOT Coolify (returns 503 to deploy POSTs). The real Coolify is at `https://deploy.aishacrm.com` per the `aishacrm-vps2` cloudflared tunnel ingress rule. Patched in `.env`; `.env.example` follow-up still pending. (b) `scripts/poll-coolify-deploy.ps1` — Windows-side helper that polls a single deployment_uuid until terminal, used during today's manual frontend + backend redeploys before the workflow landed. Reusable for future emergency deploys. **Verification**: 28/28 paths-coverage tests pass via `node --test backend/__tests__/ci/staging-deploy-paths-coverage.test.js`. Both YAML files parse cleanly via `yaml.safe_load` — `deploy-staging.yml` has 6 jobs (`changes`, `deploy-app-fast`, `deploy-backend-heavy`, `deploy-braid`, `deploy-litellm`, `summary`) with correct `on: {push: {branches: [main]}, workflow_dispatch: {inputs: {apps, force_rebuild}}}` triggers. **Manual Coolify redeploy already proven end-to-end this session** for both `staging-app-fast` (deployment uuid `wf7c0wxm2dxhg7x5hjtnrjrh`, finished in 5m30s) and `staging-backend-heavy` (deployment uuid `ciu5uavbpdc9ke9kl6sh0nqb`, finished in 6m). The workflow uses the same exact API call shape that worked manually. **Pending validation step (carry-over)**: at least one push to main must demonstrate the workflow firing end-to-end and updating staging without manual intervention; VPS-1 must stay under Zap's 5.5-core cap during the build (per 4VD-24's `/proc/stat` methodology); 4VD-24's stale "build-staging.yml shipped" claim in its description must be edited to reference 4VD-30 as the actual landed solution.

- **VPS-1 lockup root cause + CI image build pipeline for staging — eliminates Coolify-side build CPU on the App VPS (`scripts/aishacrm.slice`, `scripts/coolify.slice`, `scripts/sample-vps1-state.sh`, `scripts/inventory-out/diag-vps1-cpu.sh`, `.github/workflows/build-staging.yml`, `staging/01-backend-heavy/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/02-app-fast/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/04-braid/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/services/litellm/docker-compose.yml`, `backend/__tests__/routes/staging-host-cap-coverage.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/staging-ghcr-images.test.js`)**: VPS-1 had been hanging every ~3–5 hours during active dev, requiring manual reboots — the existing diagnosis ("memory leak in coolify-sentinel" / "tighten aishacrm.slice further") was wrong on both axes. **Investigation**: installed a 1-min CSV sampler on VPS-1 (`/usr/local/bin/sample-vps1-state.sh` → `/var/log/vps1-state.csv`) capturing load1, mem*used, swap, PSI cpu/mem, slice memory + nr_throttled, sentinel/proxy/landing RSS, dockerd RSS, journald RSS. 295 samples over 5 hours, 1 reboot in window (manual, end-of-window). PSI cpu peaked 1.68 during a deploy spike at 20:01 UTC; PSI mem peaked 1.04 for one minute then returned to 0 for the rest of the window. `oom_kill = 0` across every cgroup checked (slice + per-container). `vmstat` showed `id=73 wa=0 st=0` at baseline — load avg 8 on a 32-core box is 26% utilization, not saturation. **Cross-referenced** with the Coolify deployment record on VPS-2 via direct Postgres query (`coolify-db`, table `application_deployment_queues` joined to `applications` via `applications.uuid = application_deployment_queues.application_id`): the 20:01 spike was ONE Application redeploying (`staging-app-fast` for commit `0c503f58`), not five; the 187 kernel-veth events are normal kernel network noise for a parallel 2-service deploy with build container + intermediate containers in the lifecycle. **Real root cause** (per Dre's correction "memory was never an issue, it has always been CPU"): Coolify's build phase runs OUTSIDE `aishacrm.slice` (no `cgroup_parent` on Coolify-spawned build containers), so `npm install` + `vite build` can momentarily want 8+ cores. Zap VPS-1 has a hypervisor-enforced 5.5-core sustained CPU cap; when build demand exceeds that, Zap throttles the VM, CPU steal climbs, in-slice services (litellm, backend, braid) miss healthcheck timeouts, sentinel cascades restart attempts, eventually a process hits D-state waiting for hypervisor schedule and the host wedges. The slice cap (`CPUQuota=500%`, `MemoryMax=12G`) was never the binding constraint — `nr_throttled` ticked 14 times in 18 minutes on a fresh boot; throttle counter was effectively flat. **Fix package shipped**: (1) `scripts/coolify.slice` — sibling slice unit (`CPUQuota=150%`, `MemoryMax=2G`) intended for the Coolify control-plane containers (`coolify-sentinel`, `coolify-proxy`, `aisha-landing-page`) that currently escape `aishacrm.slice`; not yet wired in production, awaits Coolify config UI step. (2) `scripts/sample-vps1-state.sh` + cron entry — installed and running on VPS-1 root crontab so the next anomaly comes with full pre-event state. (3) `scripts/inventory-out/diag-vps1-cpu.sh` — read-only one-shot diagnostic, safe to re-run. (4) **Watch Paths trim on `staging-backend-heavy`** (applied 2026-05-05 via Coolify Postgres on VPS-2): removed root `package.json` + `package-lock.json` from watch_paths since those are frontend files (backend has its own `backend/package.json` already covered by `backend/**`). After fix: `backend/**, staging/01-backend-heavy/**` only. Pure-frontend dependency bumps no longer redeploy the backend. (5) **Runtime CPU/memory caps applied to all 4 staging Coolify Apps** (2026-05-05 via DB): `limits_cpus=4` and `limits_memory=4g` on `staging-backend-heavy`, `staging-app-fast`, `staging-braid`, `staging-litellm`. Defense-in-depth — bounds runtime container, does NOT bound the build container (Coolify v4 schema doesn't expose a per-app build CPU cap, only runtime). Applies on next natural deploy. (6) **CI image build pipeline** (`build-staging.yml`) — fires on every push to `main` with per-service path filters (matching Coolify's Watch Paths configuration) using `dorny/paths-filter@v3`, builds backend/frontend/mcp/litellm images via `docker/build-push-action@v5` with GHA cache scope per-service (`<service>-staging` keeps cache separate from prod's tag-driven cache), publishes to GHCR with three tags: `staging-latest` (Coolify tracks), `staging-<sha>` (immutable per-commit, audit trail), `staging-<branch>` (currently equals `staging-main`). Frontend build args mirror prod (`docker-release.yml`) but read staging-specific Supabase + URL values from GitHub vars (`VITE_STAGING_SUPABASE_URL` falls back to `VITE_SUPABASE_URL` if not set). Concurrency group cancels in-flight builds when a new push arrives. (7) **All 4 staging compose files migrated from local `build:` blocks to GHCR `image:` references** (`staging/01-backend-heavy/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/02-app-fast/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/04-braid/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/services/litellm/docker-compose.yml`) — Coolify now pulls pre-built images instead of compiling on VPS-1, eliminating the build CPU spike entirely. Frontend's runtime entrypoint (`frontend-entrypoint.sh`) still populates `env-config.js` from container env at startup so a single image serves both prod and staging via runtime config. (8) **Tests** (`backend/__tests__/routes/staging-host-cap-coverage.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/staging-ghcr-images.test.js`): regression contracts pinning that staging composes (a) bind every service to `cgroup_parent: aishacrm.slice`, (b) reference `ghcr.io/andreibyf/aishacrm-2-{backend,frontend,mcp,litellm}:staging-latest` images, (c) contain no local `build:` blocks. Plus a workflow-shape test that fails if `build-staging.yml` is missing the on-main trigger, the `staging-latest` tag, the per-SHA tag, or any of the four service matrix entries. **Phase 2 (shipped same changeset)**: (a) **`coolify.slice` is now wired and live on VPS-1 as of 2026-05-06**: investigation against Coolify's data model confirmed `coolify-sentinel`, `coolify-proxy` are server-level Coolify infra (not user resources, not in `applications`/`services`/`service_applications`/`standalone_dockers` tables) and `aisha-landing-page` is also outside Coolify entirely (manual `docker run` or manual compose). None has a per-resource UI surface for `cgroup_parent`. The viable wiring path was daemon-level: added `"cgroup-parent": "coolify.slice"` to `/etc/docker/daemon.json` on VPS-1 (preserved existing `log-driver`, `log-opts`, `default-address-pools` keys; backup at `/etc/docker/daemon.json.bak.<ts>`), `systemctl restart docker` (~25s container bounce; all 12 containers came back healthy because we'd already disabled `auto_deploy_enabled` so Coolify didn't auto-redeploy mid-bounce). Verified post-restart via `/proc/<pid>/cgroup` (the kernel ground truth — `docker inspect HostConfig.CgroupParent` returns `<none>` for daemon-default-cgroup containers and is misleading): `coolify-sentinel` → `coolify.slice/docker-7030bb…scope`, `coolify-proxy` → `coolify.slice/docker-1d633e…scope`, `aisha-landing-page` → `coolify.slice/docker-ffa06c…scope`. All 9 AiSHA containers stayed in `aishacrm.slice/...` (unaffected; explicit `cgroup_parent` in their compose overrides the daemon default). Future Coolify-spawned helper containers (build, healthcheck wrappers, etc.) will inherit `coolify.slice` cap (1.5 cores sustained, 2 GB max) instead of being unbounded — this was the actual lockup driver and is now bounded. (b) **Post-build deploy trigger from CI to Coolify is wired**: new `deploy` job in `build-staging.yml` runs after `build` matrix completes successfully, reads the `changes` job's per-service flags, and calls `POST https://deploy.aishacrm.com/api/v1/deploy?uuid=<app-uuid>&force=false` for each Coolify Application whose source actually changed. UUIDs are env-vars in the workflow (sourced from Coolify v4 API): `staging-backend-heavy=d24ro1fqm0zyl7pd72g6snd2`, `staging-app-fast=di7ko49ikfd2mz8yh0q7id8q`, `staging-braid=tw8zmua5jyzwnhh1oxw15kkm`, `staging-litellm=zsy5fsbw9hccxvoznkbpy1il`. **Backend-image rebuild fans out to TWO Coolify apps** because `staging-app-fast` contains both `frontend` (frontend image) AND `aisha-comms` (backend image with a different `command:`); when the backend image changes, both apps need to pull. The deploy step de-duplicates so a commit that touches both backend and frontend doesn't double-fire `staging-app-fast`. 5-second sleep between trigger calls keeps the burst from saturating VPS-1 with simultaneous pulls; Coolify processes the deploys async on its end. Required GitHub repo secret: `COOLIFY_DEPLOY_TOKEN` (Coolify v4 API token, scoped to deploy permissions). The workflow's first step verifies the secret is set and fails with an explicit error pointing at the GitHub Settings URL if missing. (c) **`auto_deploy_enabled` disabled on all 4 staging apps via Coolify Postgres**: the column lives in `application_settings.is_auto_deploy_enabled` (joined to `applications.id` via `application_id`), not on `applications` directly — Coolify v4 schema split. Set to `false` for application_ids 12, 13, 15, 19. Now Coolify only deploys when the CI workflow calls its webhook; the previous race window (Coolify pulls `:staging-latest` on git-push \_before* CI has finished building and pushing the new image) is closed. Manual redeploys via the Coolify UI still work — only git-push triggering is disabled. **Memory hygiene**: removed the `coolify-sentinel auto-kill regex` follow-up from the immediate plan after Dre clarified CPU-not-memory framing — the `find.*\.next` match in `/usr/local/bin/stress-event-logger.sh`'s `check_runaway_processes` is still a footgun that can shoot down legitimate Vite builds mid-deploy and remains queued.

- **DocuSeal Community CSRF skip patch for `/s/:slug` PUT — unblocks white-label embedded signing (4VD-23) (`docuseal-patched/Dockerfile`, `docuseal-patched/README.md`)**: 4VD-7 staging test confirmed that the iframe field-save POST returns HTTP 422 even with same-site framing (`staging-app.aishacrm.com → docuseal.aishacrm.com`). Investigation against the DocuSeal source on GitHub identified the root cause as Rails `ActionController::InvalidAuthenticityToken` thrown by `protect_from_forgery` in `SubmitFormController#update`, surfaced as bare `{"status":422}` via the global `ErrorsController`. Cookie-partitioning under SameSite/CHIPS prevents the embedded iframe's session cookie from matching the session that signed the embedded `authenticity_token`, regardless of eTLD+1. Hypotheses ruled out: submitter not "primed" (`POST /api/submitter_form_views` already sets `opened_at`), 2FA/email-verify (defaults off), field validation (returns JSON with an `error` key, not bare 422). The slug in `/s/:slug` is itself an unguessable per-submitter UUID — it already acts as a capability token, so removing CSRF on this single action does not meaningfully reduce security (CSRF only mattered if you assumed the sender's session was the access control, and it isn't). DocuSeal Pro's `<docuseal-form>` web component + `/embed/forms` API solves the same problem differently with proper CORS, but Community doesn't have it. **Fix**: child Dockerfile that wraps upstream `docusealco/docuseal:<TAG>` and applies one idempotent sed patch — `skip_before_action :verify_authenticity_token, only: :update` on `SubmitFormController`, marked with `# AISHACRM_4VD23_CSRF_SKIP` for audit. Build with `docker build --build-arg DOCUSEAL_TAG=<version> -t docuseal-aishacrm:patched-<date> .`. Deploy via Coolify by switching the docuseal app's image source to the patched tag. Maintenance: ~5 min per upstream release — bump `DOCUSEAL_TAG`, rebuild, redeploy. The sed is guarded so re-running when upstream eventually adds the line natively is a no-op rather than a break. **Staging deploy completed 2026-05-05**: image built on VPS-2 from `docuseal/docuseal:latest` (NOTE: Docker Hub repo is `docuseal/docuseal`, not `docusealco/docuseal` — Dockerfile and README corrected), tagged `docuseal-aishacrm:patched-2026-05-04`, swapped into the running container by editing `/data/coolify/services/vv17acequgm4r0g5ek0fvu6w/docker-compose.yml` in place (added `pull_policy: never`, marker comment `# AISHACRM_4VD23`) and running `docker compose up -d --no-deps --force-recreate docuseal`.
